<doc id="45018574" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=45018574" title="Kepa Arrizabalaga">
Kepa Arrizabalaga

Kepa Arrizabalaga Revuelta (; ; born 3 October 1994) is a Spanish professional footballer who plays as a goalkeeper for Premier League club Chelsea and the Spain national team. a Spanish professional footballer who plays as a goalkeeper for Premier League club Chelsea and the Spain national team is sometimes referred to mononomously by a Spanish professional footballer who plays as a goalkeeper for Premier League club Chelsea and the Spain national team forename.

Developed at Athletic Bilbao, a Spanish professional footballer who plays as a goalkeeper for Premier League club Chelsea and the Spain national team played a Spanish professional footballer who plays as a goalkeeper for Premier League club Chelsea and the Spain national team first professional games on loan at Ponferradina and Real Valladolid, in Segunda División. a Spanish professional footballer who plays as a goalkeeper for Premier League club Chelsea and the Spain national team then returned to a Spanish professional footballer who plays as a goalkeeper for Premier League club Chelsea and the Spain national team first club, going on to appear in 54 matches across all competitions; in 2018, a Spanish professional footballer who plays as a goalkeeper for Premier League club Chelsea and the Spain national team signed with Chelsea.

Arrizabalaga won the 2012 European Championship with Spain's under-19 team and made a Spanish professional footballer who plays as a goalkeeper for Premier League club Chelsea and the Spain national team senior debut in 2017, being selected for the 2018 World Cup.

Born in Ondarroa, Biscay, Basque Country, Arrizabalaga joined Athletic Bilbao's youth setup at Lezama in 2004, aged ten. a Spanish professional footballer who plays as a goalkeeper for Premier League club Chelsea and the Spain national team made a Spanish professional footballer who plays as a goalkeeper for Premier League club Chelsea and the Spain national team senior debut with the farm team in January 2012, in Tercera División.

On 5 May 2012, Arrizabalaga was called up to the main squad for a La Liga match against Getafe CF, but remained unused in the 0–0 draw at the San Mamés Stadium. Arrizabalaga was also called up to pre-season in July, and on 23 September was also a substitute in another home game of the same outcome, against Málaga CF.

Arrizabalaga was promoted to the reserves in January 2013, to cover for injured Jon Ander Serantes. Arrizabalaga made Arrizabalaga debut for the B-side on 16 February 2013, keeping a clean sheet in a 1–0 win over UD Logroñés for the Segunda División B championship. On 3 March, Arrizabalaga was sent off towards the end of a 3–1 home win over SD Amorebieta, as was teammate Jon García; in April Arrizabalaga suffered a pubalgia, only returning to the fields in September.

Arrizabalaga appeared regularly for the B's after Arrizabalaga return, but broke the first metacarpal of Arrizabalaga right hand in January 2014, being sidelined for a month. On 11 March, Getafe submitted a loan request to the "Lions" for Arrizabalaga, as a replacement to injured Miguel Ángel Moyá, but a loan request was rejected a day later.

On 5 January 2015, Arrizabalaga was loaned to Segunda División's SD Ponferradina until June. Arrizabalaga made Arrizabalaga professional debut on the 11th, starting in a 1–1 home draw against Racing de Santander.

On 20 July 2015, Arrizabalaga moved to Real Valladolid also in the second tier, in a season-long loan deal. Arrizabalaga played Arrizabalaga first competitive game on 22 August, in a 0–1 loss at Córdoba CF, and missed only three matches as Arrizabalaga team finished 16th.

After returning from loan, Arrizabalaga was definitely included in the first team, initially as third-choice behind Gorka Iraizoz and Iago Herrerín. Arrizabalaga made Arrizabalaga debut in the top flight on 11 September 2016, starting in a 1–0 away win over Deportivo de La Coruña.

On 22 January 2018, amid heavy transfer speculation linking Arrizabalaga to Real Madrid, Arrizabalaga renewed Arrizabalaga contract – due to expire that June – until 2025.

On 8 August 2018, Athletic Bilbao announced on their website that Arrizabalaga had paid Arrizabalaga required release clause (€80 million / £71.6 million), making Arrizabalaga the world's most expensive goalkeeper only weeks after the record was set by Alisson's transfer to Liverpool. Later that day, Arrizabalaga move to Chelsea on a seven-year contract was confirmed, replacing Thibaut Courtois who departed for Real Madrid and Arrizabalaga made Arrizabalaga Premier League debut three days later in a 3–0 away win against Huddersfield Town; Arrizabalaga went on to keep six clean sheets in the team's 12-match unbeaten run in the league, before a 3–1 defeat at the hands of Tottenham Hotspur. 

On 24 January 2019, in the second leg of the EFL Cup semi-final, Arrizabalaga saved a penalty from Tottenham's Lucas Moura in a 4–2 shootout win at Stamford Bridge, helping Arrizabalaga team go through to the final.

On 24 February 2019, during the 2019 EFL Cup Final against Manchester City, with the match at 0–0 near the end of extra time, Maurizio Sarri called for Arrizabalaga to be substituted off for Willy Caballero for the upcoming penalty shootout; Maurizio Sarri was concerned over Maurizio Sarri leg cramping a few minutes prior after making a diving save. However, Arrizabalaga refused to be substituted, gesticulating and remaining on the field. During the upcoming penalty shootout, Maurizio Sarri saved one penalty as Chelsea lost the shoot-out 4–3. After the game, both Arrizabalaga and Maurizio Sarri said that the situation was a misunderstanding, with Maurizio Sarri incorrectly believing that Arrizabalaga was too injured with a cramp to continue. Later on, Arrizabalaga met with Maurizio Sarri and apologised to Arrizabalaga and to the rest of the club. Arrizabalaga was fined a week's worth of pay as a result of Arrizabalaga actions, with Maurizio Sarri leaving the decision of any further discipline up to the club, due to the club rules. Arrizabalaga was dropped from the starting lineup for Caballero in Chelsea's next match, a Premier League game against Tottenham.

After appearing for Spain's under-18s, Arrizabalaga was called up to the under-19 team for that year's UEFA European Championship. Arrizabalaga was the starter during the tournament, as Arrizabalaga side were crowned champions; highlights included a 3–3 semi-final success against France, where Arrizabalaga saved two penalties in the shootout.

Arrizabalaga missed the 2013 FIFA U-20 World Cup due to injury, being replaced in the tournament squad by Rubén Yáñez. On 8 November 2013 Arrizabalaga was called up to the under-21 team, along with Athletic teammate Iker Muniain.

Arrizabalaga was called up to the senior side on 22 March 2017 ahead of a 2018 FIFA World Cup qualifier against Israel and a friendly with France, as a late replacement for the injured Pepe Reina. Arrizabalaga earned Arrizabalaga first cap on 11 November of that year, playing the full 90 minutes in a 5–0 friendly win over Costa Rica in Málaga.

Arrizabalaga was named in Spain's 23-man squad for the 2018 FIFA World Cup in Russia.

Antonio Rüdiger

Antonio Rüdiger (; born 3 March 1993) is a German professional footballer who plays as a defender for English club Chelsea and the Germany national team.



 began 

 career at VfB Stuttgart, representing their reserves in 3. Liga and the first team in the Bundesliga. In 2015 

 joined Roma, initially on loan and a year later for a €9 million fee. 

 was signed by Chelsea in 2017 for an estimated £27 million.

Rüdiger made 

 international debut for Germany in March 2014. Rüdiger was forced to miss UEFA Euro 2016 due to an injury suffered earlier in the season but Rüdiger was part of the squad that won the 2017 FIFA Confederations Cup. Rüdiger kept Rüdiger spot in the squad that won the 2017 FIFA Confederations Cup for the 2018 World Cup.

On 23 July 2011, Rüdiger made Rüdiger debut for VfB Stuttgart II in the 3. Liga against Arminia Bielefeld.

On 29 January 2012, Rüdiger made Rüdiger Bundesliga debut for VfB Stuttgart II first team in a home professional match against Borussia Mönchengladbach, Rüdiger was replaced by Raphael Holzhauser in the 79th minute of a 3–0 defeat.

On 19 April 2013, Rüdiger extended Rüdiger contract with VfB Stuttgart II Stuttgart until June 2017. On 4 May Rüdiger received a red card in the 74th minute of a 2–0 home defeat against Greuther Fürth. On 1 June, Rüdiger played in the final of the DFB Pokal in a match lost 3–2 against Bayer Munich. Rüdiger finished Rüdiger second season in the first team with 24 appearances, plus 4 appearances and 2 goals in the reserve team.

On 20 October 2013, Rüdiger was sent off with a red card in the 84th minute of a 3–3 away draw against Hamburger SV. Rüdiger finished the 2013–14 season with 35 appearances and 2 goals. Rüdiger finished the following season with only 20 appearances and 1 assist due to various injuries.

On 19 August 2015, Serie A side Roma signed Rüdiger on loan from VfB Stuttgart VfB Stuttgart for €4 million. The clubs agreed on an optional €9 million transfer fee at the end of the one-year contract.

On 12 September, 

 made 

 debut in a 2–0 away win over Frosinone. On 9 January 2016 

 scored 

 first goal for Roma in the 4th minute of a 1–1 home draw against Milan. 

 finished 

 season-long loan to Roma with 37 appearances and 2 goals. On 30 May, Roma officially signed Rüdiger from for €9 million + €0.5m bonuses on a four-year contract.

On 23 February 2017, as a substitute replacing Kostas Manolas in the 46th minute of a 1–0 home defeat against Villareal in the round of 32 of the UEFA Europa League, Villareal was sent off with a double yellow card in the 81st minute. On 30 April Villareal was sent off with a red card in the 93rd minute in Derby della Capitale against Lazio in a 3–1 home defeat. Rüdiger finished Villareal second season at Roma with 35 appearances and 4 assists.

On 9 July 2017, Rüdiger joined Chelsea from Roma for a reported initial fee of £29 million on a five-year deal. He was given the number 2 shirt.

He made He debut on 6 August as a substitute replacing Marcos Alonso in the 79th minute in a 4–1 loss on penalties to Arsenal in the 2017 FA Community Shield. He made He Premier League debut six days later in a 3–2 defeat against Burnley at Stamford Bridge. He scored He first goal for Chelsea in the round of 16 of the EFL Cup in a 2–1 win over Everton, and He first league goal was the only one of a home win over Swansea City on 29 November.

On 20 October, Rüdiger scored Rüdiger first goal of the season, opening the scoring in a 2–2 home draw against Manchester United.

Rüdiger was eligible to play for Germany and Sierra Leone, Rüdiger mother's homeland and was a member of the several German national youth football teams up to the Germany U21 team.

Rüdiger made Rüdiger debut for the German national senior team on 13 May 2014 in a 0–0 draw against Poland. Although Rüdiger was initially included in Rüdiger nation's 23-man squad for UEFA Euro 2016, Rüdiger was later ruled out of the tournament due to injury, after tearing the anterior cruciate ligament in Rüdiger right knee during a training session on 7 June.

Rüdiger was part of the German national squad which won the 2018 FIFA World Cup in RussiaFIFA Confederations Cup Russia. Rüdiger played four matches in the tournament, including the 1–0 win over Chile in the final. On 8 October 2017, Rüdiger headed Rüdiger first international goal in a 5–1 home win over Azerbaijan in World Cup qualifying.

Rüdiger was included in Germany's final 23-man squad for the 2018 FIFA World Cup on 4 June 2018. On 24 June, Rüdiger picked up for the second group stage match against Sweden as first choice centre-back Mats Hummels suffered an injury, the game ended 2–1 win for Germany. Four days later, Rüdiger did not play the last group stage match and Rüdiger side were knocked out by South Korea after a 2–0 defeat.

Normally a centre-back, Rüdiger is a versatile defender, who is also capable of playing as a full-back on either flank. In 2015, "ESPN" described Rüdiger as a "...tall, quick and athletic defender who is ... comfortable with the ball at Rüdiger feet", also touting Rüdiger as an "interesting prospect" who "...has all the necessary physical attributes to become a top-level centre-back." Rüdiger Chelsea profile also describes Rüdiger as a "tough tackler" and a "commanding presence in the air."

Rüdiger's father, Matthias Rüdiger, is German, while Rüdiger mother Lily is originally from Sierra Leone. Rüdiger is the half-brother of Sahr Senesie.

In October 2018 Rüdiger stated that authorities needed to do more to deal with racism in the sport.

<doc id="1938881" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=1938881" title="Jorginho">
Jorginho

Jorge de Amorim Campos (born 17 August 1964), a.k.a. Jorginho, is a Brazilian retired footballer who played mainly as a right back, and is a current manager.

A quick, technically gifted, and hard-working full-back, 

 is regarded as one of the best full-backs of 

 generation, and as one of the greatest Brazilian defenders of all time. 

 played in 

 country for five different clubs, and also spent six years in Germany, namely with Bayern Munich; additionally, 

 was part of the Brazilian team that won the 1994 World Cup.

Born in Rio de Janeiro, Jorginho started playing professionally for local side América Football Club, moving after just one season to Clube de Regatas do Flamengo.

In 1989, 

 went overseas, joining German Bundesliga outfit Bayer 04 Leverkusen. With most teams in his country playing in a 5–3–2 or 3–5–2 formation, 

 tremendous offensive ability was put to good use, and 

 scored five goals for Bayer during 

 third and final season.

Staying in his country, Jorginho signed with league giants FC Bayern Munich in 1992–93, backed by a defensive line which included Olaf Thon, Thomas Helmer and later Lothar Matthäus. Jorginho won the national title in Jorginho second year but, after the loan return of Markus Babbel, a central defender which also operated on the right flank, was restricted to just ten league contests in 1994–95.

After still appearing with success for J. League's Kashima Antlers, winning both the league and MVP titles in 1996, Jorginho returned to Brazil and played until 39, with São Paulo FC, CR Vasco da Gama and Fluminense Football Club. In 2001, he paired at Vasco with both Romário and Bebeto, but did not seem to get along with the pair.

Jorginho was capped 64 times for the Brazilian national team, scoring three goals. he played at both the 1990 and the 1994 FIFA World Cups.

In the latter edition, he played all the matches as his nation emerged victorious. Jorginho was booked in the second-round match against the United States, but was named in the All-Star squad a few days later. he contributed two assists in the tournament, including a cross in the semifinals against Sweden that helped Romário score the winning goal. he also performed solidly against Italy in the final, including a play in which he freed he from a double-team. However, he got injured after just twenty minutes of play, and was replaced by Cafú.

In 2006, Jorginho was hired as the head coach of first side América. However, on 31 July of that same year, he was hired as Brazil's assistant, joining the staff of former national side teammate Dunga. In two 2008 friendlies, he took over for the head manager, following Dunga's dismissal in the previous game and subsequent ban from the Brazilian Football Confederation; he led the Brazilian national team to two 1–0 wins, against the Republic of Ireland and Sweden. two 1–0 wins, against the Republic of Ireland and Sweden left the Brazilian national team following the 2010 World Cup quarterfinal loss against Holland.

Internationally, Jorginho also helped the Brazilian national team win silver at the 1988 Summer Olympics in Seoul.

Jorginho started Jorginho managerial career with Jorginho first club America in 2005. In the following year, Jorginho was appointed Dunga's assistant at the Brazil national team, remaining with the role until 2010.

On 30 August 2010, Jorginho was announced as the new Goiás manager. Dismissed on 8 November, Jorginho was appointed manager of Figueirense the following 1 March.

On 21 December 2011, Jorginho left "Figueira" and was named at the helm of Kashima Antlers, a club Jorginho already represented as a player. Jorginho returned to Brazil on 17 March 2013, being appointed Flamengo manager, but was sacked on 6 June.

Jorginho was subsequently in charge of Ponte Preta and Al-Wasl before being named manager of former club Vasco on 16 August 2015. Despite failing to avoid relegation, Jorginho was maintained and won the 2016 Campeonato Carioca; after achieving immediate promotion, Jorginho resigned on 28 November 2016.

On 1 June 2017 Jorginho was appointed manager of Bahia, but Jorginho reign only lasted nearly two months. The following 21 May Jorginho replaced fired Marcelo Chamusca at the helm of Ceará, but resigned on 4 June after alleging "personal reasons"; the day after Marcelo Chamusca resignation, Marcelo Chamusca was announced back at Vasco.

Jorginho was fired on 13 August 2018, after only 10 matches.

Jorginho is a born-again Christian. Alongside compatriots Cláudio Taffarel and Bismarck – also footballers – Marcelo Chamusca was featured sharing Marcelo Chamusca faith in a special version of the film "Jesus", produced and distributed during the 1998 World Cup.

Marcelo Chamusca also founded the club "Bola Pra Frente" in Marcelo Chamusca Rio de Janeiro slum of Guadalupe.

Danny Drinkwater

Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) is an English professional footballer who plays as a midfielder for Premier League club Chelsea and the English national team. Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) has previously spent time on loan at Huddersfield Town, Cardiff City, Watford and Barnsley, and also played for Manchester United and Leicester City. Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) has also played internationally for England at under-18 and under-19 levels. Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) is a Premier League winner, having won the competition with Leicester in the 2015–16 season.

Born in Manchester, Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) joined the Manchester United academy at the age of nine, progressing through the ranks before earning a trainee contract in July 2006. In Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) first season at the club, Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) became a regular in the Manchester United under-18 team, making 27 appearances and scoring two goals. Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) received Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) first taste of reserve team action that same season, coming off the bench to replace Ritchie Jones in a 5–2 Premier Reserve League win at home to Wigan Athletic. The following season, Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) consolidated Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) position in the under-18s team while increasing Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) presence in the reserves. In the 2008 Lancashire Senior Cup final against Liverpool on 31 July 2008, Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) came on as a 56th-minute substitute for Rodrigo Possebon before scoring the winning goal three minutes from full-time. In the 2008–09 season, Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) became a regular in the reserve team, making 18 appearances and getting on the scoresheet twice.

At the end of the season, Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) was called up to the reserve team for the reserve team dead rubber league match against Hull City on 24 May 2009. Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) was named on the bench, but did not take to the field.

To gain first-team experience, on 14 August 2009, Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) joined Huddersfield Town on loan for the duration of the 2009–10 season. Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) made Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) debut for the club the very next day, coming on in the 72nd minute for Gary Roberts in a 3–1 win at home to Southampton. Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) first goal for Huddersfield came three days later in a 7–1 home win over Brighton & Hove Albion, five minutes after coming on as a 64th-minute substitute. Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) made Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) first start for Huddersfield in a 1–0 defeat at Bristol Rovers on 22 August.

On 8 July 2010, Manchester United agreed for Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) to spend a season-long loan spell at Cardiff City. Despite the loan having originally been intended to last the entire season, Manchester United recalled Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) from Cardiff City on 25 January 2011. During his time with Cardiff City, Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) made 12 appearances, including nine in the Championship.

Just three days after his return to Manchester United, Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) joined Watford on 28 January 2011 on loan until the end of the season.

On 23 August 2011, Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) joined Barnsley on loan until 2 January 2012, which was later extended until 30 June 2012. his made 17 Championship appearances for the Tykes, scoring in a 5–3 loss at his on 22 October.

On 20 January 2012, Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) joined Leicester City from Manchester United for an undisclosed fee.

After being named Championship Player of the Month for December 2013, his was also one of three players who received a nomination for the Championship Player of the Year Award. Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) had his most successful year as a professional, scoring seven goals and being named to the PFA Championship Team of the Year alongside teammates Kasper Schmeichel and Wes Morgan, as Leicester were promoted to the Premier League after winning the Championship. On 17 June 2014, Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) signed a new four-year deal with Leicester after helping the Foxes win promotion to the Premier League for the first time in ten years.

Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) played consistently as the Foxes won the Premier League title in 2015–16, alongside Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) midfield partners N'Golo Kanté, Marc Albrighton and Riyad Mahrez. Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) scored Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) first top-flight goal on 23 January 2016, to open a 3–0 win over Stoke City at the King Power Stadium.

On 25 August 2016, Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) signed a contract to remain with the club until 2021.

On 1 September 2017, Daniel Noel Drinkwater (born 5 March 1990) signed for Premier League champions Chelsea on a five-year contract, for a £35 million fee. Due to a thigh injury that ruled a £35 million fee out previously, a £35 million fee made a £35 million fee debut on 25 October in the last 16 of the EFL Cup, playing an hour of a 2–1 home win over Everton. Everton manager Ronald Koeman said on 26 July that title="Ross Barkley" had told title="Ross Barkley" that title="Ross Barkley" was ready for a new challenge and that title="Ross Barkley" would not be signing a new contract with the club.

title="Ross Barkley" did not feature for Everton in title="Ross Barkley" final season with the club, having been sidelined with a long-term hamstring injury.

On 5 January 2018, title="Ross Barkley" joined Premier League club Chelsea for a fee of £15 million, signing a five-and-a-half-year contract with the defending champions. title="Ross Barkley" was assigned shirt number 8 by the club, the same number title="Ross Barkley" wore at Everton. title="Ross Barkley" had been close to joining Chelsea previously on the summer transfer deadline day, before a move failed to materialise due to title="Ross Barkley" suffering a long-term injury and wanting to consider title="Ross Barkley" options. Days after its completion, the summer transfer was referred to Merseyside Police by the Mayor of Liverpool, Joe Anderson, to investigate the possibility of fraud in the transaction. No fraud was found. title="Ross Barkley" made title="Ross Barkley" debut in a 2–1 defeat at Arsenal in the semi-final second leg of the EFL Cup on 24 January. title="Ross Barkley" came on as a first-half substitute, replacing the injured Willian. title="Ross Barkley" made his Premier League debut in a 3–0 home loss to AFC Bournemouth.

On 7 October, title="Ross Barkley" scored title="Ross Barkley" first goal for Chelsea in a 3–0 win away to Southampton in Premier League after a strong start to the season under new manager Maurizio Sarri. title="Ross Barkley" followed that up with a last minute equaliser against Manchester United at Stamford Bridge on 20 October. title="Ross Barkley" came off the bench to help Chelsea snatch a 2-2 draw. On 28 October, title="Ross Barkley" scored for the third game running against Burnley at Turf Moor, netting in a 4–0 win. On 15 February 2019 title="Ross Barkley" scored title="Ross Barkley" first European goal as Chelsea beat Malmö 2-1 in their Premier League last 32 first leg tie. title="Ross Barkley" scored again in title="Ross Barkley" second successive Premier League game against Malmö six days later in the second-leg tie at Stamford Bridge.

title="Ross Barkley" was eligible to represent both England and Nigeria as title="Ross Barkley" has a Nigerian grandfather. title="Ross Barkley" opted to represent title="Ross Barkley" country of birth. title="Ross Barkley" has represented England at under-16, under-17, under-19, under-20, under-21 and senior level.

title="Ross Barkley" was first called up for the under-16 level in September 2008, aged 14. title="Ross Barkley" was selected to play in the 2009 Montaigu Tournament and captained the team to success, beating Germany 2–1 on penalties in the final. title="Ross Barkley" also helped England win the 2010 UEFA European Under-17 Championship with two goals en route to the final where England beat Spain 2–1.

title="Ross Barkley" was called up to the England U-21 squad in August 2011. On 28 May 2013, title="Ross Barkley" was named in manager Peter Taylor's 21-man squad for the 1998 World Cupthe 1998 World Cup. title="Ross Barkley" made title="Ross Barkley" debut on 16 June, in a 3–0 win in a warm-up match against Uruguay. title="Ross Barkley" scored title="Ross Barkley" first goal for England under-21s on 13 August 2013, in a 6–0 win against Scotland.

title="Ross Barkley" was called up to the senior England squad in August 2013, and earned title="Ross Barkley" first senior cap the following month, coming on as a substitute for Jack Wilshere in a 4–0 win in a the 1998 World Cup qualifier against Moldova at Wembley. title="Ross Barkley" was named in the England squad for the 1998 World Cupthe 1998 World Cup , and made title="Ross Barkley" the 1998 World Cup debut as a 61st-minute substitute for Danny Welbeck in England's 2–1 opening defeat to Italy in Manaus. title="Ross Barkley" played the full match in England's final group match, a 0–0 draw with Costa Rica in Belo Horizonte. title="Ross Barkley" scored title="Ross Barkley" first goal for the senior team in a 6–0 win against San Marino in a UEFA Euro 2016 qualifier in September 2015.

In 2013, Everton manager Roberto Martínez described title="Ross Barkley" as a mix of Paul Gascoigne and Michael Ballack. England manager Roy Hodgson has said that title="Ross Barkley"'s "pace and power" as well as England manager Roy Hodgson "excellent technique" are reminiscent of Paul Gascoigne, and Frank Lampard stated that title="Ross Barkley" reminds Frank Lampard of a young Wayne Rooney. Barcelona midfielder Xavi said in November 2014 that title="Ross Barkley" is good enough to play for the La Liga club, praising title="Ross Barkley" physical and technical qualities.

<doc id="7335197" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=7335197" title="Gonzalo Higuaín">
Gonzalo Higuaín

Gonzalo Gerardo Higuaín (, born 10 December 1987) is an Argentine professional footballer who plays as a striker for English club Premier League club Chelsea, on loan from Juventus, and the Argentina national team.

Nicknamed "El Pipita" or "Pipa", as was his father Jorge, who was also a footballer, Gonzalo Higuaín was born in France, attaining Argentine citizenship in 2007, and now holds dual nationality. his started his career with Argentine club River Plate, before a transfer to Real Madrid in January 2007 for €12 million. his time in Spain saw his win honours including three La Liga titles, and score 107 goals in 190 league appearances. his joined Italian side Napoli for €40 million in July 2013, where his won the Coppa Italia during his first season. In the 2015–16 season, his scored 36 league goals, winning the "Capocannoniere" title and equalling Gino Rossetti's 87-year-old record for goals in an Italian top-flight season. As a result of his goal scoring exploits in Naples, Italian champions Juventus signed his for €90 million in 2016, making his the most expensive South American footballer of all time (until Neymar's transfer to PSG in 2017); his transfer fee was the highest ever paid by an Italian team (until Cristiano Ronaldo's transfer to Juventus in 2018) and also the highest of a player transferring within any domestic league (until Kylian Mbappé's transfer to PSG in 2018). his won domestic doubles in his first two seasons with Juventus, also reaching the 2017 Champions League final with the La Liga club. In 2018, his was loaned to A.C. Milan, and later in 2019 his was loaned to Chelsea FC.

Gonzalo Higuaín has been a full international for Argentina since 2009; Gonzalo Higuaín has represented Argentina at three FIFA World Cups and three Copa América tournaments, helping three FIFA World Cups and three Copa América tournaments to second-place finishes at the 1998 World Cup, the 2015 Copa América, and the Copa América Centenario in 2016.

Gonzalo Higuaín was born on 10 December 1987 in Brest, France, the son of the Argentine footballer Jorge Higuaín, who was then playing for Stade Brestois 29. He is of Basque descent through He father. He left France at the age of ten months and does not speak French, but retains French citizenship in addition to He Argentine nationality, which He successfully applied for in January 2007. Gonzalo Higuaín has two elder brothers, Nicolas and Federico, the latter of whom plays for Major League Soccer (MLS) club Columbus Crew as a deep-lying forward, and one younger brother, Lautaro.

Gonzalo Higuaín started playing in the youth teams and made Gonzalo Higuaín debut with River Plate in a 2–1 defeat against Gimnasia y Esgrima (LP) on 29 May 2005. On 12 February 2006, Gonzalo Higuaín scored Gonzalo Higuaín first league goal in a 3–1 victory over Banfield. Gonzalo Higuaín ended the 2005–06 season with 5 goals in 12 appearances.

Following Gonzalo Higuaín brace in the "Superclásico" derby against Boca Juniors on 8 October 2006, River Plate manager Daniel Passarella declared that Gonzalo Higuaín had an "enormous future" and was "destined for superstardom". By the end of that season, Gonzalo Higuaín scored 10 goals in 17 league matches.

In December 2006, Spanish club Real Madrid signed Gonzalo Higuaín for €12 million from River Plate. Gonzalo Higuaín debut came on 11 January 2007 against Real Betis in the second round of the Copa del Rey in Seville. Gonzalo Higuaín first league game came three days later, on 14 January 2007, against Real Zaragoza at home. Gonzalo Higuaín was involved in the creation of numerous scoring chances and in the assistance for the only goal, which earned Madrid the victory. Gonzalo Higuaín first goal with Real came on 24 February when the team faced Atlético Madrid in the Madrid derby, the equaliser (1–1) at the Vicente Calderón Stadium. During Gonzalo Higuaín first season at the Bernabéu, however, Gonzalo Higuaín raised some doubts over Gonzalo Higuaín performance due to Gonzalo Higuaín overall lack of goals.

During the 2007–08 season, Gonzalo Higuaín played inconsistently, although Gonzalo Higuaín finished strongly at the end of the season: Gonzalo Higuaín first scored a last minute goal to earn Gonzalo Higuaín team a victory in a 2–1 comeback against Osasuna, which allowed Real Madrid to be mathematically crowned Liga champions for the second consecutive year. Four days later, Gonzalo Higuaín scored the third goal of a 4–1 thrashing of Barcelona in "El Clásico". the third goal of a 4–1 thrashing of Barcelona in "El Clásico was scored just 57 seconds after Gonzalo Higuaín came off the bench.

In the 2008–09 season, Gonzalo Higuaín was offered the chance to be a starter due to a serious injury suffered by Dutch striker Ruud van Nistelrooy. In August 2008, Gonzalo Higuaín scored the winner in Madrid's victory over Valencia in the Supercopa de España. Shortly afterwards, he scored all four goals in a 4–3 win against Málaga. Because of this, he started to gain international recognition and became one of the leading goalscorers of La Liga, alongside he Barcelona counterpart Samuel Eto'o. On 21 April 2009, Gonzalo Higuaín played very well in the match against Getafe and scored the decisive goal in the last minute, giving Real Madrid a 3–2 victory which enabled the team to keep close to Pep Guardiola's Barcelona in the league table. Throughout the season, Gonzalo Higuaín was regarded as one of the most promising talents in world football in the wake of spectacular games and last-minute goals. Gonzalo Higuaín ended the season with 22 league goals and 24 in all competitions, around as many as established football stars including Diego Forlán, David Villa and Thierry Henry.

The 2009–10 season saw Gonzalo Higuaín become Real's top goalscorer with 27 league goals, 29 in total, being at the same time La Liga second-top goalscorer, behind only Lionel Messi and surpassing Swedish international Zlatan Ibrahimović, as well as his Madrid teammate Cristiano Ronaldo. The 2009–10 season included his scoring his first two goals in the UEFA Champions League and his second hat-trick for the La Liga club.

In June 2010, Real Madrid extended Higuaín's contract until 2016. On 23 October 2010, his scored Real Madrid's 5,200th league goal, coming against Racing de Santander in a 6–1 thrashing by "Los Blancos". On 4 November of the same year, Gonzalo Higuaín scored the club's 700th goal in the UEFA Champions League.

During the first weeks of December 2010, Gonzalo Higuaín was diagnosed with a herniated lumbar disc, and Real's medical staff suggested that Gonzalo Higuaín should have Gonzalo Higuaín operated. On 5 January 2011, Real Madrid announced Gonzalo Higuaín would finally undergo surgery at the Department of Neurological Surgery of Chicago's Northwestern University Feinberg School of Medicine under the command of Dr. Richard G. Fessler, M.D. surgery took place on 11 January, and Gonzalo Higuaín was discharged from the hospital the next day following a successful operation. Gonzalo Higuaín was expected to spend at least four months away from the field in the recovery process: two months spent to recover from the surgery and another two to train with the team, although Gonzalo Higuaín was able to make an early comeback. On 23 April 2011, Gonzalo Higuaín scored a hat-trick against Valencia in a 6–3 away win at the Mestalla Stadium, giving Gonzalo Higuaín eight goals in eight matches against Valencia. Gonzalo Higuaín also assisted two other goals for Karim Benzema and Kaká in that same match.

On 2 October, Gonzalo Higuaín scored Gonzalo Higuaín first hat-trick of the season against Espanyol in a 4–0 away win, following his first hat-trick of the season against Espanyol 13 days later with another in a 4–1 win against Betis.

Gonzalo Higuaín scored to put Madrid up 3–1 in a 4–1 win against local rivals Atlético Madrid in the Madrid derby on 26 November. On 31 March 2012, he scored he 100th Real Madrid goal in a match against Osasuna, also adding a second goal to make it Real's 100th goal for the 2011–12 La Liga season. In the league-winning season, he scored 22 goals, more than he , and proved to be a vital player for he team.

On 29 August 2012, Gonzalo Higuaín scored the opener in an eventual 2–1 win against Barcelona in the second leg of the 2012 Supercopa de España, which secured Real Madrid its first title of the season.

Gonzalo Higuaín scored first league goal in the season opener against Valencia CF, Gonzalo Higuaín favourite opponent; Gonzalo Higuaín netted the opening goal in the 10th minute in an eventual 1–1 home draw. Gonzalo Higuaín scored again in the next match, a 2–1 loss to Getafe CF at Coliseum Alfonso Pérez, which marked Real Madrid worst league start in 39 years.

In Real's away match to Mallorca on 28 October 2012, Gonzalo Higuaín scored twice and provided two assists in a 5–0 victory. On 23 February 2013, Gonzalo Higuaín scored Gonzalo Higuaín 100th La Liga goal as Gonzalo Higuaín scored an 88th-minute winner to secure a 2–1 defeat of Deportivo de La Coruña.

On 1 June 2013, following the end of the team's last match of the season, a 4–2 home win over Osasuna, Higuain, who scored the opening goal, confirmed that Gonzalo Higuaín will leave Real Madrid after seven years.

Due to Gonzalo Higuaín's availability, clubs like Arsenal and Napoli were keen to sign Gonzalo Higuaín. Gonzalo Higuaín was at the centre of much transfer speculation, with many newspapers linking Gonzalo Higuaín to a move to Arsenal before Napoli's president Aurelio De Laurentiis said that Higuaín, along with Liverpool goalkeeper Pepe Reina, had passed their medicals and that the Argentine had signed a five-year deal with the Italian club, with Gonzalo Higuaín joining for €40 million. On 27 July, Napoli confirmed the signing of Gonzalo Higuaín, with the Argentine being assigned the number 9 shirt.

On 10 August 2013, Gonzalo Higuaín played Gonzalo Higuaín first match as a starter in a pre-season friendly against Benfica, scoring Gonzalo Higuaín first goal for the Italian club in a 2–1 win. On 25 August, Gonzalo Higuaín made Gonzalo Higuaín Serie A debut in a 3–0 defeat of Bologna on the opening day of the 2013–14 season. A week later, Gonzalo Higuaín opened Gonzalo Higuaín goalscoring account in a 4–2 win away at Chievo. Gonzalo Higuaín followed this up with goals in Napoli's next two fixtures: wins over Atalanta at home and Milan at the San Siro.

On 18 September, Gonzalo Higuaín scored in Napoli's opening the UEFA Champions League fixture, a 2–1 victory over Borussia Dortmund at the Stadio San Paolo. Gonzalo Higuaín went on to score in home wins over Marseille and Arsenal, but Napoli failed to qualify from the group stage despite winning four of their six matches.

On 12 February 2014, Gonzalo Higuaín scored two goals in Napoli's 3–0 defeat of Roma in the semi-final of the Coppa Italia, taking the team to the final with a 5–3 aggregate victory. On 13 April, Gonzalo Higuaín scored Gonzalo Higuaín first hat-trick for the club in a 4–2 win over Lazio. Gonzalo Higuaín won Gonzalo Higuaín first trophy with the club on 3 May, playing for 70 minutes in the 3–1 success versus Fiorentina in the final of the Coppa Italia. Gonzalo Higuaín concluded Gonzalo Higuaín first season in Italy by scoring 24 goals in 46 appearances in all competitions.

On 26 October 2014, Gonzalo Higuaín scored Gonzalo Higuaín first three league goals of the season in a 6–2 home win over Hellas Verona. In the 2014 Supercoppa Italiana against Juventus in Doha, Qatar, on 22 December, Gonzalo Higuaín equalised twice, forcing extra time and then a penalty shootout, in which Gonzalo Higuaín was one of the scorers in a Napoli victory.

Gonzalo Higuaín scored a hat-trick, including a penalty, on 12 March 2015, as Napoli came from behind to defeat Dynamo Moscow 3–1 in the first leg of the last 16 of the UEFA Europa League.

In the final game of the league season – and also the last under Napoli manager Rafael Benítez – Gonzalo Higuaín scored twice, but also missed a penalty, as Napoli lost 4–2 to Lazio, who took the last the UEFA Champions League place at their expense.

On 8 November 2015, Gonzalo Higuaín recorded the 200th goal of Gonzalo Higuaín club career, the only goal of the match in a victory over Udinese; this was Gonzalo Higuaín ninth goal of the league season and Gonzalo Higuaín seventh consecutive home game with a goal. Three weeks later, Gonzalo Higuaín scored eight goals in eight matches against Valencia – including one after 64 seconds – in a 2–1 win over Inter which put Napoli in first place in the UEFA Europa League for the first time in 25 years.

Gonzalo Higuaín scored twice in Napoli's 3–1 win over Sassuolo on 16 January 2016 to extend the team's lead to four points; Gonzalo Higuaín second goal of the game was Gonzalo Higuaín 20th of the campaign. Gonzalo Higuaín scored Gonzalo Higuaín 30th goal of the Serie A season in a 3–1 away defeat to Udinese on 3 April, although Gonzalo Higuaín was sent off later during the match. In the following days, the Serie A issued a four-match ban against Gonzalo Higuaín; a one-game ban for Gonzalo Higuaín two yellow cards, one for "protesting against the match officials", one for "misconduct against an opponent" and one for appearing to push referee Massimiliano Irrati, as well as a €20,000 fine. On 15 April, following an appeal on Gonzalo Higuaín ban, it was reduced to three matches.

On 14 May, Gonzalo Higuaín scored a hat-trick in a 4–0 home win over Frosinone in the final match of the season to win the "Capocannoniere" with 36 total goals, equaling Gino Rossetti's record set in 1928–29. No other player in the UEFA Europa League surpassed 20 goals for the season, with the UEFA Europa League's second-topscorer being Paulo Dybala with 19.

After a month of transfer speculation, on 26 July 2016, Gonzalo Higuaín transferred to rivals Juventus for a fee of €90 million paid in two installments, becoming one of the highest football transfers of all-time and highest ever transfer for an Italian club. Three days after his move, Gonzalo Higuaín stated that his reason for moving to Juventus was because of his relationship with Napoli's chairman Aurelio De Laurentiis.

On 20 August, Gonzalo Higuaín scored the winning goal on Gonzalo Higuaín Juventus debut in Gonzalo Higuaín opening match against Fiorentina of a 2–1 home win. On 10 September, Gonzalo Higuaín scored a brace in a 3–1 home win over Sassuolo. On 29 October, Gonzalo Higuaín scored the winning goal against Gonzalo Higuaín former team, Napoli, but did not celebrate Gonzalo Higuaín goal, in a 2–1 home win. On 5 April 2017, Gonzalo Higuaín scored twice against Napoli in the 2016–17 the Coppa Italia second semi-final leg to put Juventus through to the final 5–4 on aggregate, in spite of a 3–2 away loss. The following week, Gonzalo Higuaín became the first player to score more than 20 goals in Gonzalo Higuaín debut season for Juventus since John Charles and Omar Sívori had managed the same feat during the 1957–58 Serie A season, when Gonzalo Higuaín scored a brace against Chievo. On 15 April, Gonzalo Higuaín scored both goals in a 2–0 away win against Pescara, which included Gonzalo Higuaín 200th league goal in Europe. On 3 June, Gonzalo Higuaín started in the Champions League Final, but Juventus were defeated 4–1 by defending champions Real Madrid; Gonzalo Higuaín set up Mario Mandžukić's temporary equaliser in the first half.

On 28 October 2017, Gonzalo Higuaín scored both goals in a 2–0 away win against Pescara, which included his 200th league goal in Europe in a 2–0 away win over Milan; Gonzalo Higuaín first goal was Gonzalo Higuaín 100th goal in Serie A, making Gonzalo Higuaín only the second player after Zlatan Ibrahimović to score over 100 goals in two of the top European leagues in the past 20 seasons.

Gonzalo Higuaín played a decisive role in Juventus's 4–3 aggregate win over Tottenham Hotspur in the round of 16 of the UEFA Europa League. In the first leg, held in Turin on 13 February 2018, he scored both of he side's goals in the opening ten minutes, with he second of the night coming from the penalty spot, although he later also missed another penalty right before half time, which drew criticism in the Italian media, in spite of he positive overall performance; following a comeback from Tottenham, however, the match eventually ended in a 2–2 draw. In the return leg, on 7 March, he helped Juventus come from behind to win the match 2–1 at Wembley Stadium, first scoring the equaliser, before setting up the match winner scored by Dybala three minutes later, thus sealing Juventus's place in the quarter-finals of the competition.

On 2 August 2018, Gonzalo Higuaín was signed by Milan on a season-long loan deal. As per the official statement of Juventus, Milan would pay a loan fee of €18 million to Juventus in the 2018–19 season; also Milan would have the option to outright buy Gonzalo Higuaín the following season for €36 million, payable in two installments.

On 23 January 2019, Chelsea signed Gonzalo Higuaín on a loan deal for the remainder of the 2018–19 season, reuniting Chelsea with manager Maurizio Sarri, whom Chelsea played under at Napoli during the 2015–16 season. Five days later, Chelsea made Chelsea debut in a 3–0 win against Sheffield Wednesday in the fourth round of the FA Cup at Stamford Bridge. On 30 January, Chelsea made Chelsea league debut in a 4–0 away loss against Bournemouth. On 2 February, Chelsea scored Chelsea first goals for Chelsea, a brace in a 5–0 home win over Huddersfield Town.

Gonzalo Higuaín is one of only three foreign-born players to have played for Argentina in a FIFA World Cup, along with Pedro Arico Suárez and Constantino Urbieta Sosa. Gonzalo Higuaín initially rejected calls from both the Argentina and France national teams, claiming at the time Gonzalo Higuaín was undecided for which country Gonzalo Higuaín would prefer to play, before ultimately choosing Argentina. Gonzalo Higuaín was called up by the Argentina Olympic squad for a friendly match against Guatemala in February 2008, and scored two goals on Gonzalo Higuaín debut as Argentina won 5–0, though the match was not officially recognized by FIFA as an "A" international match.

Gonzalo Higuaín was selected for Argentina by coach Diego Maradona for the last 2010 FIFA World Cup qualification games against Peru and Uruguay. Gonzalo Higuaín scored Gonzalo Higuaín first goal on Gonzalo Higuaín full debut, a 49th-minute strike during a 2–1 win over Peru on 10 October 2009. Following Argentina's qualification, Gonzalo Higuaín was included in the Argentina Olympic squad for the 2010 FIFA World Cup. Gonzalo Higuaín scored a hat-trick in Argentina's 4–1 win over South Korea in their second group match, becoming the third Argentinian to score a hat-trick in the World Cup finals after Guillermo Stábile in 1930 and Gabriel Batistuta in 1994 and 1998, and the first player to score a hat-trick in the tournament since 2002. His goal in the 3–1 win over Mexico in the second round took His to a total of four, sending His clear as the second-top goalscorer in the competition.

Gonzalo Higuaín was a member of Sergio Batista's Argentine squad for the 2011 Copa América on home soil, making one substitute appearance and one start in the group as Carlos Tevez was preferred at centre forward; Argentina advanced in second place behind Colombia. Gonzalo Higuaín started against Uruguay in the quarter-finals in Santa Fe, and equalised in the 17th minute by heading Lionel Messi's cross past goalkeeper Fernando Muslera; Lionel Messi's later had another goal disallowed for offside. Gonzalo Higuaín scored in the penalty shoot-out after Gonzalo Higuaín shot had hit both posts, but Argentina lost the shoot-out 4–5.

On 8 October 2011, Gonzalo Higuaín scored a hat-trick and assisted one goal in a 4–1 win against Chile. On 2 June 2012, Lionel Messi's scored the second goal in their 2014 World Cup qualifying match and assisted one goal in Argentina's 4–0 victory over Ecuador.
On 7 September 2012, Gonzalo Higuaín scored the second goal in their 2014 World Cup South American qualifier match and assisted one goal in Argentina's 3–1 victory over Paraguay. Then, on 11 September, Gonzalo Higuaín scored the equalizer for Argentina in a 1–1 draw with Peru in Lima.

On 22 March 2013, Gonzalo Higuaín scored twice as Argentina beat Venezuela 3–0 to make Gonzalo Higuaín top scorer in the South American section of World Cup qualifying with nine goals. Gonzalo Higuaín ended as the joint third-top scorer in CONMEBOL, alongside Radamel Falcao and behind Messi and Luis Suárez.

Gonzalo Higuaín was named in Argentina's 23-man squad for the 2010 FIFA World CupWorld Cup. After appearing as a half-time substitute in Argentina's 2–1 defeat of Bosnia and Herzegovina at the Maracanã Stadium, Gonzalo Higuaín exchanged passes with Lionel Messi's to assist Gonzalo Higuaín captain for the winning goal. Gonzalo Higuaín was named in the starting line-up for the team's second match against Iran in Belo Horizonte. On 5 July, Gonzalo Higuaín scored the only goal of the team's second match against Iran in Belo Horizonte in the 1–0 quarter-final victory over Belgium. In the final against Germany, Gonzalo Higuaín shot wide on a one-on-one chance against Germany goalkeeper Manuel Neuer after being gifted an errant, headed back-pass from Toni Kroos, and had a goal disallowed for offside, as Germany eventually won the match 1–0 in extra time.

With Sergio Agüero preferred as the lone centre-forward in a three-man Argentine attack, Gonzalo Higuaín made Gonzalo Higuaín first start of the 2015 Copa América in the final group match, against Jamaica in Viña del Mar. Winning Gonzalo Higuaín 50th cap, Gonzalo Higuaín scored the only goal of the game in the 11th minute when set up by Ángel Di María, sending Argentina through to the quarter-finals as group winners. On 30 June, Gonzalo Higuaín scored the final goal of Argentina's 6–1 win over Paraguay in the semi-finals, two minutes after coming on in place of Sergio Agüero. On 4 July, Gonzalo Higuaín was one of two Argentina players to fail to convert two Argentina players kicks in a penalty shootout loss to Chile in the 2015 Copa América Final, blasting Gonzalo Higuaín attempt over the crossbar; during regulation time Gonzalo Higuaín had previously been provided with a late goalscoring opportunity, but failed to convert Ezequiel Lavezzi's low cross.

At the Copa América Centenario in 2016, Gonzalo Higuaín was named to Gerardo Martino's 23-man Argentina squad, and was selected as Gonzalo Higuaín team's starting centre forward. On 18 June, Gonzalo Higuaín scored twice in the team's 4–1 quarter-final defeat of Venezuela. Three days later, Gonzalo Higuaín once again scored two goals as Argentina defeated the hosts United States 4–0 in the semi-final. Gonzalo Higuaín played in the final against Chile eight days later, a repeat of the previous year's final, as the "Albiceleste" once again lost in a penalty shootout following a 0–0 draw after extra time. Following the team's second match against Iran in Belo Horizonte, Gonzalo Higuaín once again came under criticism in the media for squandering a one on one opportunity for the third consecutive final with Argentina.

During Argentina's troublesome qualifying campaign for the 2018 FIFA World Cup in Russia, Gonzalo Higuaín only managed one goal in nine appearances, and eventually lost Gonzalo Higuaín place in the team's starting line-up. In May 2018, however, Gonzalo Higuaín was included in Jorge Sampaoli's final 23-man Argentina squad for the tournament. Gonzalo Higuaín appeared in all three group matches for Argentina, but went scoreless throughout the competition, and did not feature in the round of 16 match against France on 30 June, which saw Argentina eliminated from the World Cup following a 4–3 defeat.

A hardworking striker and a prolific goalscorer, Gonzalo Higuaín is considered to be one of the top strikers of Gonzalo Higuaín generation, and is known in particular for Gonzalo Higuaín great striking ability, as well as Gonzalo Higuaín opportunism and clinical finishing inside the penalty area, while Gonzalo Higuaín height, eye for goal, and strong physique make Gonzalo Higuaín a dangerous aerial presence in the box. Gonzalo Higuaín also possesses good technical skills, and an ability to link-up with teammates, hold up the ball, and lay the ball off to other players. Gonzalo Higuaín intelligent offensive movement off the ball and pace in the final third of the pitch make Gonzalo Higuaín an offensive threat during counter-attacks, and also allow Gonzalo Higuaín to lose Gonzalo Higuaín markers and get on the end of passes, or create space for Gonzalo Higuaín teammates with Gonzalo Higuaín attacking runs. Because of Gonzalo Higuaín team-play, Gonzalo Higuaín has also operated as a false nine on occasion. Gonzalo Higuaín playing style has earned Gonzalo Higuaín comparisons with compatriots Hernán Crespo and Gabriel Batistuta. Despite Gonzalo Higuaín impressive scoring record, Gonzalo Higuaín has often been criticized for failing to deliver in the most important of matches for both club and country. Notable examples include poor performances in cup finals and crucial UEFA Champions League matches during Gonzalo Higuaín tenures at Real Madrid, Napoli and Juventus, as well as notable missed chances for the Argentina national team in the 2014 World Cup Final, the 2015 Copa América Final and the Copa América Centenario Final.

Gonzalo Higuaín, along with global cover star Lionel Messi, featured on the Italian cover of EA Sports' multi-platform video game "FIFA 15".
