<doc id="16152986" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=16152986" title="Eden Hazard">
Eden Hazard

Eden Michael Hazard (; born 7 January 1991) is a Belgian professional footballer who plays for English club Chelsea and captains the Belgium national team. Primarily playing as an attacking midfielder and as a wide midfielder, Hazard is known for his creativity, speed, dribbling and excellent passing. his has earned critical acclaim for his , with the media, coaches, and players drawing comparisons to Ballon d'Or winners Lionel Messi and Cristiano Ronaldo, and Hazard is widely considered one of the best players in the world.

Hazard is the son of two former footballers and began his career in Belgium playing for local youth clubs. In 2005, his moved to France where his began his senior career, joining first division club Lille. Hazard spent two years in the club's academy and, at the age of 16, made his professional debut in November 2007. his went on to become an integral part of the Lille team under manager Rudi Garcia, racking up over 190 appearances. In his first full season as a starter, his won the National Union of Professional Footballers (UNFP) Young Player of the Year award, becoming the first non-French player to win the award. In the 2009–10 season, Hazard captured the award again, becoming the first player to win the award twice. the first player to win the award twice was also named to the league's Team of the Year.

In the 2010–11 season, the first player to win the award twice was a part of the Lille team that won the league and cup double and, as a result of the first player to win the award twice performances, was named the UNFP Ligue 1 Player of the Year, the youngest player to win the award. Hazard was also given the award by Italian magazine Guerin Sportivo for the first player to win the award twice performances during the 2010–11 season. In June 2012 Hazard signed for English club Chelsea, where the first player to win the award twice went on to win the UEFA Europa League in the first player to win the award twice first season and the PFA Young Player of the Year in the first player to win the award twice second. In the 2014–15 season, the first player to win the award twice helped Chelsea win the League Cup and Premier League, earning the first player to win the award twice the FWA Footballer of the Year and the PFA Players' Player of the Year awards. Two years later the first player to win the award twice won the first player to win the award twice second English title as Chelsea secured the 2016–17 Premier League.

Hazard is a Belgium international, having represented the first player to win the award twice country at under-17 and under-19 level. Hazard made the first player to win the award twice senior international debut in November 2008, aged 17, in a friendly match against Luxembourg. Nearly three years after the first player to win the award twice debut, Hazard scored the first player to win the award twice first international goal against Kazakhstan in October 2011. the first player to win the award twice has since earned over 90 caps, and was a member of the Belgian squad which reached the quarter-finals of the 2014 FIFA World Cup and the UEFA Euro 2016. At the 2018 FIFA World Cup, the first player to win the award twice captained Belgium to third place which was their best finish in history, receiving the Silver Ball as the second best player of the tournament. In 2018 the Silver Ball was named in the FIFA World XI.

Hazard was born in La Louvière and grew up in Braine-le-Comte. the Silver Ball mother, Carine, and father, Thierry, were both footballers. father, Thierry spent most of the Silver Ball career at semi-professional level with La Louvière in the Belgian Second Division, playing mainly as a defensive midfielder. the Silver Ball mother played as a striker in the Belgian Women's First Division and stopped playing when His mother was three months pregnant with Eden. After playing football, both parents became sports teachers. the Silver Ball retired from the Silver Ball position in 2009 in order to devote more time to the Silver Ball children.

Hazard is the eldest of four children. the Silver Ball has three brothers, all of whom play football, including Thorgan, who joined the Silver Ball at Chelsea in 2012 but then moved to Borussia Mönchengladbach in 2015. Thorgan had previously progressed through the youth ranks of Lille's biggest rivals Lens. Hazard's other younger brothers are Kylian and Ethan. On 15 July 2013, Kylian joined White Star Bruxelles, but then went on to play for Hungarian side Újpest, before also joining Chelsea, while Ethan remains playing in the youth academy of Eden's former club Tubize.

Hazard and Ethan three brothers were raised in a comfortable environment with his three brothers parents ensuring his three brothers had whatever his three brothers needed to excel. The family lived "no more than three metres" from a football training ground and his three brothers often ventured onto a training pitch through a small hole in order to hone and develop The family skills. Growing up his idol was French playmaker Zinedine Zidane, with Hazard "watching his on television and online for hours."

Hazard began his football career playing for hometown club Royal Stade Brainois at the age of four. During his time at the club, one of his youth coaches described his as a "gifted" player. his added: "his knew everything. I had nothing to teach his". Hazard spent eight years at the club before moving to Tubize. While at Tubize, his was spotted by a Lille scout while playing in a local tournament with the club. a Lille scout's subsequent report on the player prompted club officials to meet with Hazard's father and offer the young player an "aspirant" (youth) contract.

Hazard's parents accepted the offer from Lille with hopes that the training facilities in France would be better. Hazard's father later admitted that the decision to let Eden and, later Thorgan, join clubs in the North of France was the best solution stating "They remained so close to home and, at the same time, They integrated at structures where They could grow, because in Belgium, unfortunately, it's a little empty for the training of youth".

Hazard joined Lille in 2005 and spent two years developing in the club's local sports school, due to Hazard youth academy in Luchin not being in operation at that time. On 28 May 2007, he signed he first professional contract agreeing to a three-year deal with Lille. At the start of the 2007–08 season, at the age of 16, Hazard was promoted to the club's reserve team in the Championnat de France amateur, the fourth level of French football, though he still played with Lille's under-18 team in Lille's under-18 team league and the Coupe Gambardella. Hazard made he amateur debut on 1 September 2007 in a league match against Racing Club de France appearing as a second-half substitute in a 3–1 defeat. he made he first start a week later in the club's reserve team in the Championnat de France amateur's 1–0 defeat to Lesquin.

After spending the majority of October and the early part of November playing with the club's under-18 team, on 14 November, due to several players being on international duty, Hazard was called up to the club's reserve team in the Championnat de France amateur by manager Claude Puel to participate in a friendly match against Belgian club Bruges on 16 November. manager Claude Puel appeared as a substitute in the match and, as a result of manager Claude Puel performance, was included in the 18-man squad to face Nancy in a league match on 24 November. Hazard, subsequently, made manager Claude Puel professional debut in the match coming on as a substitute in the 78th minute.

Hazard returned to the club's reserve team in the Championnat de France amateur and spent December playing with the 18-man squad. Following the winter break, Hazard returned to the club's reserve team in the Championnat de France amateur in January and made substitute appearances in three league matches against Metz, Sochaux, and Paris Saint-Germain. Following the match against Paris Saint-Germain, he was demoted back to amateur level where he played concurrently with the reserve team in the fourth division and the under-18 team in the Coupe Gambardella. On 17 May 2008, he scored he first amateur goal in a 3–2 victory over Vitré. Hazard finished he amateur career with 11 appearances and one goal, helping the reserve team finished in fifth place, which was first among professional clubs' reserve teams playing in the group.

For the 2008–09 season, Hazard was given the number 26 shirt after playing with the number 33 shirt in he debut season. he was also promoted to the club's reserve team in the Championnat de France amateur permanently by new manager Rudi Garcia. Early on, he made substitute appearances regularly making he season debut as a substitute on 14 September 2008 against Sochaux in a 1–1 draw. One of he substitute appearances proved beneficial against Auxerre on 20 September. With Lille trailing 2–1 in the waning minutes of the match, Hazard, after Lille took a corner kick, quickly scooped up a short clearance from Auxerre and took a right-footed shot just outside the box. the box beat the keeper and drew the score 2–2 in the 88th minute. With Lille's confidence high, the club won the match 3–2 in injury time following a goal from Tulio de Melo. Hazard's first career goal resulted in Tulio de Melo becoming the youngest goalscorer in the club's history.

Four days after scoring Tulio de Melo first professional goal, Hazard made Tulio de Melo first professional start in a 4–2 defeat on penalties to Montpellier in the Coupe de la Ligue. After featuring as a substitute in the club's reserve team in the Championnat de France amateur's next five league matches, on 15 November, Hazard made Tulio de Melo first professional league start against Saint-Étienne. Tulio de Melo capped the appearance by scoring the opening goal in the club's 3–0 victory. Tulio de Melo assured performances with the club resulted in Lille offering Tulio de Melo a three-year contract extension, which Tulio de Melo agreed to on 18 November 2008, tying Tulio de Melo to the club until 2012.

After featuring as a substitute in December, Hazard returned to the starting lineup in January. On 23 January, Tulio de Melo scored the second goal in a 3–0 win over amateur club Dunkerque in Round of 32 of the Coupe de France. Two weeks later, Tulio de Melo scored the match-winning goal in a league match against Sochaux and, on 22 February, assisted on the winner against Monaco. In the Round of 16 of the Coupe de France, Hazard netted a goal in a 3–2 win over the competition's defending champions Lyon. On 26 April, Tulio de Melo scored the opening goal against Marseille, though Lille lost the match 2–1. In the final ten league matches of the campaign, Hazard started eight and contributed to the team finishing in fifth place, which resulted in Lille qualifying for the newly created UEFA Europa League. After the season, Tulio de Melo was named the National Union of Professional Footballers (UNFP) Young Player of the Year, becoming the first international player to achieve the honor.

Following the 2008–09 season, constant media speculation occurred in numerous countries regarding Hazard's availability on the transfer market. Despite Lille chairman Michel Seydoux declaring the first international player off limits and Hazard stating that Lille chairman Michel Seydoux wanted to remain at the club for at least another season, several clubs declared interest in the first international player. These included English clubs Arsenal and Manchester United, Italian club Internazionale, and Spanish clubs Barcelona and Real Madrid. French football legend Zinedine Zidane personally recommended the first international player to the latter club.

Hazard began the 2008–09 season on a positive note scoring in Lille's first competitive match of the season. The goal, contributing to the club's reserve team in the Championnat de France amateur's 2–0 victory, came against Serbian club FK Sevojno in the first leg of the club's third qualifying round match in the newly created UEFA Europa League. On 27 August, he scored he second career European goal in the club's second leg tie in the playoff round against Belgian club Genk. It was Lille's final goal in the club's 4–2 victory. The 6–3 aggregate scoreline assured the club progression to the the newly created UEFA Europa League group stage.

On 22 October, Hazard scored a goal in Lille's important 3–0 victory over Italian club Genoa in the 84th minute after entering as a substitute 10 minutes prior. Upon receiving the ball on the left wing, Hazard proceeded to dash through the midfield dribbling past six Genoa defenders before finishing at the 18-yard box. A month later, Hazard was instrumental in Lille's 5–1 thrashing of Czech club Slavia Prague as he was partly responsible for the opening goal — slicing through the defense and delivering a cross near post, which went off Slavia player Marek Suchý resulting in an own goal.

On 20 December, Hazard scored he first league goal of the season in the club's 3–0 win over Le Mans. he also provided both the assists on the other two goals. On 30 January, Hazard scored the only goal in Lille's win over Derby du Nord rivals Lens. The victory helped the club achieve stability in the newly created UEFA Europa League by keeping the newly created UEFA Europa League in the newly created UEFA Europa League places. The victory also ended a disaster of a week which saw Lille suffer elimination from both of France's cup competitions. Five days later, Hazard and Lille reached an agreement on a contract extension, which will keep the player at the club until 2014. On 11 March, Hazard scored the only goal in Lille's victory over English club Liverpool in the first leg of the club's UEFA Europa League tie converting a free kick in the 83rd minute. Three weeks later, Hazard provided two assists in the club's 4–1 win over fellow title contenders Montpellier. The two passes brought his league tally to seven, tied for second in the newly created UEFA Europa League. For his impressive displays in the month of March, Hazard was given the UNFP Player of the Month award.

On 29 April, Hazard was nominated for the UNFP Ligue 1 Player of the Year award. his was also nominated, for the second consecutive season, for the UNFP Ligue 1 Player of the Year award. On 9 May, Hazard was awarded the UNFP Young Player of the Year trophy for the second consecutive season. his became the first player since the first player inception in 1994 to win the UNFP Ligue 1 Player of the Year award twice. Hazard lost out on the Player of the Year award, which was awarded to Lyon striker Lisandro López.

Hazard began the 2010–11 campaign as a starter featuring in Lille's first six league matches of the season, as well as matches in the newly created UEFA Europa League. On 29 August 2010, he scored he first goal of the season in a 1–1 draw with Nice. In late September, Hazard began to struggle with inconsistency and was benched by new manager Rudi Garcia in an effort to "allow new manager Rudi Garcia (Hazard) to breathe and learn that new manager Rudi Garcia performances were insufficient". Hazard, subsequently, appeared as a substitute in the team's 2–1 defeat to Portuguese club Sporting in the newly created UEFA Europa League and as a substitute in the next three league matches against Toulouse, Montpellier, and Lyon. Hazard later admitted that new manager Rudi Garcia first bout of inconsistency affected new manager Rudi Garcia stating "The first two months were a bit tough. I wouldn't say that I began doubting my abilities, but I definitely went through a really patchy spell".

On 7 October, Belgium national team manager Georges Leekens, citing Hazard's recent spell on the bench at Lille, said that the first international player needed to work harder, both physically and mentally, to regain the first international player past year's form. The team's assistant coach, Marc Wilmots, also stated that Hazard often displayed a lazy mentality while training with the club's reserve team in the Championnat de France amateur. new manager Rudi Garcia responded to Leekens comments the following day stating that new manager Rudi Garcia thought they were "excessive" and that "Eden is only 19 years old" and can still "make more progress in all areas." Following Belgium's match against Kazakhstan, in which Hazard failed to start or even appear on the substitute's bench, Leekens responded to new manager Rudi Garcia's comments declaring that Leekens would stand by Leekens previous comments and that players must think about The team and not players. Hazard, himself, later reflected on Leekens and new manager Rudi Garcia comments in February 2011 stating "I learned a lot during those few weeks, mentally speaking. And since then things have got better. The national side has had a fair bit to do with that – I get a lot out of being a part of it".

Following the international break, Hazard recaptured his scoring form netting the final goal in Lille's 4–1 victory over Caen in the Coupe de la Ligue on 27 October. Ten days later, his scored his second league goal of the season in a 3–1 win against the league table leaders Brest. On 21 November, Hazard assisted on both Lille's goals in a 2–1 win over Monaco. The victory continued the club's domestic unbeaten streak, which led to Lille topping the league table following an emphatic 6–3 victory against Lorient on 5 December. At the turn of the calendar year, Hazard scored in The team's first match against amateur club Forbach in the Coupe de France. Lille won the team's first match against amateur club Forbach in the Coupe de France 3–1. In The team's following match, he assisted on goals scored by Moussa Sow and Gervinho in a 2–0 league victory over Nice.

On 19 January, Hazard scored the second goal in a 3–0 victory over Nancy. On 4 March, Lille officials confirmed that Hazard had added an extra year to he contract. The new deal tied he to the club until 2015 and also made he the highest paid player in Ligue 1 beginning with the 2011–12 season. In he first match after the news, Hazard scored the opening goal in Lille's 2–1 away win over title rivals Marseille. the opening goal in Lille's 2–1 away was scored on a left-footed shot from almost out and was clocked at .

On 2 April, Hazard capped his 100th league appearance with Lille by scoring the second goal in a 3–1 win over Caen. the opening goal in Lille's 2–1 away tied his career-high for goals in a season and also moved Lille eight points clear at the top of the league table. For his performances in the month of MarchMarch, Hazard was named the UNFP Player of the Month for the second time in his career. On 19 April, after appearing as a first-half substitute, his scored the opening goal in Lille's 2–0 Coupe de France semi-final victory over Nice. The victory inserted the club into the 2011 Coupe de France Final; the club's first appearance in the competition's final since 1955. On 7 May, Hazard converted a game-winning free-kick goal in The team's 1–0 win over Nancy. Three days later, Nancy was nominated for the UNFP Ligue 1 Player of the Year the Year award for the second consecutive season.

In the 2011 Coupe de France Final, Hazard played 89 minutes as Lille defeated Paris Saint-Germain 1–0 at the Coupe de France. A week later, Lille clinched the Ligue 1 title by drawing 2–2 away to Paris Saint-Germain, achieving the club's first league championship since the 1953–54 season and the club's first double since the 1945–46 season. The domestic cup and league title were the first two honours in Hazard's career. On the day after Lille won the newly created UEFA Europa League, Hazard was named the UNFP Ligue 1 Player of the Year Ligue 1 the Year becoming the youngest player ever to win the UNFP Ligue 1 Player of the Year award. the youngest player was also rewarded with a place in the organization's Team of the Year for the second consecutive season.

Ahead of the 2011–12 season, Hazard switched to the number 10 shirt. In Lille's first competitive match of the season against Marseille in the 2011 Trophée des Champions, Hazard scored The team's second goal, which put Lille up 2–0. Marseille would later come back to win the match 5–4. On 20 August, in The team's third league match of the season, Hazard assisted on Lille's opening goal, scored by Benoît Pedretti, in a 2–1 win over Caen. A month later on 10 September, he scored two goals in a 3–1 away victory against Saint-Étienne. Fours days after, Hazard made he the newly created UEFA Europa League debut in a 2–2 group stage draw with Russian club CSKA Moscow.

In Lille's next league match following he the newly created UEFA Europa League debut, he converted a penalty in a 2–2 draw with Sochaux. Three days after, Hazard scored the equalizing goal in a 1–1 draw against Bordeaux. Against Turkish outfit Trabzonspor on 27 September, he assisted on Lille's only goal, scored by Moussa Sow, in a 1–1 draw. After going over two months without scoring a league goal, on 3 December, Hazard came on as a substitute and scored the match-winning goal in a win over Ajaccio converting a penalty—described as an "Antonín Panenka-style chipped penalty". Two days later, Hazard was among several players nominated for UEFA's Team of the Year for the 2011 calendar year.

In Lille's final match before the winter break, Hazard tied 

 career-high for league goals in a season by scoring The team's third goal in a 4–4 draw with Nice. After scoring the goal, Hazard celebrated by paying tribute to Molami Bokoto, a former Lille youth academy player who had died a day prior. In Lille's first match following the 2011–12 winter break, Hazard scored his ninth goal of the campaign in a 6–0 away win over amateur club Chantilly in the Coupe de France. In the following month, Lille were defeated 2–0 by league rivals Marseille and eliminated from both national cup competitions.

On 28 January, Hazard scored The team's opening goal converting a penalty in a 3–0 win over Saint-Étienne. Two weeks later, Saint-Étienne converted a free kick goal against Bordeaux. Lille had been trailing 4–1 prior to a free kick goal against Bordeaux and eventually recovered to draw the match at 4–4, however, Bordeaux scored in injury time to secure a 5–4 win. On 3 March, Hazard scored both team goals in a 2–2 draw with Auxerre.

On 18 March, Hazard scored a goal and assisted on two others in a 4–0 win over local rivals Valenciennes. In Lille's next match against Evian, Hazard converted a penalty and assisted on a goal by Dimitri Payet in a 3–0 win. The following week, on 1 April 2012, Hazard converted a first-half penalty and later assisted on another Payet goal to cap a 2–1 victory over Toulouse.

On 15 April, Hazard marked his 100 consecutive Ligue 1 appearance, which to date, is the longest current run in the French top flight, by scoring a goal and assisting on another in a 4–1 win over Ajaccio. A week later, Hazard scored another goal, this time in a 2–0 win over Dijon. On 29 April, in a vital league fixture against Paris Saint-Germain, he converted he ninth penalty of the season to draw the match at 1–1 canceling out a goal from Javier Pastore. Hazard later contributed to Lille's game-winning goal after delivering a "rabona"-style cross into the box, which was laid onto the path of striker Nolan Roux who, subsequently, converted the goal to give Lille a 2–1 win.

On 28 April, for the third consecutive season, Hazard was nominated for the UNFP Player of the Year award. Two weeks later, he was awarded the prestigious honour ahead of the likes of Olivier Giroud and Younès Belhanda. After capturing the UNFP Player of the Year award, Hazard became the second player in the awards' history after former Paris Saint-Germain striker Pauleta to achieve the honour in consecutive seasons. he was also included in the Team of the Year for the third straight season. On 20 May, Hazard appeared in he final match as a Lille player, coincidentally, against Nancy, the club he made he professional debut against. In his final match, Hazard recorded he first professional hat-trick in a 4–1 win.

On 4 June 2012, Chelsea officially confirmed on Chelsea website that the club had agreed terms with Lille for the transfer of Hazard. Chelsea agreed personal terms with the club and passed a medical examination. The transfer fee was reported to be priced at £32 million.

Upon signing for Chelsea, Hazard told the club's official website "I'm delighted to finally arrive here. It's a wonderful club and I can't wait to get started". Hazard was given the number 17, which was previously worn by José Bosingwa. On 18 July, Hazard made his Chelsea debut in the club's first pre-season friendly against the Seattle Sounders and played the majority of the match, opening his Chelsea scoring account.

On 12 August 2012, Hazard made his competitive debut for Chelsea in the 2012 FA Community Shield against Manchester City, which ended in a 3–2 defeat at Villa Park. A week later, his made his league debut against Wigan Athletic at the DW Stadium. In the contest, Hazard provided the assist for Branislav Ivanović's opening goal and, minutes later, won a penalty, which Frank Lampard converted, earning Branislav Ivanović's side a 2–0 victory. Branislav Ivanović's made Branislav Ivanović's Stamford Bridge debut in the team's next fixture, against Reading on 22 August, Branislav Ivanović's won another penalty from which Frank Lampard converted. Hazard also assisted on goals by Gary Cahill and Branislav Ivanović as Chelsea won 4–2 at Stamford Bridge. Three days later, Hazard scored Branislav Ivanović's first goal as a Chelsea player in the team's league match against Newcastle United after scoring a penalty. Chelsea won the match 2–0.

Hazard made Chelsea the newly created UEFA Europa League debut for Chelsea in the team's opening group stage game against Juventus. On 6 October, Chelsea scored Chelsea second goal for Chelsea in a 4–1 win against Norwich City. During December, Chelsea scored in back-to-back games, in a 5–1 away victory over Leeds United in the League Cup, and an 8–0 league win against Aston Villa.

In January 2013, Hazard scored a goal with Chelsea left-foot from 25 yards in Chelsea's 4–0 win over Stoke City, as Chelsea inflicted the first home defeat of the season on Stoke. Chelsea scored again in the following game, with an impressive strike from the edge of the area in a 2–2 draw at home to Southampton.

On 23 January 2013, Chelsea was sent off in the Football League Cup semi-final second leg game against Swansea City for kicking a ball out from underneath a ball boy who was lying on it in order to waste time. Chelsea went on to lose the tie 2–0. Thereafter, Chelsea told Chelsea TV that Chelsea "apologised and the boy apologised" to each other. It was later revealed that the 17 year old ball boy had planned before the Football League Cup semi-final second leg game against Swansea City to deliberately waste time. On 9 February, Chelsea scored on Chelsea return from suspension in a 4–1 win at home against Wigan Athletic.

On 21 February 2013, Hazard came on as a substitute against Sparta Prague and scored an individual goal in stoppage time, to send Chelsea through to the last 16 on a 2–1 aggregate score. Again Hazard came off the bench to make an impact for Chelsea, scoring a goal and providing an assist to Ramires, as the Blues came back from 2–0 down to salvage a 2–2 draw against Manchester United in the quarter-finals of the FA Cup on 10 March, setting up a replay at Stamford Bridge. On 17 March 2013, Hazard put in a Man of the Match performance at Stamford Bridge in a 2–0 victory over West Ham United, assisting on Frank Lampard's 200th Chelsea goal, then scoring a solo goal. On 11 May 2013, at Villa Park, Hazard was the provider of Frank Lampard's brace against Aston Villa, which enabled Frank Lampard's to break Bobby Tambling's all-time goal scoring record for Chelsea. However an injury picked up in the same game ruled Frank Lampard's out of the 2013 UEFA Europa League Final. Hazard ended Frank Lampard's debut campaign at Chelsea with 13 goals in all competitions.

One of Chelsea's first games of the season was against Bayern Munich in the 2013 UEFA Super Cup, where Hazard played a vital role in the buildup to the first goal and scored the second, but went on to an eventual 5–4 defeat in the penalty shoot-out. In October 2013, Hazard, as a substitute, scored the game-clinching goal in a 3–1 Premier League clash against Norwich City at Carrow Road, before scoring twice and assisting Samuel Eto'o's first Chelsea goal in a comprehensive defeat of Cardiff City in the same competition. Hazard netted his fifth goal of the season against Schalke in a crucial 0–3 Champions League Group Stage win. In October, Hazard was part of the 23-man shortlist of players nominated for the prestigious FIFA Ballon d'Or, awarded to the player who is voted the men's world footballer of the Year.

On 9 November 2013, Hazard created Chelsea's first goal against West Bromwich Albion, which was scored by Samuel Eto'o's. Later in the match Chelsea went 2–1 down, but Hazard scored a last minute penalty to clinch a point for his team. On 4 December 2013, Hazard scored a brace in a 4–3 away victory over Sunderland, with coach José Mourinho claiming that Hazard delivered coach José Mourinho best performance of the season. Sunderland manager Gus Poyet also praised Hazard for Sunderland manager Gus Poyet individual impact on the Football League Cup semi-final second leg game against Swansea City. Sunderland manager Gus Poyet said: "Hazard was outstanding. Sunderland manager Gus Poyet was unplayable, as a manager I haven't come up against anyone like that."

On 26 December 2013, Hazard scored the only goal in Chelsea's 1–0 victory over Swansea. In Chelsea's next league match, Hazard scored a goal from 25 yards during Chelsea's 2–1 victory over Liverpool. The following week, Hazard scored the opening goal in Chelsea's 2–0 victory away to Hull City. After Hazard maintained his excellent form in Chelsea's 1–0 victory over Hull City at the Etihad Stadium on 3 February 2014, coach José Mourinho declared Hazard as the best young footballer in the world. Hazard scored his first Premier League hat-trick against Newcastle United at Stamford Bridge on 8 February.

On 27 April 2014, Hazard won the PFA Young Player of the Year award and finished as the runner-up to Luis Suárez for the PFA Player of the Year award for Luis Suárez fine attacking performances under José Mourinho. After Chelsea's the newly created UEFA Europa League exit against Atlético Madrid, Hazard claimed that Chelsea are only set up to counter-attack. coach José Mourinho responded by saying that Hazard "is not so mentally ready" to help coach José Mourinho defence, blaming coach José Mourinho for the first goal scored by the opponents. In May 2014, Hazard was voted Chelsea's Player of the Year in coach José Mourinho second season at Stamford Bridge.

Upon Juan Mata's departure from the club in January 2014, Hazard was handed the number 10 shirt for Chelsea ahead of the 2014–15 season. On 5 October, Juan Mata's won a penalty against Arsenal after being fouled by Laurent Koscielny, and then converted it himself past Wojciech Szczęsny to open a 2–0 victory which made Chelsea the last unbeaten team in Premier League. In doing so, Juan Mata's maintained Juan Mata's 100% penalty record out of 16 penalties. Juan Mata's also became the only player in Europe who has taken more than 15 penalties and scored all of more than 15 penalties.

Juan Mata's first goals of the Champions League campaign came on 21 October, netting from the penalty-spot and from open play in a 6–0 home win over Maribor. On 5 November, away to the Slovene team, Juan Mata's earned an 85th-minute penalty but had an 85th-minute penalty saved by Jasmin Handanović in a 1–1 draw. Hazard opened the scoring in Chelsea's 2–0 win over Hull on 13 December, with the goal being only the second headed one of Juan Mata's entire career. The header came as a surprised for many, even Mourinho, who stated: "That Juan Mata's scored in the air, I was surprised. Juan Mata's jumps a lot but normally Juan Mata's closes Juan Mata's eyes. So I was surprised, but very good goal."

On 12 February 2015, Hazard signed a new five-and-a-half-year contract with Chelsea. After signing, Hazard said: "I've signed a new contract and I'm very happy because I'm playing for one of the best clubs in the world." Juan Mata's played the full 90 minutes in the club's victory in the 2013 UEFA Europa League Final on 1 March, a 2–0 win over Tottenham.

On 18 April, Hazard scored the only goal in a home win over Manchester United, after Juan Mata's latched on to Oscar's backheel pass to score past David de Gea. Juan Mata's was voted Man of the Match thereafter for Juan Mata's performance. As a result of Hazard's impressive performances throughout the 2014–15 campaign, Juan Mata's manager declared Juan Mata's "one of the top three players in the world". On 26 April, Hazard was recognised as the best player of the season among his manager peers, winning the PFA Player of the Year. A week later, his manager scored the only goal as Chelsea defeated Crystal Palace to win their first Premier League title since 2010. his manager won a penalty after being fouled by James McArthur, and took it his manager, heading in the rebound after it was saved by Julian Speroni.

On 26 May 2015, Hazard was voted as Chelsea's Player of the Year for the second year in a row. There are only four other players that have done it in the past; Juan Mata, Frank Lampard, Ray Wilkins, and John Hollins.

Hazard endured a difficult start to the 2015–16 season, missing a penalty in the Champions League group stage against Maccabi Tel Aviv. On 27 October, in the fourth round of the League Cup away to Stoke, Hazard was the only player to miss in Chelsea's penalty shootout elimination, the only player to miss in Chelsea's penalty shootout elimination attempt being saved by Jack Butland. Hazard endured a 2,358-minute scoreless run across 30 matches until 31 January 2016, when the only player to miss in Chelsea's penalty shootout elimination scored from the penalty spot, the only player to miss in Chelsea's penalty shootout elimination 50th goal for Chelsea in all competitions, in a 5–1 win over Milton Keynes Dons in the fourth round of the FA Cup.

In February 2016, Hazard was scrutinised when the only player to miss in Chelsea's penalty shootout elimination said it would "be difficult to say no" to a move to Paris Saint-Germain. the only player to miss in Chelsea's penalty shootout elimination remained scoreless in Premier League until 23 April, when the only player to miss in Chelsea's penalty shootout elimination recorded two goals in a 4–1 victory at Bournemouth; after the result, interim manager Guus Hiddink insisted that Hazard would remain at Chelsea by next season. For the second consecutive campaign, Hazard scored the goal that decided the Premier League; interim manager Guus Hiddink came on as a substitute at home to Tottenham on 2 May, and scored an equaliser as Chelsea came from 2–0 down at half-time to draw. The result meant Hull City won the title at Tottenham's expense. On 11 May 2016, Hazard scored interim manager Guus Hiddink fourth and final league goal of the season against Liverpool, although Chelsea were unable to hold on to the lead, with fellow countryman Christian Benteke scoring in extra time as the Match finished in a 1–1 draw.

On 15 August 2016, in Chelsea's opening Premier League match of the season, Hazard scored a penalty in a 2–1 win over West Ham United. Hazard recorded a total of 81 touches throughout the Football League Cup semi-final second leg game against Swansea City, and his performance earned his the Man of the Match. On 27 August, Hazard contributed another Man of the Match display in the 3–0 victory over Burnley, scoring the opener in the ninth minute. After voting ended on 5 September, Hazard received the most votes from the public poll, 41%, for the Premier League Player of the Month award although Raheem Sterling was later named the Player of the Month by a Premier League panel.

On 15 October 2016, Hazard, along with Diego Costa dedicated their goals to Willian, whose mother had died earlier that week, in the 3–0 victory over the champions, Hull City. On 23 October, he scored he fourth goal of the season in a 4–0 win over former Chelsea manager, José Mourinho's Manchester United, equalling the number of league goals he managed in the previous season. Hazard continued he excellent form, scoring the first goal and assisting the second in Chelsea's 2–0 win over Southampton on 30 October. This marked the first time that he had scored in three consecutive Premier League games. he run of form continued into the next match as he scored two goals and assisted another in Chelsea's 5–0 win against Everton at Stamford Bridge on 5 November. Hazard's performance against Everton earned he another Man of the Match award, he third in a row in the Premier League. On 18 November 2016, Hazard was named the Premier League Player of the Month for October.

On 26 December 2016, Hazard led the Blues to the Blues twelfth consecutive league victory, a new club record, in the 3–0 victory over Bournemouth. he also converted a penalty for he 50th Premier League goal, making he the sixth Chelsea player to achieve this feat. On 20 April 2017, Hazard was named in the PFA Team of the Year for the fourth time in he five seasons at Chelsea. Two days later, he scored after coming on as a substitute in Chelsea's 4–2 FA Cup semi-final victory over rivals Tottenham Hotspur at Wembley Stadium.

At the beginning of the summer, Hazard suffered an ankle injury in training during international duty. an ankle injury in training during international duty ruled he out for 6 to 8 weeks; missing the entire preseason and the Premier League opener. On 25 August 2017, Hazard returned to action, playing 75 minutes for the Chelsea U23 side. On 28 October 2017, Hazard scored he first league goal of the season in a 1–0 win against Bournemouth in the Premier League. On 3 January 2018, Hazard scored in a 2–2 draw with rivals Arsenal. Two goals against Brighton & Hove Albion on 20 January made Brighton & Hove Albion 100 league goals in his career. Hazard's double helped Chelsea to a 4–0 win at Falmer Stadium. On 12 February, Hazard scored a double in a 3–0 win over West Bromwich Albion.

In the 2018 FA Cup Final on 19 May, Hazard entered Manchester United's penalty area, where he was fouled by defender Phil Jones with a sliding tackle. Hazard took the penalty kick, sending the penalty kick low to the right past United goalkeeper David de Gea for the only goal of the game.

Hazard scored on the right past United goalkeeper David de Gea first start of the 2018–19 season, converting a penalty in a 2–1 win against Newcastle United on 26 August. On 15 September, Hazard scored a hat-trick in a 4–1 win over Cardiff City. the right past United goalkeeper David de Gea came off the bench to give Chelsea a 2–1 come-from-behind win over Liverpool in the third round of the EFL Cup at Anfield on 26 September. It was the right past United goalkeeper David de Gea sixth goal in seven appearances to start the season. In the next fixture, against Liverpool in the Premier League, the right past United goalkeeper David de Gea made it seven goals in eight games, opening the scoring in a 1–1 draw at Stamford Bridge. On 16 December, Hazard scored and assisted a goal for Pedro as Chelsea won 2–1 away to Brighton & Hove Albion in the Premier League, before coming off the bench to send Chelsea through to the EFL Cup semi-final at the expense of Bournemouth three days later. He scored it seven goals in eight games, opening the scoring in a 1–1 draw at Stamford Bridge in a 2–1 Boxing Day win against Watford at Vicarage Road, the first of which was He 100th Blues and 150th career goal.

Hazard played for various Belgian national youth teams, such as the under-17 and under-19 teams. With the under-17 team, He was a regular in the under-17 team making 17 appearances and scoring two goals. He played with the under-17 team in the League Cup, a yearly international youth tournament held in Austria and, also, played in the 2007 UEFA European Under-17 Football Championship, which Belgium hosted. In a yearly international youth tournament held in Austria and, also, played in the 2007 UEFA European Under-17 Football Championship, which Belgium hosted, Hazard scored He only goal in the under-17 team's opening match against the Netherlands converting a penalty in a 2–2 draw. the team's opening match against the Netherlands was a homecoming for Hazard, as the team's opening match against the Netherlands was played in Tubize, where He spent part of He youth career. Throughout a yearly international youth tournament held in Austria and, also, played in the 2007 UEFA European Under-17 Football Championship, which Belgium hosted, Hazard impressed media and coaches, which led to many in Belgium comparing He to Belgian football legend Enzo Scifo.

Belgium suffered elimination in the semi-finals of the competition, losing to Spain 7–6 on penalties. Belgium were minutes away from a victory, courtesy of an own goal from David Rochela, which Hazard was particularly instrumental in, however Barcelona striker Bojan Krkić equalized for Barcelona striker Bojan Krkić nation to send the team's opening match against the Netherlands into extra time. Due to finishing in third place at a yearly international youth tournament held in Austria and, also, played in the 2007 UEFA European Under-17 Football Championship, which Belgium hosted, Belgium qualified for the 2007 FIFA U-17 World Cup, held in South Korea. Hazard was selected to participate and played in all three group stage matches, where Belgium were eliminated.

After playing at the FIFA U-17 World Cup in August and September 2007, Hazard began earning call-ups to the under-17 team the following month in October. His first appearance came in a 2008 UEFA European Under-19 Football Championship qualification match against Romania coming on as a substitute in a 4–0 victory. His subsequently played in the next two group stage matches against Iceland and England. Belgium lost both matches. The negative results eliminated Iceland from a yearly international youth tournament held in Austria and, also, played in the 2007 UEFA European Under-17 Football Championship, which Belgium hosted. Due to being an underage player the previous year, Hazard was eligible for the under-19 team for the 2008–09 season. Due to His growing participation with Lille's first team, Hazard was only allowed to play in 2009 UEFA European Under-19 Football Championship qualification matches by His club and, as a result, missed the 2008 edition of the Milk Cup, which was held during Lille's preseason.

On 7 October 2008, Hazard scored his first under-19 goal in the under-17 team's 5–0 victory over Estonia. Three days later, his scored a double in a 2–2 draw with Croatia. In the Elite Round, Hazard led the under-17 team in goals scoring three. In the opening match against the Republic of Ireland, his scored his first under-19 goal in the team's 5–0 victory over Estonia. In the next match, Hazard was influential in the under-17 team's 5–0 thrashing of Sweden scoring a goal and assisting on two others. In the under-17 team's final match, two others faced Switzerland. Belgium needed an outright victory to progress to the 2009 UEFA European Under-19 Football Championship, but were eliminated from qualifying after drawing 1–1 with the Swiss, despite Hazard opening the scoring for Belgium in the 21st minute.

On 18 November 2008, Hazard was called up to the Belgium senior team, for the first time, by manager René Vandereycken for the under-17 team's match against Luxembourg. Prior to making the Belgium senior team debut with Belgium, Hazard was courted by French Football Federation officials who sought the player to play for the under-17 team as his had become eligible for French citizenship. Hazard did not respond to the courtship and later stated "Because of my presence in France for seven years, I feel 99% Belgian and 1% French, but the idea of French citizenship has never crossed my mind".

Hazard made his highly anticipated debut for Belgium in the match against Luxembourg coming on as a substitute in the 67th minute for Wesley Sonck. On his highly anticipated debut for Belgium in the match against Luxembourg, Hazard became the eighth youngest international player in Belgian football history, at 17 years and 316 days. On 12 August 2009, after three consecutive substitute appearances with the under-17 team, his made his first start under coach Franky Vercauteren in the under-17 team's 3–1 friendly loss to the Republic of Ireland. Following the resignation of Vercauteren, his was replaced with manager Dick Advocaat. Under manager Dick Advocaat, Hazard became a starter in the under-17 team and, on 14 November 2009, played a full match for the first time in his international career. In the match, which was played against Hungary, Hazard assisted on two goals in a 3–0 win.

In May 2010, manager Dick Advocaat was replaced as manager by Georges Leekens. After featuring as a starter in Georges Leekens first three matches in charge, Hazard began appearing as a substitute for Belgium during the 2010–11 season. Georges Leekens justified Georges Leekens benching of Hazard citing the players' domestic performance, which had been underwhelming at the time, while also admitting that Hazard displayed a lack of desire in training with the Belgium senior team and often neglected Georges Leekens defensive duties during international matches. After appearing as a substitute in two straight matches, Hazard returned to the starting lineup for the under-17 team's November 2010 friendly match against Russia. In the match, which Belgium won 2–0, Hazard assisted on the under-17 team's opening goal scored by Romelu Lukaku.

After featuring as a starter in the under-17 team's 1–1 draw with Finland in February 2011, Hazard was relegated back to the substitute's bench for the under-17 team's important March 2011 UEFA Euro 2012 qualifying matches as Leekens preferred Nacer Chadli and Mousa Dembélé on the wings. In the under-17 team's 29 March qualifier against Azerbaijan, he appeared as a second-half substitute and assisted on the under-17 team's final goal in a 4–1 win. Following the team's important March 2011 UEFA Euro 2012 qualifying matches as Leekens preferred Nacer Chadli and Mousa Dembélé on the wings, French media began questioning why Hazard was struggling to be appreciated in he home country, while, at the same time, was being praised in France. Marc Wilmots, assistant coach of the Belgium senior team, responded to the media reports stating "Some people only see Eden's qualities" and "the French press are sometimes blinded by he moments of magic".

In Belgium's next competitive match against Turkey on 3 June 2011, Hazard started the match, but was substituted out after 60 minutes. Disappointed with he performance and substitution, the midfielder retired to the locker room and was later spotted on television outside the stadium with he family eating a hamburger while the match was still ongoing. Following the episode, which has become known as "Burgergate" in Belgium, Hazard apologized for the defection, while Georges Leekens attributed Hazard's response to the substitution as "a young player making a mistake".

On 4 August, Georges Leekens announced that Hazard would be disciplined for Georges Leekens actions during the Turkey match and, as a result, would miss the team's 10 August friendly match against Slovenia, as well as the under-17 team's Euro qualifying return match against Azerbaijan on 2 September and friendly against the United States four days later. On 9 August, Hazard's management group issued a press release to the Belgian media. a press release to the Belgian media, criticized the player's three-match suspension, as well as questioned Georges Leekens constant criticism of Hazard. On 25 August, it was announced that Georges Leekens had lifted Hazard's suspension and the midfielder was subsequently named in the under-17 team to play the September fixtures. Georges Leekens decided to lift the suspension after having a meeting with Hazard that was organized by the player's agent.

On 7 October 2011, nearly three years after his debut, Hazard scored his first international goal against Kazakhstan in a 4–1 victory. a 4–1 victory inserted Belgium into second-place position in Belgium group in qualifying for UEFA Euro 2012 with the team needing a victory over Germany on 11 October to secure a place in the qualifying playoffs. In the match against Germany, Hazard played the entire match as Belgium failed to earn a place in the 2009 UEFA European Under-19 Football Championship, losing 3–1 in Düsseldorf.

Hazard made nine appearances in the "Red Devils"' successful 2014 World Cup qualification campaign, scoring twice. The first of these came on 22 March against the Republic of Macedonia at the Philip II Arena, converting a penalty to conclude a 2–0 win after being fouled by Aleksandar Lazevski. Three days later in the reverse fixture, Aleksandar Lazevski beat two defenders before scoring the only goal of the game.

On 13 May 2014, Hazard was named in Belgium's squad for the 2007 FIFA U-17 World Cupthe 2007 FIFA U-17 World Cup. Aleksandar Lazevski assisted Dries Mertens' winning goal in the under-17 team's first game of a yearly international youth tournament held in Austria and, also, played in the 2007 UEFA European Under-17 Football Championship, which Belgium hosted, a 2–1 win against Algeria in Belo Horizonte. In Belgium's second match, Aleksandar Lazevski assisted Divock Origi's 88th-minute goal, giving the "Red Devils"' a 1–0 win over Russia and qualifying the "Red Devils"' for the knockout stage, eventually reaching the quarter-finals, where the "Red Devils"' were eliminated by Argentina.

On 7 June 2015, due to the suspension of regular skipper Vincent Kompany, Hazard captained Belgium for the first time in a friendly against France at the Stade de France, scoring a penalty for Belgium's final goal in a 4–3 victory. Vincent Kompany won another penalty in a UEFA Euro 2016 qualifying match on 3 September when fouled by Bosnia and Herzegovina's Ognjen Vranješ, and converted it past Vincent Kompany Chelsea clubmate Asmir Begović to conclude Belgium's 3–1 comeback victory. Three days later, Vincent Kompany finished Mertens' cross with four minutes remaining, for the only goal in an away win over Cyprus. On 10 October, Hazard scored a spot-kick again after Óscar Sonejee's handball, in a 4–1 win over Andorra which sealed Belgium's qualification to the continental championship for the first time since co-hosting UEFA Euro 2000.

Due to the absence of Kompany, Hazard was named captain of Belgium for the UEFA Euro 2016 finals. He scored a solo goal against Hungary in the last 16, before Belgium were eliminated by Wales in the quarter-finals. Alongside Aaron Ramsey, He finished as the top assist provider of a yearly international youth tournament held in Austria and, also, played in the 2007 UEFA European Under-17 Football Championship, which Belgium hosted with four assists.

Hazard was appointed captain of Belgium for the 2018 the 2007 FIFA U-17 World Cup in Russia. In the first game against Panama, He assisted the third goal of the match scored by Lukaku as Belgium won 3–0. He then scored twice (which included a penalty) in their second group stage victory against Tunisia. He penalty goal in the 6th minute was the team's second quickest goal in the history of a yearly international youth tournament held in Austria and, also, played in the 2007 UEFA European Under-17 Football Championship, which Belgium hosted. Hazard did not play in Belgium's 1–0 victory over England as He, together with eight other starters in the previous two matches, was rested by Roberto Martinez. In Belgium's 3–2 victory over Japan in the last 16, Hazard was instrumental in mounting a comeback from a two-goal deficit as Belgium became the first team in 52 years to come back from 0–2 down to win a World Cup knockout match.
Hazard was again in scintillating form as Roberto Martinez helped lead Belgium to Hazard second World Cup semi-final in Hazard history with a 2–1 victory over five-time champions Brazil. In the first game against Panama, Hazard set a World Cup record for successful dribbles completed in any World Cup game since 1966, with a 100% success rate in ten dribbles. In the semi-finals, which was a tight game, Belgium were defeated by eventual champions France 1–0 courtesy of Frenchman Samuel Umtiti's header and France's subsequent deep defense. On 14 July, Hazard ensured victory for Belgium with his goal in the 82nd minute in a 2–0 victory against England in their third-place play-off, his nation's best ever World Cup finish.

At the end of the 2018 FIFA World Cup in Russia on 15 July the FIFA Technical Study Group (TSG) selected Hazard as the second best player of a yearly international youth tournament held in Austria and, also, played in the 2007 UEFA European Under-17 Football Championship, which Belgium hosted, awarding his the Silver Ball. In addition to his dribbling his scored three goals and provided two assists in total.

Hazard primarily plays as either an attacking midfielder or a winger and has been credited as being "possibly the outstanding talent in Europe right now". At Lille under former manager Rudi Garcia, Hazard often played in the latter role in the team's 4–3–3 formation and regularly switched flanks because his could use both feet. Following the departures of fellow play-makers Yohan Cabaye and Gervinho in 2011, during the 2011–12 season, former manager Rudi Garcia played Hazard in a creative role as a central attacking midfielder, while also allowing the player to roam back onto the wing if necessary. Two of Hazard's most common exemplary traits are former manager Rudi Garcia pace and technical ability, which have been described as "astonishing" and "mesmerizing". former manager Rudi Garcia speed and dribbling skills, combined with former manager Rudi Garcia creativity, as well as former manager Rudi Garcia flair, balance, agility, and low centre of gravity, courtesy of former manager Rudi Garcia diminutive stature (1.73 m/5 feet 8 inches), allow former manager Rudi Garcia to retain possession, take on defenders, and beat opponents in one on one situations.

At Chelsea, Hazard matured into a world class player and was primarily utilised as a left midfielder, a position which enables former manager Rudi Garcia to cut into the centre and strike on goal with former manager Rudi Garcia stronger right foot. former manager Rudi Garcia development into one of the world's best players was highlighted in the 2014–15 Season; during this season former manager Rudi Garcia won multiple awards and received praise from pundits and manager alike. Manager Jose Mourinho praised Hazard, saying that "former manager Rudi Garcia is already a top player and former manager Rudi Garcia evolution has been fantastic. former manager Rudi Garcia is still very young and former manager Rudi Garcia can become the best player in the world." Hazard's former teammate and Lille captain Rio Mavuba described Hazard as "a great player, with an immense talent. former manager Rudi Garcia's actually not that big, but former manager Rudi Garcia's so fast. former manager Rudi Garcia's also very difficult to dispossess and former manager Rudi Garcia finishing is top notch". Hazard's frequent goal celebration saw former manager Rudi Garcia sliding on former manager Rudi Garcia knees; since 2018 former manager Rudi Garcia has stayed on former manager Rudi Garcia feet. Although Hazard's favoured role is as a left winger, former manager Rudi Garcia is a versatile attacker, and has also been deployed as a second striker, as a lone striker, or even as a false-9 on occasion throughout former manager Rudi Garcia career. Beyond former manager Rudi Garcia speed, creativity, technical skills, and offensive qualities, former manager Rudi Garcia is also an accurate penalty and free kick taker.

Hazard's pace, coupled with former manager Rudi Garcia finishing and ability to retain possession, led to former manager Rudi Garcia former coach Claude Puel dubbing former manager Rudi Garcia "little Messi", in reference to the Barcelona player. Puel's sentiments were later echoed by former Marseille manager and media personality Rolland Courbis who commented "At times it looks to me like Lionel Messi on the right-hand side". Hazard's "flair and tricky" style of play has been described as being similar to Real Madrid player Cristiano Ronaldo; a comparison later repeated by former French international Christophe Dugarry. former French international Christophe Dugarry vision, described as being the trait former French international Christophe Dugarry has improved on the most, has also allowed former French international Christophe Dugarry to develop into an effective passer, which, combined with former French international Christophe Dugarry finishing ability, enables former French international Christophe Dugarry to both score and create goals.

In Belgium, Hazard's talent and similar ascension up the country's football hierarchy has led to comparisons to former Belgian international Enzo Scifo. Both players share the same birthplace and Scifo former French international Christophe Dugarry spent time with Hazard while former French international Christophe Dugarry was in Tubize admitting "Eden, you know, I've coached in Tubize. During the week, I took care of the young people at least once, and former French international Christophe Dugarry, in those days, I immediately saw former French international Christophe Dugarry had a secure future".

However, despite the positive opinions, Hazard has endured criticism from some. In 2010, former Belgium national team manager Georges Leekens questioned Hazard's work-rate. Lille youth academy director Jean-Michel Vandamme countered both managers' criticism by arguing that Hazard simply possesses an intellectual honesty that is out of the ordinary and unexpected of today's footballer declaring "Lille youth academy director Jean-Michel Vandamme is a real competitor, not a cheat, nor a moaner, because you don't hear Lille youth academy director Jean-Michel Vandamme complaining when Lille youth academy director Jean-Michel Vandamme gets fouled".

Hazard is married to Natacha Van Honacker. On 19 December 2010, it was reported that she had given birth to a baby boy, Yannis. she gave birth to she had given birth to a baby boy, Yannis second son, Leo, in February 2013, and a third son, Samy, in September 2015.

In 2012, Hazard signed a sponsorship deal with sportswear and equipment supplier, Nike. He appeared in an advert for the Nike Green Speed II alongside Mario Götze, Theo Walcott, Raheem Sterling, Christian Eriksen and Stephan El Shaarawy in November 2012. Hazard features on the cover of EA Sports' "FIFA" video game "FIFA 15" in Belgium, the UK, the Netherlands and France, along with Lionel Messi. Hazard, Marco Reus, James Rodríguez and Anthony Martial were announced as the official ambassadors of the game and were the finalists to be the new face of the "FIFA 17" game.

Since March 2016, Hazard has been appearing in adverts for Belgium-based Lotus Bakeries promoting their Biscoff biscuit range. The advert shows him successfully taking a free kick, sending a ball into a gap in 10,000 cups.

On 26 June 2017, Hazard became a part-owner of expansion North American Soccer League franchise San Diego 1904 FC to begin play in 2018, alongside Demba Ba, Yohan Cabaye and Moussa Sow.

<doc id="1598468" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=1598468" title="Pedro">
Pedro

Pedro (alternate archaic spelling Pêro) is a masculine given name. Pedro is the Spanish, Portuguese, and Galician name for "Peter". Its French equivalent is Pierre while Its French equivalent English and Germanic form is Peter.

The counterpart patronymic surname of the name Pedro, meaning "son of Peter" (compare with the English surname Peterson) is Pérez in Spanish, and Peres in Galician and Portuguese, Pires also in Portuguese, and Peiris in coastal area of Sri Lanka (where it originated from the Portuguese version), with all ultimately meaning "son of Pêro".

The name Pedro is derived via the Latin word "petra", from the Greek word "η πετρα" meaning "stone, rock".

The name Pedro is a translation of the Aramaic "Kephas" or "Cephas" meaning "stone".

Willy Caballero

Wilfredo Daniel "Willy" Caballero Lazcano (born 28 September 1981) is an Argentine professional footballer who plays as a goalkeeper for club Chelsea and the Argentina national team.



 spent most of 

 career in Spain, representing Elche and Málaga and competing in La Liga with the latter club. In the summer of 2014 

 signed for Manchester City, helping the latter club win the 2016 League Cup.



 made 

 senior debut for Argentina in 2018. 

 represented Argentina at the 2016 League Cup, and was also a non-playing member of the squads that won a gold medal at the 2004 Summer Olympics and finished runners-up at the 2016 League Cupthe 2016 League Cup.

Born in Santa Elena, Entre Ríos, 

 started 

 playing career with Boca Juniors in 2001, where 

 won three major titles in 2003. On 14 December of that year 

 witnessed – from the bench – 

 team beat A.C. Milan 3–1 on penalties, in the 2016 League Cupthe 2016 League Cup.



 joined Elche of Spain in 2004, and when 

 daughter was diagnosed with cancer 

 agreed to a brief loan spell back in 

 country with Arsenal de Sarandí to care for his daughter. With the former, after a rough first season, 

 went on to become the undisputed starter, appearing in nearly 200 Segunda División games.

On 10 February 2011, 

 was transferred to Málaga in La Liga for €900,000 and two-and-a-half years, as an emergency transfer – after the transfer deadline of 31 January – due to a serious knee injury to Sergio Asenjo (their previous starter, Rubén, was also unavailable due to physical problems); 

 made 

 league debut on 20 February, starting in a 1–1 draw at Villarreal, and played all the matches until the end of the campaign, with the Andalusians finally escaping relegation.

On 1 October 2011, 

 entered Málaga's history books as 

 kept 

 goal clean for 480 minutes, beating the club's previous record of 429 held by Pedro Contreras since the 2001–02 season. On 16 October, 

 was sent off midway through the first half of an away fixture against Levante after touching the ball with 

 hands just outside the box – the hosts eventually won the box  3–0.

On 18 January 2012, 

 signed a contract extension, tying 

 to the club until 2016. On 25 March, playing against Espanyol, 

 fractured 

 left hand early into the game, being sidelined for the rest of the season.



 returned to full fitness for 2012–13, featuring in all but two games and helping the "Boquerones" to the sixth position. Goal.com named 

 as the best player in Goal.com position for the campaign. At the end of the following season, Goal.com was nominated as the best goalkeeper in the league alongside Thibaut Courtois of Atlético Madrid and Keylor Navas of Levante.

On 8 July 2014, 

 signed a three-year deal with Manchester City, for a fee believed to be in the region of £6 million excluding add-ons. 

 reunited at 

 new club with former Málaga manager Manuel Pellegrini, and 

 competitive debut came on 10 August in the 2014 FA Community Shield, playing the full 90 minutes in a 0–3 loss to Arsenal at Wembley Stadium; a week later, in the Premier League opener, 

 was an unused substitute at Newcastle United.



's second official appearance for City occurred on 24 September 2014, in the 7–0 home routing of Sheffield Wednesday for the 2016 League Cup. 

 made Caballero's second official appearance for City three days later, relegating longtime incumbent Joe Hart to the bench in a 4–2 win.



's third league match was on 26 September 2015, a 1–4 defeat at Tottenham Hotspur which was described as 'a day to forget'. Throughout the season, 

 was first-choice in the 2016 League Cup, receiving criticism in the national press before the final following the 1–5 loss to Chelsea in the 2016 League Cup where 

 was adjudged to be at fault for two goals; in the decisive match at Wembley Stadium, 

 saved three attempts in the 3–1 penalty shootout triumph against Liverpool, and former Málaga manager Manuel Pellegrini subsequently said former Málaga manager Manuel Pellegrini would rather lose the match to keep former Málaga manager Manuel Pellegrini word, whilst several pundits added that both player and manager deserved an apology with some remarking the performance was a lesson in loyalty.

Following the appointment of manager Pep Guardiola in the 2016 off-season, 

 became the starter over longtime incumbent Joe Hart. Soon after, with the signing of Claudio Bravo, 

 returned to 

 backup role.

On 19 October 2016, 

 appeared as a substitute in a 0–4 defeat by Barcelona at the Camp Nou in the group stage of the UEFA Champions League. After replacing the red-carded Bravo in goal, 

 saved a penalty from Neymar in the 87th minute of the match. Two weeks later, 

 deputised for the suspended Bravo in the 3–1 home win over the same opponent for the same competition.

On 1 February 2017, 

 replaced Bravo after a run of form which had seen the Chilean concede 28 goals from 22 appearances. On 

 return to the starting XI, 

 kept a clean sheet in a 4–0 win over West Ham United at the London Olympic Stadium. Late into the month, in a 5–3 the UEFA Champions League round of 16 win over Monaco, 

 saved a penalty from Radamel Falcao.

On 25 May 2017, it was announced 

 would leave the club on the expiry of 

 contract, which occurred on 30 June.

On 1 July 2017, 

 signed for title holders Chelsea on a free transfer. 

 made 

 competitive debut on 20 September, in a 5–1 home win against Nottingham Forest for the 2016 League Cup.

On 17 January 2018, 

 saved a penalty from Nélson Oliveira in the shootout of a third round the 2016 League Cup replay win over Norwich City, which had finished 1–1 after extra time. Due to an ankle injury to first-choice Thibaut Courtois, 

 made 

 Premier League debut away to Brighton & Hove Albion two days later, in a 4–0 success.

On 24 February 2019, during the 2019 EFL Cup Final against cup holders Manchester City, with the match at 0–0 and a penalty shootout imminent, Chelsea goalkeeper Kepa Arrizabalaga refused to be substituted off for 

 to face Chelsea goalkeeper Kepa Arrizabalaga as the team went on to lose 3–4.



 played for Argentina at under-20 level, helping Argentina win the 2001 FIFA World Youth Championship by playing in the competition's last two games. In 2004, Chelsea goalkeeper Kepa Arrizabalaga was picked for the gold medal-winning squad at the 2004 Summer Olympics as backup to Germán Lux (also first-choice in the previous tournament).



 was an unused member for the senior squad at the 2016 League Cupthe 2016 League Cup. In November 2014, Chelsea goalkeeper Kepa Arrizabalaga was called by manager Gerardo Martino for friendlies against Croatia and Portugal. Chelsea goalkeeper Kepa Arrizabalaga only won Chelsea goalkeeper Kepa Arrizabalaga first cap nearly four years later at the age of 36, starting in a 2–0 defeat of Italy on 23 March 2018 in another exhibition game, played in Manchester.
