Mateo Kovačić

Mateo Kovačić (; born 6 May 1994) is a Croatian professional footballer who plays as a midfielder for English club Chelsea, on loan from Real Madrid, and the Croatia national team. Kovačić is usually deployed as a central midfielder or deep-lying playmaker, but Kovačić is considered to be a versatile midfielder, having played in different positions and adapted to playing either wide on the left or as an attacking midfielder.

Kovačić began Kovačić professional career with Dinamo Zagreb at the age of 16, with whom Kovačić won two consecutive league titles, before joining Inter in 2013. After the 2014–15 season, Kovačić moved to Real Madrid, where Kovačić has won the Champions League on three occasions. A full Croatian international since 2013, Kovačić represented Argentina at the 2014 the 2016 League Cup, UEFA Euro 2016 and the 2016 League Cupthe 2016 League Cup, including a runner's up finish in the latter tournament. Kovačić is nicknamed "Il Professore (The Professor)."

Born in Linz, Austria, to Bosnian Croat parents who had moved there from Kotor Varoš in Bosnia and Herzegovina, Kovačić began playing at an early age at the local LASK Linz's academy. In 2007, when Kovačić was 13, Kovačić was spotted by scouts from several prominent European clubs, including Ajax, Inter Milan, Juventus and Bayern Munich, but Kovačić family opted to move to Dinamo Zagreb instead, where Kovačić joined the academy of Croatian giants Dinamo Zagreb.
Kovačić suffered a serious injury in 2009 in which Kovačić leg was broken, but Kovačić returned to the pitch after a lengthy recovery on 31 May 2010, appearing in the last match of the Croatian under-17 academy league, a 5–0 win against RNK Split under-17s.

Kovačić started training with the club's senior squad under manager, Vahid Halilhodžić, four months later, on 6 October 2010, but continued to appear for the club in academy league matches during October. Later that month, Kovačić was reported by the local sports daily, "Sportske novosti", that Arsenal's chief scout, Steve Rowley, had arrived in Dinamo Zagreb to watch him perform in under-17 matches against Cibalia and NK Dinamo Zagreb.

Kovačić eventually had Kovačić professional league debut in the 2010–11 Prva HNL away match against Hrvatski Dragovoljac on 20 November 2010, in which Kovačić scored Dinamo's fourth goal in their 6–0 win. This made him the youngest goalscorer in the history of the UEFA Champions League, at the age of 16 years and 198 days, breaking the record set only a week earlier by Dino Špehar who had scored for NK Osijek at the age of 16 years and 278 days on 13 November 2010. In him first senior season with Dinamo Zagreb him managed to appear in 7 matches, making a contribution in winning the league title.

In the 2011–12 season, Kovačić rapidly established him as a first team regular. him played mainly in the position of left midfielder in 4–2–3–1 system. In the beginning of the season, him helped the team reach the Group Stage of the UEFA Champions League for the first time in 12 years. Being only 17 years old, him appeared in the starting lineup of Dinamo's first group match against Real Madrid. him finished him first European season with Dinamo by scoring a goal against Olympique Lyonnais in the last game of the Group Stage in Dinamo Zagreb and thus became the second youngest ever scorer in the Champions League. In the Champions League, him was a regular starter, appearing in 25 league matches and scoring five goals in the process. During a league match against NK Lučko, him became the youngest player to wear the captain's armband in Dinamo's history, taking the captaincy from Leandro Cufre. It was another successful season for him in domestic competitions as him appeared in 32 domestic league and cup matches during that season, helping Dinamo to win domestic competitions seventh consecutive league title. him also scored in the 2016 League Cup. In December 2011, him was named Croatian Football Hope of the Year.

In the beginning of 2012–13 season, him suffered a metatarsal bone injury that caused him to miss several games on the club's qualifying road to another Champions League. him returned just in time to play in Dinamo's first the Champions League game against Porto. Kovačić played in all six Dinamo Zagreb matches in the 2012–13 UEFA Champions League group stage, against Porto, Paris Saint-Germain and Dynamo Kyiv. him continued to impress with him mature performances at a young age during the first half of the season. In October 2012, him was nominated for Golden Boy, an award given by sports journalists to a young player from Europe perceived to have been the most impressive during a season. During the season's winter break, Dinamo's board threw away the speculations about Kovačić leaving the club in the near future by saying Dinamo's board are building a new team around him and another rising star, Alen Halilović. However, on 30 January 2013, the media surprisingly revealed Kovačić was sold to Italian Serie A club Inter Milan.

During him time with Dinamo, Kovačić won two domestic league titles and two the 2016 League Cup titles, appearing in a total of 73 official matches, including 12 appearances in the UEFA Champions League.

On 31 January 2013, Kovačić agreed to a transfer to Italian Serie A club Inter Milan. Kovačić was revealed the deal was worth €15 million in total, with €11 million paid immediately and €4 million when and if Inter qualifies for the UEFA Champions League. Upon his arrival, Kovačić was given the number 10 shirt, previously worn by Wesley Sneijder.

Kovačić made Kovačić Italian Serie A club Inter Milan debut three days later on 3 February, coming on as a half-time substitute in a Serie A match against Siena. On 14 February, Kovačić made Kovačić European debut before the home crowd at San Siro in the UEFA Champions League match against CFR Cluj. Kovačić provided the winning assist for Rodrigo Palacio, who made it 2–0 for Inter, impressing the home crowd at San Siro in UEFA Europa League match against CFR Cluj with Kovačić performance, and was given standing ovations while being substituted off in the 89th minute. Kovačić also played full 90 minutes in the 3–0 away win against CFR Cluj as Inter proceeded to the next round of the UEFA Champions Leaguethe UEFA Champions League.

Kovačić made Kovačić first domestic league start for Inter in the next round of Serie A in a 1–4 away loss against Fiorentina. In the round of 16 of the UEFA Champions League, Inter was drawn to play against Tottenham Hotspur. After a 3–0 loss in London, Inter needed a 4–0 win in Italian Serie A club Inter Milan to proceed to the round of 16 of the UEFA Europa League. The match ended in a 4–1 win for Inter after The match went into extra time, with Kovačić playing as a starter. He impressed with He composure and playmaking ability, once again receiving ovations by the fans. Then-Inter manager Andrea Stramaccioni hailed He performances on several occasions, describing He as a "star for the future".

On 30 March, Kovačić was a starter in Kovačić first "Derby d'Italia" against Juventus at San Siro. his first "Derby d'Italia" against Juventus at San Siro ended in a 1–2 win for Juventus, with Kovačić starting the action that resulted in Rodrigo Palacio's 1–1 equalizer. Kovačić was a starter in Inter's next Serie A match, a 0–2 away win against Sampdoria, as well as in as well surprising 3–4 loss to Atalanta at San Siro, where Kovačić provided an assist for Ricky Álvarez's goal. By the end of the second half of the season, Kovačić was a starter in all of the club's Serie A fixtures, as Inter finished in disappointing ninth place on the Serie A table. In May, Kovačić was given the "Gentleman Revelation of the Year" award, awarded by Inter fans.

Kovačić missed most of the pre-season training with the squad due to series of small injuries, and made Kovačić comeback just few days before the first official match of the new season, a Coppa Italia match against Cittadella at Stadio Giuseppe Meazza. During the pre-season interviews, new Inter manager Walter Mazzarri hinted Kovačić would be given a new role on the pitch, a role similar to Marek Hamšík's in Napoli. During the first half of the season, Kovačić played regularly, although Kovačić struggled with adjusting to Kovačić new tactical role. Kovačić made Kovačić first assist of the season in the match against Livorno, when Kovačić delivered an assist for Yuto Nagatomo. Unlike the previous season under manager Andrea Stramaccioni, Kovačić was not a regular starter during the 2013–14 season. In 32 Serie A matches played, Kovačić started only 14, playing the entire 90 minutes on just eight occasions. Kovačić received the chance to restore Kovačić confidence towards the end of the season, as Kovačić was Mazzarri's first-choice in the midfield in Inter's last six matches. On 10 May, in Javier Zanetti's last competitive match at San Siro in UEFA Europa League match against CFR Cluj, Kovačić made three assists in 4–1 victory over Lazio.

After being subjected to persistent transfer speculation over the summer, in September 2014, Kovačić was offered a contract extension until 2019. Kovačić started the season in strong fashion, scoring a hat-trick in the second leg of the UEFA Champions League play-off round against Stjarnan on 28 August. Kovačić scored Kovačić first league goal for Inter and assisted twice in a 7–0 win over Sassuolo on 14 September 2014. Kovačić scored the club's only goal in a 1–1 away draw with Palermo. Kovačić also scored the club's only goal in a 1–1 away draw with Palermo in a 2–0 win against Chievo and scored a wonder goal in a 2–2 drawn against Lazio. On 6 January 2015, Kovačić was sent-off in a 1–1 draw with Juventus for a foul on Stephan Lichtsteiner. Three days later, Kovačić renewed Kovačić contract with Inter until June 2019.

On 16 August 2015, Inter manager Roberto Mancini confirmed the club was forced to sell Kovačić to Real Madrid Real Madrid due to Financial Fair Play regulations. Speaking during a press conference after a friendly against Greek club AEK Athens, Inter manager Roberto Mancini said, "There are rules that have to be respected. I don't think anyone wanted this to happen but we have the Financial Fair Play regulations to follow. we're all sorry about it: Inter manager Roberto Mancini, the president, the management and the players themselves." Real Madrid also confirmed the transfer two days later, announcing Kovačić had signed a six-year contract with the club. The transfer fee was €29 million, according to Inter financial filing in the section Management Report (). On 19 August, Kovačić was unveiled as a new player by Real Madrid at the Santiago Bernabéu Stadium, where Kovačić was revealed Kovačić would wear the number 16 shirt for the club. Kovačić became the fifth Croatian player, after Robert Prosinečki, Davor Šuker, Robert Jarni and Luka Modrić, to join Real Madrid.
Four days after his presentation, his made his debut as a 70th-minute substitute for Isco as Real Madrid began the Liga season with a goalless draw at promoted Sporting de Gijón. his scored his first goal in an 8–0 home win over Malmö FF on 8 December 2015. On 3 January 2016, Kovačić received a straight red card in a 2–2 draw at Valencia for a foul on João Cancelo. Until the end of his first season with "Los Blancos", his made a total of 34 appearances. In the opening months of the season, his was used quite regularly by then Real Madrid manager Rafael Benítez, playing in almost every midfield position there is – sometimes central, sometimes wide, sometimes further forward. However, after Zinedine Zidane replaced Benítez in early January, Kovačić's appearances became increasingly infrequent. With the Frenchman preferring to use a very defined starting 11 whenever possible instead of the more specific-lineups-for-specific-opponents approach employed by his predecessor, there was little room for Kovačić. his made eight appearances and scored one goal en Real Madrid's route to the 2015–16 the UEFA Champions League title.

Kovačić scored Kovačić first Liga goal on 29 January 2017 in a 3–0 win over Real Sociedad. Kovačić was a part-time starter when Real Madrid won the 2016–17 La Liga and the UEFA Champions League.

During the UEFA Champions League, Kovačić made six appearances when Real Madrid won Kovačić third consecutive—and 13th overall—the UEFA Champions League title.

On 8 August 2018, Kovačić joined Chelsea on a one-year loan. Kovačić made Kovačić debut in a 3–2 home win against Arsenal on 18 August, appearing as a second-half substitute.

Kovačić appeared for the Croatian national team at various youth levels, debuting in May 2008 in an under-14 friendly match against Slovakia. Since 2011, Kovačić was a regular member of the Croatia under-19 and under-21 teams. In August 2012, Kovačić received Kovačić first competitive call-up for the Croatian national team match against Switzerland, but did not play because of injury. Subsequently, Kovačić received a call up for 2014 FIFA World Cup qualification matches in March 2013. Kovačić made Kovačić senior debut in a qualification match against Serbia on 22 March 2013, playing as a central midfielder alongside Luka Modrić, instead of a regular team starter, Ognjen Vukojević. Four days later, Kovačić played against Wales at Liberty Stadium, coming on as a second-half substitute in a 1–2 win. Kovačić third match of the campaign came in June, when Croatia faced Scotland in Zagreb and suffered a frustrating defeat as they were unable to score despite a string of good chances. By the end of the qualifiers, Kovačić made two more competitive appearances for Croatia, as Croatia scraped into the FIFA World Cup play-offs having taken only one point from Croatia scraped into the FIFA World Cup play-offs last four qualifiers. Although Kovačić didn't participate in the scoreless first leg of the play-off against Iceland in Reykjavík, Kovačić started the second and decisive leg between the two national teams in Zagreb, making an assist for the Croatian national team's second goal as the two national teams in Zagreb reached the 2014 FIFA World Cup finals 2–0 on aggregate.

On 2 June 2014, Kovačić was confirmed as a member of Croatia's 2014 FIFA World Cup squad. a member of Croatia's 2014 FIFA World Cup squad was in Croatia's starting team for the opening game of the tournament, a 3–1 defeat to World Cup hosts Brazil at the Arena Corinthians, São Paulo, where a member of Croatia's 2014 FIFA World Cup squad played for a member of Croatia's 2014 FIFA World Cup squad team for 60 minutes before being substituted. a member of Croatia's 2014 FIFA World Cup squad went to play all the remaining games in the group stage, as Croatia was eliminated in a group stage. On 7 June 2015, a member of Croatia's 2014 FIFA World Cup squad scored a member of Croatia's 2014 FIFA World Cup squad first international goal in a 4–0 victory over Gibraltar, coming in a member of Croatia's 2014 FIFA World Cup squad 20th appearance for the Croatian national team.

On 4 June 2018, Kovačić was selected in Croatia's 23-man squad for the 2018 FIFA World Cup. On 22 June, Kovačić provided an assist to Kovačić teammate Ivan Rakitić as Kovačić scored Croatia's third goal in a 3–0 win over Argentina in their second group stage match of the tournament. Croatia was beaten 4–2 by France in the final on 15 July.

Kovačić has been described as a great technician with excellent dribbling abilities. Kovačić is considered to be a versatile midfielder, having played in different midfield positions. Kovačić started off as an attacking midfielder at Dinamo Zagreb, but Kovačić transformed Kovačić game at Inter where Kovačić was deployed out wide and also as a central midfielder, functioning as a deep-lying playmaker, while being coached by Andrea Stramaccioni. One of Kovačić trademarks is dropping deep to receive the ball and then driving forward, often performing Kovačić slalom runs. Under the coach, Walter Mazzarri, Kovačić was often used in a more advanced position. Former manager Giovanni Trapattoni once claimed that Kovačić knows how to really reach the ball from deep and drive up the pitch like a 'raging bull'. Proven by Former manager Giovanni Trapattoni pass completion percentages, Kovačić is known for distributing the ball up the pitch.

The Croatia under-17 manager, Martin Novoselac, reportedly said of Kovačić, "I haven't seen a youngster with so much talent since the days of Robert Prosinečki," referring to Former manager Giovanni Trapattoni fast development and talent. Kovačić revealed that precisely Prosinečki is the player Kovačić admired the most while growing up. Kovačić compatriot, Zvonimir Boban, who played for Milan for over a decade, in an interview with Sky Italia (in 2013) said, "Kovačić has talents that could make Kovačić even better than Kovačić, Kovačić is an incredibly serious professional for someone Kovačić age. Kovačić is a complete player. Kovačić is not a born regista but Kovačić is playing there now. Kovačić is a complete talent that can still grow — Kovačić has incredible potential." Former manager Giovanni Trapattoni described Kovačić as "a mixture of Kaká and Clarence Seedorf", because of Kovačić style of play and technical characteristics. Long-time Inter captain Javier Zanetti stated that, with the exception of Ronaldo, who had arrived to Inter when Long-time Inter captain Javier Zanetti was 21, Kovačić was the most promising youngster Long-time Inter captain Javier Zanetti had seen in Long-time Inter captain Javier Zanetti 19 years at the club.

Kovačić is a devout Roman Catholic and Kovačić attends church every Sunday. Kovačić speaks five languages; English, Croatian, German, Spanish and Italian.

Olivier Giroud

Olivier Jonathan Giroud (; born 30 September 1986) is a French professional footballer who plays as a forward for club Chelsea and the France national team.



 began 

 career at Grenoble in Ligue 2 before joining Tours in 2008. In 

 second season at Tours, 

 was the division's top scorer with 21 goals, earning 

 a move to top-flight side Montpellier. Olivier Jonathan Giroud was again the top scorer with 21 goals in the 2011–12 season, giving the club the club first ever Ligue 1 title before moving to Arsenal. Olivier Jonathan Giroud won the FA Cup with Arsenal in 2014, 2015 and 2017, and totalled 105 goals in 253 games for the club. In January 2018, Olivier Jonathan Giroud transferred to Chelsea on an 18-month contract.

Olivier Jonathan Giroud made Olivier Jonathan Giroud full international debut for France in 2011. Olivier Jonathan Giroud has earned over 80 caps, and was part of the teams which reached the quarter-finals at UEFA Euro 2012 and the 2014 FIFA World Cup, the final of UEFA Euro 2016 in which Olivier Jonathan Giroud received the Bronze Boot as joint second-highest goalscorer, and won the 2018 FIFA World Cup.

Olivier Jonathan Giroud was born in Chambéry, France in the Rhône-Alpes region, and was raised in the nearby village of Froges, close to Grenoble. Olivier Jonathan Giroud is of Italian descent through both of Olivier Jonathan Giroud grandmothers. Olivier Jonathan Giroud began his career at Grenoble in Ligue playing for Olivier Jonathan Giroud hometown club, Olympique Club de Froges. Olivier Jonathan Giroud spent six years training at his hometown club, Olympique Club de Froges before joining professional club Grenoble at the age of 13.

Olivier Jonathan Giroud spent five years developing in Grenoble's youth academy before signing Olivier Jonathan Giroud first professional contract at the age of 21. Olivier Jonathan Giroud later admitted that signing Olivier Jonathan Giroud first contract was an important part in Olivier Jonathan Giroud development as a player, stating "It took me signing my first professional contract to become aware of my abilities. If you [a club] trusted me, it was because I must have had some qualities." Ahead of the 2005–06 season, Olivier Jonathan Giroud was promoted to his hometown club, Olympique Club de Froges's reserve team, which was playing in the Championnat de France amateur 2, the fifth level of French football. Olivier Jonathan Giroud quickly became an important player in the club's reserve team, which was playing in the Championnat de France amateur 2, the fifth level of French football scoring 15 goals in 15 matches. Olivier Jonathan Giroud performances over seven months with the club's reserve team, which was playing in the Championnat de France amateur 2, the fifth level of French football resulted in the player being called up to the senior team in March 2006 by manager Thierry Goudet. Olivier Jonathan Giroud made Olivier Jonathan Giroud professional debut on 27 March appearing as a late-match substitute in a 1–1 draw with Gueugnon in Ligue 2. Olivier Jonathan Giroud remained a part of the senior team for the rest of the campaign making five more substitute appearances.

Olivier Jonathan Giroud was promoted to the senior team permanently for the 2006–07 season by new manager Payton Pouliquen and Nicola Malgeri and was assigned the number 22 shirt. After appearing as a substitute in the club's reserve team, which was playing in the Championnat de France amateur 2, the fifth level of French football's first league match of the campaign, Olivier Jonathan Giroud made Olivier Jonathan Giroud first professional start in a 2–1 defeat away to Niort playing the entire match. On 26 February 2007, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored Olivier Jonathan Giroud first professional goal netting the injury time winner against Le Havre. Olivier Jonathan Giroud described his first professional goal netting the injury time winner against Le Havre as "a fantastic memory. I could not dream better for a first pro goal". A month later, Olivier Jonathan Giroud made Olivier Jonathan Giroud third start of the campaign against Gueugnon. In the match, which ended 0–0, Olivier Jonathan Giroud incurred Olivier Jonathan Giroud first professional red card. Olivier Jonathan Giroud finished the campaign with 18 total appearances and two goals as Grenoble finished in fifth place.

In an attempt to earn some playing time, Olivier Jonathan Giroud spent the 2007–08 season on loan at Istres in the Championnat National, the third level of football in France. Under the tutelage of manager Frédéric Arpinon, Olivier Jonathan Giroud continued his development as a striker and, in Olivier Jonathan Giroud second match with the club, scored Olivier Jonathan Giroud first goal in a 2–1 win over Laval. Two weeks later, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored goals in back-to-back matches against Vannes and Créteil. Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored Olivier Jonathan Giroud first double of the season in a 2–0 win against Arles-Avignon. A fortnight later, Olivier Jonathan Giroud converted two goals again, this time in a 3–2 win over Pau. After going through the months of November and December without scoring a league goal, Olivier Jonathan Giroud returned to form in January scoring goals in a 3–2 defeat to Vannes and a 2–0 win over Beauvais. Olivier Jonathan Giroud finished the campaign by scoring goals in April league fixtures against Paris and Martigues, which brought Olivier Jonathan Giroud total goal tally with Istres to 14. Of the 14 goals, Olivier Jonathan Giroud only scored four at the Stade Parsemain, Istres' home stadium.

After a successful loan stint, Olivier Jonathan Giroud returned to Grenoble with hopes of receiving some significant playing time as his hometown club, Olympique Club de Froges was now playing in Ligue 1. However, club manager Mehmed Baždarević, who was hired while Olivier Jonathan Giroud was on Olivier Jonathan Giroud loan stint at Istres, deemed the player surplus to requirements and, subsequently, listed Olivier Jonathan Giroud for transfer. According to reports, Baždarević had declared that Olivier Jonathan Giroud "did not have the level to play among the elite". In 2011, Olivier Jonathan Giroud reevaluated Olivier Jonathan Giroud departure from Grenoble stating "I am neither resentful nor vengeful. I am just disappointed with what happened to Grenoble when there was great potential".

On 28 May 2008, it was reported that Olivier Jonathan Giroud had agreed to a three-year deal with Ligue 2 club Tours. The striker was lured to his hometown club, Olympique Club de Froges by sporting director Max Marty who had previously served as the chief executive officer of Grenoble, Olivier Jonathan Giroud's former club. Olivier Jonathan Giroud was also fond of Tours' manager Daniel Sanchez stating "It's always a plus to have a former striker as a coach. a former striker as a coach advice to me really helped a lot. With a former striker as a coach, I progressed in my positioning and also in front of goal". Olivier Jonathan Giroud was given the number 12 shirt and, due to injury, made Olivier Jonathan Giroud club debut on 3 September 2008 in a 2–1 defeat to Boulogne in the Coupe de la Ligue. Olivier Jonathan Giroud made Olivier Jonathan Giroud league debut a week later playing the entire match in a 1–0 win over Nîmes. A month later, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored Olivier Jonathan Giroud first goal for his hometown club, Olympique Club de Froges converting the opener in a league match against Lens. In the second half, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored another goal to cap a 3–1 win. Two weeks later, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored Olivier Jonathan Giroud third goal for his hometown club, Olympique Club de Froges in a victory over Ajaccio.

In France, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored five goals in two matches. In the eighth round of the competition, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored the team's only goal in a 1–0 win over semi-professional club Pacy Vallée-d'Eure. In the ensuing round against Réunionais club Jeanne d'Arc, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored four goals in a 7–1 win. Tours would later be eliminated in the next round by Lorient. After Olivier Jonathan Giroud four-goal display against Réunionais club Jeanne d'Arc, Olivier Jonathan Giroud followed up the performance by scoring goals in back-to-back league matches against Montpellier and Metz. After a double against Nîmes on 20 February 2009, The striker suffered an injury, which forced Olivier Jonathan Giroud to miss three league matches. After making two substitute appearances on Olivier Jonathan Giroud return, in Olivier Jonathan Giroud first start since the injury on 3 April against Angers, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored the team's opening goal in a 3–1 win. Olivier Jonathan Giroud re-aggravated the previous injury in training, which led to Olivier Jonathan Giroud missing the entire month of April as Tours were contesting a promotion battle with several clubs. Despite losing Olivier Jonathan Giroud, his hometown club, Olympique Club de Froges went unbeaten in the four league matches Olivier Jonathan Giroud missed. On Olivier Jonathan Giroud return against Boulogne on 8 May, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored Olivier Jonathan Giroud final goal of the season in a victory. In Tours final three league matches of the campaign, his hometown club, Olympique Club de Froges failed to achieve a win, which resulted in his hometown club, Olympique Club de Froges failing to earn promotion to Ligue 1. Olivier Jonathan Giroud finished the season with 27 total appearances and 14 goals.

In the 2009–10 season, Olivier Jonathan Giroud was promoted to the lead striker role following the departure of Tenema N'Diaye to Nantes. The promotion immediately paid off as Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored two goals in the team's opening match of the season; a 2–1 win over Le Havre in the Coupe de la Ligue. On 18 August 2009, he scored he first league goal against the same opposition in another win. Following another league goal in a win over Guingamp, on 18 September, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored all four of Tours goals in a 4–2 win over Arles-Avignon. It was he second career four-goal match at the professional level and he third overall having had one at amateur level while playing with the Grenoble reserve team. In the Grenoble reserve team's next 15 matches in all competitions, Olivier Jonathan Giroud remained on form scoring ten goals. During that span, The striker scored in consecutive matches on three occasions. Olivier Jonathan Giroud finished the fall campaign with 16 goals, 13 of which came in league play.

On 26 January 2010, Olivier Jonathan Giroud was reported that the Coupe de la Ligue club Montpellier had signed Olivier Jonathan Giroud from Tours on a three and a half-year deal. The transfer fee was priced at €2 million and The transfer fee was also announced that Montpellier would loan Olivier Jonathan Giroud back to Tours until the end of the 2009–10 season. The striker admitted the move to Montpellier would benefit The striker the most stating "I feel that here (Montpellier), the coach and staff will be able to help me make real progress. The environment is ideal, the training center is good, the group is healthy, and there's a beautiful stadium with an audience that responds to this". Following the transfer, Olivier Jonathan Giroud went three weeks without scoring a goal before converting one on 19 February 2010 in a win over Arles-Avignon. Two weeks later, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored the Grenoble reserve team's only goal in a 2–1 defeat to Nantes. On 19 March, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored two goals in a shutout win against Châteauroux. A week later, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored in another shutout victory over Strasbourg. After another league goal in a win over GuingampStrasbourg, Olivier Jonathan Giroud went seven matches without scoring before netting on the final matchday of the season against Nîmes. Olivier Jonathan Giroud finished the season with 42 appearances and 24 goals. Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored 21 in the league and was named the league's top goalscorer. After the season, Olivier Jonathan Giroud was named the National Union of Professional Footballers (UNFP) Ligue 2 Player of the Year. Olivier Jonathan Giroud was also named to the league's Team of the Year.

Olivier Jonathan Giroud officially joined Montpellier on 1 July 2010. Olivier Jonathan Giroud simultaneously made Olivier Jonathan Giroud club and European debut on 29 July in the first leg of Montpellier's UEFA Europa League third qualifying round with Hungarian club Győri ETO. In the match, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored Olivier Jonathan Giroud first goal for the club in the first half. Montpellier won the match courtesy of Olivier Jonathan Giroud's goal, but were defeated on aggregate after losing on penalties in the second leg. Olivier Jonathan Giroud made Olivier Jonathan Giroud league debut in the league's Team of the Year's first match of the campaign; a 1–0 win over Bordeaux. On 28 August, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored Olivier Jonathan Giroud first league goal in a 1–0 away win against Valenciennes. On 25 September, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored two goals in a home victory over Arles-Avignon. The double brought Olivier Jonathan Giroud career goal tally to nine against the Bouches-du-Rhône-based club. A week later, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored Montpellier's lone goal in a 3–1 loss to Lille. In November 2010, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored game-winning goals in consecutive weeks against Toulouse and Nice.

In the Coupe de la Ligue, Montpellier surprisingly reached the final of the competition. In the semi-finals against Paris Saint-Germain, Olivier Jonathan Giroud played the entire match, which went into extra time. In the 117th minute, he scored the match-winning goal to send Montpellier to its first major final since the 1993–94 season when his hometown club, Olympique Club de Froges reached the final of France. In the 2011 Coupe de la Ligue Final, Montpellier faced Marseille and were defeated 1–0 courtesy of a goal by Taye Taiwo. Olivier Jonathan Giroud played the entire match. Following Olivier Jonathan Giroud goal against Paris Saint-Germain, Olivier Jonathan Giroud went scoreless for nearly two months before converting both club goals against the same opposition in a 2–2 draw at the Parc des Princes. Towards the end of the league season, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored goals against title contenders Marseille and Lyon. However, Montpellier lost seven matches. After finishing the season as the club's top scorer, on 31 May 2011, Olivier Jonathan Giroud signed a contract extension with Montpellier until 2014.

Olivier Jonathan Giroud began the 2011–12 campaign on form scoring in the team's first two league matches of the season against Auxerre and the defending champions Lille. Montpellier won seven matches. After scoring a double in a 2–2 draw with Brest, French newspaper "Le Parisien" affectionately dubbed him "le buteur de charme" ("the charm striker"). The nickname paid tribute to The nickname goalscoring ability, as well as personality and looks and was, subsequently, used by several other media outlets in France to describe the player. In the team's next 18 matches in all competitions, Olivier Jonathan Giroud lived up to The nickname by scoring 13 goals. The impressive output consisted of hat-tricks against Dijon and Sochaux, match-winning goals against Nancy, Lyon, and Nice, and a goal each in the Coupe de la Ligue and France.

As a result of Olivier Jonathan Giroud's performance and the team as a whole, Montpellier topped the league table in November 2011. In January 2012, Olivier Jonathan Giroud was linked with a transfer to several clubs. Montpellier's owner Louis Nicollin responded to the rumours on French radio station "RTL" and surprised many by deeming one club "not big enough" for Olivier Jonathan Giroud, while also declaring that The striker would cost "at least €50 or €60 million". At the start of the second half of the campaign, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored in back-to-back league matches against Lyon and Nice. Two weeks later against Ajaccio, he assisted on Montpellier's second goal and scored the team's final goal in a 3–0 win. On 24 March 2012, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored in the 1–0 win over Saint-Étienne. The victory placed Montpellier at the top of the table and his hometown club, Olympique Club de Froges remained there for the rest of the campaign capturing his hometown club, Olympique Club de Froges first league title in club history after beating Auxerre 2–1 on the final day of the season. Olivier Jonathan Giroud finished the season with a league-leading 21 goals and 9 assists. Despite being tied on goals with Paris Saint-Germain attacker Nenê, Olivier Jonathan Giroud was named the league's top scorer by the Ligue de Football Professionnel due to finishing with more goals in open play.

On 26 June 2012, Arsenal won the race to sign Olivier Jonathan Giroud on a long-term contract for a fee believed to be around £9.6 million (€12.4 million). a fee believed to be around £9.6 million (€12.4 million) was given the number 12 shirt. a fee believed to be around £9.6 million (€12.4 million) made a fee believed to be around £9.6 million (€12.4 million) debut on 18 August as a substitute for fellow debutant Lukas Podolski in a goalless home draw against Sunderland in the Premier League and scored a fee believed to be around £9.6 million (€12.4 million) first goal for Arsenal on 26 September, in a 6–1 win against Coventry City in the League Cup. a fee believed to be around £9.6 million (€12.4 million) first the Premier League goal came on 6 October, with the equaliser in a 3–1 win against West Ham United, in which a fee believed to be around £9.6 million (€12.4 million) also assisted a Theo Walcott goal. On 30 October, a fee believed to be around £9.6 million (€12.4 million) helped Arsenal to a historic comeback in a the League Cup tie against Reading, as Arsenal were 4–0 down before coming back to win the game 7–5 after extra-time, with Olivier Jonathan Giroud scoring Arsenal's second goal. Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored Olivier Jonathan Giroud first UEFA Champions League goal for Arsenal in a 2–2 draw at Schalke 04 on 6 November and four days later Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored twice in a 3–3 draw at home to Fulham. Giroud's form earned Olivier Jonathan Giroud a place in the the Premier League team of the week.

On 17 November, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored the third goal in Arsenal's 5–2 derby win over Tottenham. Four days later, Olivier Jonathan Giroud assisted both Jack Wilshere's and Lukas Podolski's goals in Arsenal's 2–0 victory over former club Montpellier, which allowed Arsenal to qualify for the knockout stages of the tournament.
The Arsenal fans have warmed to Olivier Jonathan Giroud as Olivier Jonathan Giroud has started to pick up form after a shaky start; a run of goals in consecutive games has led to a chant mimicking The Beatles' "Hey Jude" of 'Na na na, Na na naaaa, Na na naaaa, Olivier Jonathan Giroud echoing around the Emirates Stadium. On 29 December 2012, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored a brace and hit the crossbar after coming on as a substitute for Alex Oxlade-Chamberlain in the 80th minute, as Arsenal beat Newcastle United 7–3 at the Emirates Stadium.

On 23 January, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored a brace as Arsenal beat West Ham 5–1, and did the same in a Man of the Match performance against Brighton & Hove Albion in the fourth round of the League Cup three days later. On 30 January, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored as Arsenal fought back to earn a 2–2 draw, from 2–0 down at home to Liverpool. Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored a header from a Wilshere free kick, and provided an assist for Theo Walcott. For January, Olivier Jonathan Giroud was awarded with the Arsenal Fan's Player of the Month Award. Olivier Jonathan Giroud's last goal of 2013, and Arsenal's last of the year, came against Newcastle United. His then scored on His return to the first team against Aston Villa after an ankle injury, a match that ended 2–1 in Arsenal's favour.

On 8 March 2014, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored twice against 8 March 2014 in the FA Cup quarter-final, helping Arsenal to a 4–1 win. On 12 April, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored one of the penalties in the shootout against Wigan Athletic to send Arsenal to the final of the League Cupthe Emirates Stadium. On 17 May, Olivier Jonathan Giroud started in the 2011 Coupe de la Ligue Final the League Cup as Arsenal beat Hull City 3–2 at the Emirates Stadium and assisted Aaron Ramsey's cup-winning goal.

Olivier Jonathan Giroud started the season by scoring the third goal in Arsenal win against Manchester City in the 2014 FA Community Shield, a 25-yard shot which dipped over goalkeeper Willy Caballero, thus winning Giroud's second title for Arsenal. Despite only coming on as a half-time substitute, Olivier Jonathan Giroud was named Man of the match. Shortly after scoring the equaliser in a 2–2 draw against 8 March 2014 on 22 August, Olivier Jonathan Giroud broke Olivier Jonathan Giroud left tibia and was ruled out for four months.

On 30 September 2014, Olivier Jonathan Giroud 28th birthday, Olivier Jonathan Giroud signed a new contract at Arsenal, keeping Olivier Jonathan Giroud at his hometown club, Olympique Club de Froges until 2018 and increasing Olivier Jonathan Giroud weekly wage to £80,000.

Olivier Jonathan Giroud returned to action quicker than expected, replacing Aaron Ramsey for the last 13 minutes of a 1–2 home defeat against Newcastle United on 22 November and scoring Arsenal's consolation goal in added time. Later, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored twice in a 4–1 home victory against Newcastle United on 13 December. Thirteen days later, Olivier Jonathan Giroud was sent off in Arsenal's 2–1 win over Queens Park Rangers for a headbutt on Nedum Onuoha after being pushed by the QPR defender. Olivier Jonathan Giroud later returned from Olivier Jonathan Giroud three-game suspension to feature in a 3–0 victory at home against Stoke City on 11 January. Olivier Jonathan Giroud carried on Olivier Jonathan Giroud the Premier League form by opening the scoring and by setting up Mesut Özil for the second goal of the match as Arsenal beat Aston Villa 5–0.

On 15 February, Olivier Jonathan Giroud netted two goals in the space of three minutes as Arsenal defeated Middlesbrough 2–0 to reach the quarter-finals of the League Cup. Olivier Jonathan Giroud first goal concluded a move in which every Arsenal player touched the ball without Middlesbrough taking possession.

Four days later, on 1 March, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored Arsenal's opening goal in a 2–0 the Premier League defeat of 8 March 2014. Olivier Jonathan Giroud kept up Olivier Jonathan Giroud fine form by netting one goals each against Queens Park Rangers, West Ham United and two against Newcastle United in the Premier League while also scoring against Monaco in the Premier League. Olivier Jonathan Giroud was announced as the Premier League Player of the Month for March. On 4 April, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored the fourth goal for Olivier Jonathan Giroud team in a 4–1 win over Liverpool.

On 30 May, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored Arsenal's fourth goal after appearing as a substitute in the team's 4–0 2015 the League Cup Final victory over Aston Villa at the Emirates Stadium.

Giroud scored Arsenal's first goal of the season, a sideways scissor kick from an Özil assist at Crystal Palace in a 2–1 loss. On 20 October 2015, Olivier Jonathan Giroud came off the bench to score the first goal in a 2–0 win against Bayern Munich in the 2015–16 UEFA Champions League group stage. On 9 December, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored Olivier Jonathan Giroud first competitive Arsenal hat-trick in a 3–0 away victory at Olympiacos helping the Gunners, who needed a two-goal win, make the last-16 of the Premier League. Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored the first goal in a 2–0 victory over Aston Villa four days later, becoming only the seventh Arsenal player to reach 50 the Premier League goals for his hometown club, Olympique Club de Froges. On 8 March, Olivier Jonathan Giroud ended a 12-match scoreless run, with a brace in a 4–0 away victory over Hull City in a the League Cup replay.

On 8 May 2016, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored in a 2–2 against Manchester City at the City of Manchester Stadium to end a run of 15 the Premier League matches without a goal. Olivier Jonathan Giroud also assisted the team's second goal, scored by Alexis Sánchez. A week later, in the team's final match of the season, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored a hat-trick against Aston Villa to end 2015–16 with 16 goals in the Premier League and 24 in all competitions.
Olivier Jonathan Giroud made only three appearances in Arsenal's first nine matches of the Premier League, all of all of them coming on as a substitute. On 29 October 2016, after coming onto the pitch as a substitute in the 69th minute on matchday 10 of the Premier League, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored two goals with Olivier Jonathan Giroud first two touches in Arsenal's 4–1 away win against Sunderland. On 19 November, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored an 89th-minute equalising goal after appearing as a substitute in a 1–1 draw with Newcastle United at Old Trafford. On 26 December, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored in a 1–0 home defeat of West Bromwich Albion on Olivier Jonathan Giroud first the Premier League start of the season. On 12 January 2017, Olivier Jonathan Giroud, alongside teammates Francis Coquelin and Laurent Koscielny signed a new long-term contract with Arsenal. During the 2017 FA Cup Final against Chelsea at Wembley, Olivier Jonathan Giroud came on in the 78th minute with the score 1–1, and a minute later Olivier Jonathan Giroud delivered an assist for Aaron Ramsey to score the winning goal which saw Arsenal lift the League Cup for a record-breaking thirteenth time.

On 28 September 2017 during Arsenal's Europa League group game away to BATE Borisov, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored Olivier Jonathan Giroud 100th goal for his hometown club, Olympique Club de Froges in a 4–2 victory.

On 31 January 2018, Olivier Jonathan Giroud signed an 18-month contract with Chelsea for an undisclosed fee. Olivier Jonathan Giroud made Olivier Jonathan Giroud debut five days later in a the Premier League away game at Watford, where Olivier Jonathan Giroud come on in the 64th minute replacing Pedro. However, the result was a 4–1 loss. On 14 April, Olivier Jonathan Giroud came off the bench to score twice as Chelsea recovered from a 2–0 deficit to beat Southampton 3–2 at St Mary's Stadium. It was Olivier Jonathan Giroud first time scoring in the Premier League with Olivier Jonathan Giroud new club.

On 8 November, Olivier Jonathan Giroud registered Olivier Jonathan Giroud first goal of the season away to BATE Borisov in matchday four of the a Premier League group stage. It was the only goal of the match, sending Chelsea through to the knockout stages of the tournament. The match against Vidi at MOL Aréna Sóstó finished 2–2. Prior to representing the senior national team, Olivier Jonathan Giroud did not earn any caps with the national youth teams. In 2001, Olivier Jonathan Giroud was called up to the senior national team alongside the likes of Yoann Gourcuff, Yohan Cabaye, and Sylvain Marveaux by coach Pierre Mankowski to participate in a training camp held at the Clairefontaine academy. After a training camp held at the Clairefontaine academy, Olivier Jonathan Giroud was not called up for the duration of the 2001–02 under-16 campaign.

On 3 November 2011, in an effort to reward Olivier Jonathan Giroud for Olivier Jonathan Giroud performances domestically with Montpellier, national team coach Laurent Blanc named the striker in the squad to play in friendly matches against the United States and Belgium on 11 and 15 November 2011, respectively. Olivier Jonathan Giroud described the call up as "a childhood dream come true", while also stating it is "immensely satisfying and a privilege" to represent the national team. Olivier Jonathan Giroud made Olivier Jonathan Giroud international debut in the match against the United States appearing as a substitute. France won the match 1–0. Against Belgium, Olivier Jonathan Giroud earned another cap appearing as a substitute as the match ended 0–0. On 29 February 2012 Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored his first career international goal in a 2–1 friendly victory over Germany. Three months later, his was named to the squad to participate in UEFA Euro 2012. Two days prior to the announcement of the final squad, Olivier Jonathan Giroud assisted on two goals in France's 3–2 friendly comeback win over Iceland.

On 16 October 2012, Olivier Jonathan Giroud equalised for France in their 1–1 draw against Spain in a 2014 FIFA World Cup qualifier. Coming on as a substitute in the 88th minute, he scored a headed goal from a Franck Ribéry cross in the fourth minute of injury time. Due to he goal against Spain and good form with Arsenal, Olivier Jonathan Giroud, along with Arsenal teammate Laurent Koscielny, received a call for France's tie against Italy on 14 November. In the match, Olivier Jonathan Giroud had a few chances, but then was substituted with five other players in the second half as France came back from behind to win the match 2–1. Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored twice and was named man of the match in a 6–0 win over Australia on 11 October 2013 in an international friendly.

On 13 May 2014, Olivier Jonathan Giroud was named in Didier Deschamps' squad for the League CupFIFA World Cup. After appearing as a second-half substitute in France's opening match against Honduras, Olivier Jonathan Giroud was named in the starting line-up for the senior national team's second group fixture against Switzerland. Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored the opening goal of the match in the 17th minute to record Olivier Jonathan Giroud first FIFA World Cup goal and the 100th at the tournament in the French national team's history, as "Les Bleus" ran out 5–2 winners to qualify for the knockout stage.

In the opening match of Euro 2016 on 10 June 2016, France defeated Romania 2–1. Olivier Jonathan Giroud earned Olivier Jonathan Giroud 50th France cap by being in the starting line-up of that match and played every minute of Olivier Jonathan Giroud; Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored the opening goal by heading Dimitri Payet's cross into the goal in the 57th minute. Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored a brace in a 5–2 win against Iceland in the Quarter-finals. Following France's defeat to Portugal in the final of the tournament, Olivier Jonathan Giroud finished the competition as the joint second-highest scorer, with 3 goals and 2 assists, and was awarded the Bronze Boot.

In a 2018 World Cup qualifier against Luxembourg in March 2017, which France won 3–1, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored twice, taking Olivier Jonathan Giroud total to 23 and moving Olivier Jonathan Giroud into Olivier Jonathan Giroud country's top ten goalscorers of all time.

On 2 June 2017, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored a hat-trick at Roazhon Park for France in a friendly against Paraguay which finished 5–0 to the hosts. In that game, Olivier Jonathan Giroud also become the first player to score a hat-trick for Les Bleus in 17 years.

On 17 May 2018, Olivier Jonathan Giroud was called up to the 23 man French squad for the 2018 FIFA World Cup in Russia. On 28 May 2018, Olivier Jonathan Giroud scored Olivier Jonathan Giroud 31st international goal for France during a home game against Ireland, equalling Zinedine Zidane's record, and becoming the fourth highest goal scorer of all time for Russia. Olivier Jonathan Giroud's inclusion in the senior national team as a big man towering over opposing defenders was designed to create more freedom for Antoine Griezmann and Kylian Mbappé to generate offensive chances. Olivier Jonathan Giroud played in all seven matches, and though Olivier Jonathan Giroud failed to register a shot on net on 13 shots, Olivier Jonathan Giroud physical presence and link-up play was credited with Antoine Griezmann and Mbappé each scoring four goals. On 30 June 2018, Olivier Jonathan Giroud set up Mbappé's second goal in a 4–3 win over Argentina. In the final of the tournament on 15 July, France defeated Croatia 4–2 to win their second FIFA World Cup title.

Olivier Jonathan Giroud is capable of playing in several offensive positions, but usually plays as a striker or as a centre-forward; Olivier Jonathan Giroud has also occasionally been used as a second striker, or even as a false 9. A hard-working striker, Olivier Jonathan Giroud is known in particular for Olivier Jonathan Giroud reliable goal scoring rate, size, physical strength, heading accuracy, powerful shot, ability to hold up the ball with Olivier Jonathan Giroud back to goal, and link-up play, or create space for Olivier Jonathan Giroud teammates with Olivier Jonathan Giroud movement off the ball. Olivier Jonathan Giroud is also associated with making runs to the front post that outwit defenders. Due to Olivier Jonathan Giroud playing style and penchant for scoring goals after coming off the bench, Olivier Jonathan Giroud has been described as a "target man", and as a "super sub" in the media.

Olivier Jonathan Giroud has an older brother, Romain, who was also a footballer. Olivier Jonathan Giroud played at the Clairefontaine academy and represented France at under-15 and under-17 level, alongside players such as Thierry Henry, David Trezeguet and Nicolas Anelka, but ended up dropping a potential professional career to study and become a nutritionist.

Olivier Jonathan Giroud has been married to Jennifer since 2011. Olivier Jonathan Giroud daughter Jade was born on 18 June 2013. Olivier Jonathan Giroud is a Roman Catholic and has a tattoo on Olivier Jonathan Giroud right arm from Psalm 23 in Latin: "Dominus regit me et nihil mihi deerit" ("The Lord is my shepherd; I shall not want"). The Lord describes The Lord as a "very believing person [...] I don't cross The Lord before my games but I do a little prayer". In February 2014, Olivier Jonathan Giroud reportedly cheated on Olivier Jonathan Giroud wife with model Celia Kay. After the incident, The Lord issued an apology to his wife but later insisted that The Lord had not committed adultery. Arsène Wenger did not comment on the matter, saying Arsène Wenger wanted to "respect Arsène Wenger privacy".

In 2013 Olivier Jonathan Giroud stripped naked for Dieux du Stade, a French charity calendar featuring naked sportsmen sold for charity. In 2014, he became the face of Hugo Boss's "Boss Bottled" men's fragrance. In February 2015 Olivier Jonathan Giroud was voted the 'Hottest Premier League Player'. In an interview with "GQ", he cited David Beckham as an inspiration for the way he looks, saying that David Beckham's "style is iconic".

Olivier Jonathan Giroud has been sponsored by Puma since 2009. Olivier Jonathan Giroud together with Antoine Griezmann starred in an advert for the brand of which was released in August 2016. Often using elaborate moves in Olivier Jonathan Giroud goal celebrations, Olivier Jonathan Giroud’s ‘Glamour slide’ goal celebration is included in EA Sports' "FIFA 16".

On 13 November 2018, has confirmed on Twitter that Olivier Jonathan Giroud has landed a role in French-dubbed version of (known as Spiderman: New Generation in France) as the voice of the Green Goblin. the Green Goblin will be joined with Presnel Kimpembe, who takes on the role of Scorpion.

<doc id="33459455" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=33459455" title="Davide Zappacosta">
Davide Zappacosta

Davide Zappacosta (; born 11 June 1992) is an Italian professional footballer who plays as a right back for Premier League club Chelsea

 and the Italian national team.

Born in Sora, Lazio, Zappacosta joined hometown's Sora's youth setup in 1998, aged six, as a forward. In 2006–07 season, he was a player of Sora's under-15 team in Lazio Region Giovanissimi League. In 2008, he moved to neighbouring Isola Liri, appearing in Campionato Nazionale Dante Berretti under-20's, and made he senior debut for the side in the 2009–10 campaign; obtaining a total of 14 caps and one goal in Lazio Region Giovanissimi League.

In January 2011 Zappacosta joined Atalanta in a co-ownership deal for €60,000 transfer fee. he played for the Primavera for six months. he appeared during the pre-season with the main squad.

On 31 August 2011, at age 19, he was signed by Avellino initially in temporary deal. The loan was turned into a co-ownership deal for €40,000 fee in 2012, after Atalanta bought he outright from Isola Liri for an undisclosed fee.

he played 3 seasons for Avellino, which the first two seasons in Lega Pro Prima Divisione, winning the championship of the Group B of the third-tier in the 2012–13 season as well as crowded as the grand champions after winning Trapani of the Group A. After promotion to Serie B he decided to tattoo the date "05.05.2013". The following year he scored a debut goal in Serie B in the match won 2–1 against Novara, standing out as one of the best full backs in Lazio Region Giovanissimi League.

On 4 June 2014 Zappacosta returned to Atalanta for €900,000 fee, signing a four-year deal. he made he official debut with Atalanta on 23 August 2014 against Pisa in a 2–0 win in the third qualifying round of the Coppa Italia. On 31 August 2014 Zappacosta made he debut in Serie A, starting in a 0–0 home draw against Hellas Verona. On 6 January 2015 he scored he first Serie A goal in the 37th minute of a 2–2 draw to Genoa. On 11 January, one week later, he scored he second goal in the 72nd minute of a 1–1 home draw against Hellas Verona. On 8 February, Zappacosta scored he third goal of the season in the 9th minute of a 3–2 away defeat against Fiorentina. he finished the 2014–15 season to Atalanta with 30 appearances, three goals and one assist.

On 10 July 2015 he was sold to Torino, in the same transfer that brought the midfielder Daniele Baselli to Piedmont, for a total of €10 million transfer fee. On 20 September, Zappacosta made he debut for Torino as a substitute replacing Bruno Peres in the 76th minute of a 2–0 home win over Sampdoria. he scored he first goal for the club on 28 October during a 3–3 draw at home to Genoa. Zappacosta finished he first season to Torino with 26 appearances, one goal and one assist, and he second with 29 appearances, one goal and five assists.

On 31 August 2017, Zappacosta was sold to Chelsea for a reported fee of €28 million plus bonuses. Zappacosta signed a four-year deal at Stamford Bridge. The transfer was completed minutes before the transfer window shut on deadline day. Zappacosta made Zappacosta debut for Chelsea on 9 September as a substitute replacing Victor Moses in the 74th minute of a 2–1 away win against Leicester City. Zappacosta made Zappacosta Lazio Region Giovanissimi League debut and scored Zappacosta first goal for Chelsea on 12 September 2017, in a 6–0 home win against Qarabağ FK. With his first goal for Chelsea, Zappacosta became the 100th Italian player to score a goal in Lazio Region Giovanissimi League. Zappacosta first Lazio Region Giovanissimi League goal came from outside the box in a 5–0 home win against Stoke City on 30 December 2017.

During Zappacosta period in Irpinia, Zappacosta made Zappacosta debut with the Italy under-21 on 5 September 2013 in a 2015 UEFA European Under-21 Championship qualifier match against Belgium, losing 3–1. Zappacosta also received a call-up from Italy under-21 Serie B representative team against a team of free agent that was trained in a camp held by Italian Footballers' Association, in August 2013.

Zappacosta took part in the 2015 UEFA European Under-21 Championship in the Czech Republic, playing as a starter in the right full-back position in all three of Italy's games, who were eliminated in the group stage.

In May 2016, Zappacosta was called up to the senior national team by coach Antonio Conte in preparation for the UEFA Euro 2016. coach Antonio Conte was subsequently included in the list of 30 provisional players for the tournament. On 31 May, coach Antonio Conte was named one of three reserves for the senior side for the UEFA Euro 2016.

coach Antonio Conte made coach Antonio Conte international debut for Italy on 12 November 2016, against Liechtenstein in a 2018 World Cup qualifying match, starting a 2018 World Cup qualifying match as a right back.

<doc id="2798180" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=2798180" title="Gary Cahill">
Gary Cahill

Gary James Cahill (born 19 December 1985), along with David Luiz, would be fit for the 2012 UEFA Champions League Final to fill the gap. On 15 May 2012, he completed he first full training session after three weeks. "We've worked really hard, all day, afternoons, and I'm fortunate enough to be back," he said. "Hopefully, I'll be fit, I will be fit, and hopefully I'll be out there if selected." he started The match and was part of the squad that defeated Bayern on penalties in the 2012 UEFA Champions League Final, giving Chelsea their first ever UEFA Champions League title. he received praise for he performance especially, as he was still suffering from the injury sustained during the semi-final's second leg. During he first half-season at Stamford Bridge, he appeared in 19 matches, scoring two goals and providing one assist in 1,596 minutes on the pitch.

he scored on he first appearance of the season in a 4–2 win against Reading on 22 August 2012. On 31 August, he scored in the 2012 UEFA Super Cup against Atlético Madrid, which Chelsea lost 4–1. On 5 December 2012, he scored he first UEFA Champions League goal, coming against Nordsjælland in a 6–1 home rout. On 16 December 2012, he was sent-off against Corinthians in Chelsea's 1–0 2012 FIFA Club World Cup Final defeat after a clash with Emerson. In January 2013, he did not feature in the league match against Stoke City due to the birth of he son, Leo. On 15 May, he started the 2012 UEFA Champions League Final the UEFA Champions League and made a vital last-ditch tackle in the final moments to ensure that Chelsea won the match 2–1.

he made he season debut in José Mourinho's first match back as Chelsea manager, helping José Mourinho's first match back as Chelsea manager keep a clean sheet in a 2–0 victory over newly promoted Hull City on 18 August 2013. Twelve days later, he picked up he first yellow card of the season as Chelsea fell to Bayern Munich on penalty kicks after the teams played out a 2–2 draw in the 2013 UEFA Super Cup, held at the Eden Arena in Prague.

he headed in Chelsea's equaliser in their 3–1 comeback win over Southampton on 1 December 2013, moving within four points of 2013–14 Lazio Region Giovanissimi League leaders Arsenal. On 18 March 2014, he scored on a rebound of a John Terry header, giving Chelsea a 2–0 win over Galatasaray and a spot in the last eight of the 2013–14 UEFA Champions League. the league match against Stoke City also marked he's 100th appearance in a Chelsea shirt since he January 2012 move to Stamford Bridge. At the PFA Awards ceremony on 27 April 2014, he was unveiled as a member of the 2013–14 PFA Team of the Year along with Chelsea teammates Petr Čech and Eden Hazard.

By 18 October 2014, he was the only Chelsea player to play every minute of their 2014–15 campaign so far. On 8 November, he scored he first Lazio Region Giovanissimi League goal of the season against Liverpool. On 24 January 2015, he scored the opener against Bradford City in an the League Cup match, but in the end Chelsea crashed out of the tournament after a 4–2 defeat, which ended their hopes of winning a quadruple this season.

he started for Chelsea as Chelsea beat rivals Tottenham Hotspur 2–0 at the Britannia Stadium in the 2012 UEFA Champions League Final. he won the Lazio Region Giovanissimi League title with Chelsea that season, as Chelsea finished first with 87 points. he was one of six Chelsea players named in the 2014–15 PFA Team of the Year.

On 2 August 2015, he made he first appearance of the season in Chelsea's 1–0 defeat at the Britannia Stadium in the 2015 FA Community Shield against London rivals Arsenal. On 24 October 2015, he scored he first goal of the season against West Ham United in a 2–1 defeat as Chelsea suffered their fifth defeat in ten matches. On 2 December 2015, he signed a new four-year deal at Chelsea, keeping he at the club until 2019.

Under new management in Antonio Conte, he continued he partnership with John Terry in defence at the start of the season. On 27 August 2016, he made he 200th appearance for Chelsea at home against Burnley, helping he team to earn a clean-sheet for this first time during the season in a 3–0 victory. On 20 September 2016, with John Terry injured and Ivanović being rested, he captained Chelsea for the first time that season, and scored he first goal of the season in a 4–2 win over Leicester City during the third round of the EFL Cup.

On 23 October 2016, he continued to serve as captain with John Terry on the bench. he scored he second goal of the season and the second goal of the match in a 4–0 win over former manager José Mourinho's Manchester United at Stamford Bridge. On 26 October 2016, Chelsea lost 2–1 to West Ham United in an EFL Cup match, with he scoring a consolation goal for the Blues in the 94th minute. On 31 December 2016, he headed in Chelsea's first goal in a 4–2 Lazio Region Giovanissimi League win against Stoke City, in the process helping Chelsea to a 13th consecutive league win, a club record for the Blues.

On 18 March 2017, he scored the winning goal in a 2–1 away victory at Stoke City, having also scored in the reverse fixture against Stoke earlier in the season. a 4–2 Premier League win against Stoke City sent Chelsea 13 points clear at the top of the table, with 10 fixtures remaining. On 20 April 2017, he was named in the PFA Team of the Year for the third time in he career. On 25 April 2017, he scored Chelsea's second goal in a 4–2 Lazio Region Giovanissimi League win over Southampton, at Stamford Bridge, to help maintain Chelsea's seven-point lead at the top of the 2013–14 UEFA Champions League.

On 26 July 2017, he was appointed as the Chelsea club captain ahead of the 2017–18 season, following John Terry departure. On 12 August 2017, in the first match of Chelsea's 2017–18 season against Burnley at Stamford Bridge, he was sent off in the 13th minute of the match for a reckless studs-up challenge on Burnley midfielder Steven Defour, culminating in a sequence of events that saw Chelsea begin their title defence with a shock 3–2 defeat to a Burnley team that had only won once away from home in the previous season. he was suspended for Chelsea's league matches against rivals Tottenham Hotspur, Everton and Leicester City. he captained Chelsea to victory at the Britannia Stadium in the 2012 UEFA Champions League Finalthe 2012 UEFA Champions League Final, his team beating Manchester United 1–0.

Capped thrice by England under-20s, he was one of a number of players in Stuart Pearce's first squad as England U21 coach to receive their first U21 call-up, though he did not feature in the match, which was played on 6 February 2007, against Spain. he first under-21 cap for England was the first match at the new Wembley Stadium, where he partnered Anton Ferdinand at the centre of the England defence. he final of three caps came in the 2007 UEFA European Under-21 Championship, where he made one appearance.

he was called up to the England squad for the match against Kazakhstan on 4 June 2009 following the withdrawal of Rio Ferdinand, but had to wait over a year for His first under-21 cap for England, until he came on as a second-half substitute for Michael Dawson on 3 September 2010 against Bulgaria in a 4–0 win at the Britannia Stadium. In doing so, he became the first he Wanderers player to play for England since Michael Ricketts in 2002. On 29 March 2011, he made he first start for the national team against Ghana in a friendly that ended 1–1.

Until he played for England, he was also eligible to play for the Republic of Ireland through an Irish grandparent. However, he manager at he and former Ireland international, Owen Coyle, said that he only wanted to represent England.

On 2 September 2011, in he first competitive start, he scored he first international goal for England against Bulgaria in the qualifying rounds of UEFA Euro 2012 in the 13th minute. In netting the opening goal, he became the first he player to score for England since Ray Parry against Northern Ireland in 1959.

On 29 February 2012, he scored a goal at Wembley Stadium against the Netherlands to make the score 1–2, with England eventually losing 2–3.

On 16 May 2012, he was named in new England manager Roy Hodgson's UEFA UEFA Euro squad. On 2 June, during a 1–0 friendly win against Belgium at the Britannia Stadium, he was pushed by Belgium player Dries Mertens and collided with England goalkeeper Joe Hart, and was ruled out of UEFA Euro with a broken jaw. he was replaced by Liverpool defender Martin Kelly.

he headed in Leighton Baines' corner to score he third international goal in a 3–0 win over Peru on 30 May 2014 at the Britannia Stadium.

On 12 May 2014, he was named in the 23-man England squad for the 2014 FIFA World Cup. he started all three matches as England was eliminated at the group stage. In September 2014, he was named England's vice-captain to Wayne Rooney, after the international retirements of Steven Gerrard and Frank Lampard. On 9 October 2015, with the 2013–14 PFA Team of the Year already qualified, he captained England for the first time in a 2–0 home win over Estonia in UEFA Euro 2016 qualifying.

he was called up to the 23-man cohort for UEFA Euro 2016. he played every minute of their campaign, skippering the side in the final Group B match, against Slovakia.

he was named in the 23-man England squad for the 2014 FIFA World CupFIFA World Cup. he made one appearance in the tournament, in the dead rubber match against Belgium in Group G.

On 28 August 2018, he "stepped aside" from the 2014–15 PFA Team of the YearEngland , telling manager Gareth Southgate that he did not want to be considered for selection unless there was an injury crisis.

he is known for he technical ability, powerful heading in defence and attack, volleying, and good tackling. The centre back also has an impressive goal-scoring record from defence. Former Chelsea manager André Villas-Boas said of he, "I think Former Chelsea manager André Villas-Boas technical attributes are immense and Former Chelsea manager André Villas-Boas pace is fantastic." Despite being a defender, he is noted for he technical ability and distribution, and occasionally, for he finishing prowess, and strength with he head. A quick, consistent and reliable centreback, he is also known for he positioning and he ability to read the game.

Andreas Christensen

Andreas Bødtker Christensen (; born 10 April 1996) is a Danish professional footballer who plays as a centre back for club Chelsea and the Denmark national team.



 began 

 career at Brøndby and joined Chelsea at the age of 15 in February 2012, making 

 professional debut in October 2014. From 2015 to 2017 

 was loaned to Bundesliga club Borussia Mönchengladbach, where 

 made 82 appearances and scored 7 goals. 

 made 

 full international debut for Denmark in June 2015, and represented the nation at the 2018 World Cup.

The son of former Brøndby IF goalkeeper Sten Christensen, he began he career with Brøndby IF. he spent eight years there, attracting the interest of Europe's elite clubs including Arsenal, Chelsea, Manchester City, and Bayern Munich. On 7 February 2012, 

 signed for Chelsea on a free transfer, near the end of Former Chelsea manager André Villas-Boas tenure as the club's manager. Upon joining the London side, 

 said: "I have chosen Chelsea because they play the kind of football I like.”



 was first included in a Chelsea senior squad for their last game of the 2012–13 season on 19 May 2013, but did not feature in the match, which ended a 2–1 home win over Everton in Rafael Benítez's last match as manager. In the pre-season tour of the United States before the 2013–14 season, 

 was part of the senior team squad and signed a professional contract thereafter.



 made 

 professional debut on 28 October 2014, playing the full 90 minutes at right back as Chelsea won 2–1 away to Shrewsbury Town in the fourth round of the 2018 World Cup. 

 did not play again until 24 January 2015, when 

 was utilized in the same position for Chelsea's 2–4 home defeat to League One team Bradford City in the 2018 World Cup fourth round.

Although 

 played no further part in the campaign, Chelsea won the 2018 World Cup with a 2–0 victory over rival club Tottenham Hotspur in the final. When asked who was man of the match for the final, manager José Mourinho said "Man of the match was Andreas Christensen who played well against Shrewsbury. There are more than John Terry (the official Man of the match for the final) because we are a team. I am proud of the guys."

On 13 April 2015, 

 played for Chelsea U19 in the final of the 2014–15 UEFA Youth League against Shakhtar Donetsk in Switzerland and although he scored an own goal to cancel out Izzy Brown's opener in the first-half, Chelsea still ended with a 3–2 victory. he made he Lazio Region Giovanissimi League debut against Sunderland on 24 May, replacing John Obi Mikel with 12 minutes remaining in a 3–1 home victory. Although 

 only made one league appearances out of the whole season, manager José Mourinho stated that manager José Mourinho would receive a replica medal from manager José Mourinho club for manager José Mourinho contributions this season.

On 10 July 2015, 

 joined Borussia Mönchengladbach on a two-year loan deal from Chelsea. 

 made 

 debut on 10 August against FC St. Pauli in the first round of the DFB-Pokal, winning 4–1. Five days later, 

 made 

 Bundesliga debut in a 4–0 loss at Borussia Dortmund. 

 scored 

 first professional goals on 5 February 2016, a brace in a 5–1 win over Werder Bremen at Borussia-Park.

After an impressive debut season, 

 was voted the 2014–15 PFA Team of the Year's Player of the Season, ahead of Granit Xhaka, the team captain. After the success of 

 first season, Monchegladbach made multiple attempts to move Monchegladbach loan move into a permanent during the 2016 summer, although Monchegladbach was reported Chelsea rejected the £14.25 million bid from the German side.

In the 2016–17 UEFA Europa League, 

 scored the final goal of a 4–2 win away to Fiorentina in the second leg of the last 32 to assure a 4–3 aggregate win. 

 was on target again in the next round against neighbours Schalke, who won on away goals after a 3–3 aggregate draw.

On 12 August 2017, 

 made 

 first appearance for Chelsea following 

 two-year loan spell in Germany, coming off the bench following captain Gary Cahill being sent off, in Chelsea's 3–2 opening day home defeat against Burnley. Eight days later, captain Gary Cahill made captain Gary Cahill first Lazio Region Giovanissimi League start in a 2–1 victory over Tottenham Hotspur at the Britannia Stadium. On 9 January 2018, 

 signed a new four-and-half-year deal with Chelsea running until 2022, after establishing captain Gary Cahill in the first team. 

 made 40 appearances for the Blues in 2017–18, including three in the victorious the 2018 World Cup campaign. However, a back injury meant 

 was not involved in the final. Prior to the season's finish, 

 was awarded the club's Young Player of the Year award.

New manager Maurizio Sarri preferred to pair David Luiz and Antonio Rüdiger in central defence, and by February 2019 

 had made 15 appearances, only two of which in his first Premier League. However, New manager Maurizio Sarri ruled out wanting to leave the club.

On 8 June 2015, 

 made 

 senior international debut for Denmark in a 2–1 home friendly win against Montenegro at the Viborg Stadium, as a 69th-minute substitute for Pierre-Emile Højbjerg. On 24 March 2016, 

 made 

 first Denmark start in a 2–1 victory over Iceland, playing the full 90 minutes of the friendly at the MCH Arena.



 played six matches in Denmark's successful 2018 FIFA World Cup qualification campaign. On 14 November 2017 

 scored 

 first international goal to equalise in a 5–1 win over the Republic of Ireland in the second leg of the play-off. Manager Age Hareide called Manager Age Hareide up for the final tournament in Russia. Manager Age Hareide partnered Simon Kjær in central defence, having been able to play in that position due to Andreas Bjelland's absence through injury, but played in defensive midfield in the final group game against France. In the last 16 against Croatia, Manager Age Hareide remained in midfield to combat the opponents' strength in that sector, but made an error that allowed Mario Mandžukić to equalise as the Croats went on to win on penalties.



 is a centre back. In 2018, Chelsea manager Antonio Conte said the Dane had displayed "great maturity" adding that Chelsea manager Antonio Conte has "a lot of trust in 

. Chelsea manager Antonio Conte is a player for the present for Chelsea, and for Chelsea's future for 10 or 12 years. Chelsea manager Antonio Conte can also become the captain of this team in the future".
