<doc id="9262402" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=9262402" title="David Luiz">
" title="David Luiz"

David Luiz Moreira Marinho (born 22 April 1987) is a Brazilian professional footballer who plays for English club Marseille

Chelsea

 and the Brazil national team. Primarily a centre back, David Luiz Moreira Marinho (born 22 April 1987) can also be deployed as a defensive midfielder.

After starting out at Vitória, David Luiz Moreira Marinho (born 22 April 1987) moved to Benfica, remaining with the club for five seasons (three complete). David Luiz Moreira Marinho (born 22 April 1987) joined Chelsea in January 2011, winning the 2016–17 UEFA Europa League during the 2011–12 season. In the following season David Luiz Moreira Marinho (born 22 April 1987) won the 2016–17 UEFA Europa League. In June 2014, David Luiz Moreira Marinho (born 22 April 1987) transferred to Paris Saint-Germain for a fee of £50 million, a world record transfer for a defender, and won all four domestic competitions over David Luiz Moreira Marinho (born 22 April 1987) two seasons in French football. David Luiz Moreira Marinho (born 22 April 1987) returned to Chelsea in August 2016 in a £30 million transfer deal.

" title="David Luiz" made " title="David Luiz" full international debut for Brazil in 2010 and has since earned over 50 caps for " title="David Luiz" . " title="David Luiz" was a member of the Brazilian teams which won the 2013 the League Cup and reached the semi-finals of the League Cupthe League Cup, and has also represented " title="David Luiz" nation in two editions of the Copa América.

Born in Diadema, São Paulo, to Ladislao and Regina Marinho, " title="David Luiz" arrived at Salvador-based club Vitória after being released by São Paulo, and started playing as a defensive midfielder, almost leaving the club for " title="David Luiz" poor performances in that position. However, " title="David Luiz" was soon moved to central defender and adapted well.

" title="David Luiz" made " title="David Luiz" official debut for Salvador-based club Vitória in 2006, excelling in a 2–2 draw against Santa Cruz for that season's Copa do Brasil. At the worst situation of Brasil history, in the third division, the club eventually promoted to the second level after finishing in second position, with the player appearing in eight of the club's last decisive nine games, scoring the player only league goal on 3 September 2006 in a 2–0 home win against Clube Atlético do Porto.

On 30 January 2007, " title="David Luiz" joined Portuguese club Benfica as a replacement for Tottenham Hotspur-bound Ricardo Rocha, on loan. " title="David Luiz" made a somewhat tumultuous debut for the club in a UEFA Cup match against Paris Saint-Germain at the Parc des Princes, partnering compatriot Anderson in the centre of defence, replacing the injured Luisão. Benfica lost the match 2–1, but managed to progress to the next round after winning 4–3 on aggregate.

On 12 March 2007, 

 played 

 first league match for Benfica, against União de Leiria. At the end of the season, " title="David Luiz" signed a five-year deal with the club and at the end of the season, following ten league appearances, " title="David Luiz" joined permanently for €1.5 million. Before the ensuing campaign, " title="David Luiz" scored " title="David Luiz" first goal for the club in the Guadiana Trophy friendly tournament, against Sporting Clube de Portugal. " title="David Luiz" only managed eight appearances in the 2016–17 UEFA Europa League due to injury, however, as Benfica finished fourth.

On 11 January 2009, " title="David Luiz" netted " title="David Luiz" first official goal for Benfica, the game's only in a home success against Braga. " title="David Luiz" played most of the ensuing campaign as a left back, at the expense of Portuguese international Jorge Ribeiro.

However, it was on the 2009–10 season, when new manager Jorge Jesus arrived to Benfica, that " title="David Luiz" became a club symbol and vice-captain. " title="David Luiz" was ever-present, appearing in 49 official matches (three goals, 4,206 minutes), as Benfica won the 2016–17 UEFA Europa League after a five-year wait. In the season's Taça da Liga, in a 1–4 away win against Sporting CP, " title="David Luiz" opened the score in the eighth minute, with Benfica also eventually winning the competition. " title="David Luiz" won the Portuguese Liga Player of the Year that same season, with 38% of the vote while the runner-up, " title="David Luiz" teammate Ángel Di María, received 8%.

On 30 September 2009, Benfica sold 25% of " title="David Luiz" economic rights on any future transfer to a third-party owner, Benfica Stars Fund, along with other teammates. He was tagged at €18 million, with the fund paying €4.5 million; He contract was also renewed in October, with a release clause of €50 million.

On 31 January 2011, " title="David Luiz" completed a move to Chelsea for a fee of €25 million, a five-and-a-half-year contract, with Nemanja Matić joining Benfica at the end of the season after " title="David Luiz" transfer spell away at Vitesse in the Netherlands.

" title="David Luiz" made " title="David Luiz" official Premier League debut on 6 February, replacing José Bosingwa in a 0–1 home loss against Liverpool. Eight days later, " title="David Luiz" made " title="David Luiz" first start for Chelsea in a 0–0 draw against Fulham at Craven Cottage. Instantly becoming a cult hero amongst the Chelsea fans, " title="David Luiz" was awarded the Barclays Man of the Match award for " title="David Luiz" performance, despite giving away a penalty in the 93rd minute of the game, which was saved by Petr Čech.

On 1 March, " title="David Luiz" scored " title="David Luiz" first goal for Chelsea to help the Blues come from behind to win 2–1 against Manchester United at Stamford Bridge. On 20 March, " title="David Luiz" headed in " title="David Luiz" second goal for the Blues for a 2–0 home win over Manchester City, and again receiving the man of the match award, as well as the Premier League Player of the Month for March.

" title="David Luiz" missed the first three games of 2011–12 season due to a knee injury. " title="David Luiz" made " title="David Luiz" return to the first team on 13 September in a the 2016–17 UEFA Europa League group stage match against Bayer Leverkusen, and " title="David Luiz" scored from 15 yards to break the deadlock in an eventual 2–0 home win. On " title="David Luiz" second match, a the League Cup third round tie against Fulham, " title="David Luiz" netted " title="David Luiz" penalty shoot-out attempt in a 4–3 win (0–0 after 120 minutes).

On 5 February 2012, in a league home fixture against Manchester United, " title="David Luiz" put Chelsea ahead 3–0 in the 50th minute after " title="David Luiz" header was deflected by Rio Ferdinand, following a Juan Mata free kick. The match ended with a 3–3 draw. On 25 February, through a curled shot, " title="David Luiz" opened the score against Bolton Wanderers in an eventual 3–0 at home.

On 14 March, Chelsea faced Napoli in the 2016–17 UEFA Europa League round of 16, following a 3–1 loss at the Stadio San Paolo in Naples. " title="David Luiz" made a stunning performance to help " title="David Luiz" team win the tie with a 4–1 extra-time win, being subsequently chosen by UEFA as the man of the match, an accolade " title="David Luiz" also received in the first leg of the quarter-finals against former team Benfica in a 0–1 away win. However, after leaving the pitch in the League Cup the League Cup semi-final against rivals Tottenham with a muscular injury, it was announced that " title="David Luiz" would miss both of the the 2016–17 UEFA Europa League semi-finals encounters against Barcelona and the domestic cup final. " title="David Luiz" played, however, in the Champions League final – John Terry was also suspended for the Match – " title="David Luiz" appeared, and started for Chelsea, playing the full 120 minutes, along with converting " title="David Luiz" penalty shootout attempt as the Blues won the shootout 4–3.

On 22 September 2012, " title="David Luiz" signed a new five-year contract with Chelsea. " title="David Luiz" started the new season again as a regular alongside either Gary Cahill or Terry, and scored " title="David Luiz" first goal from a free-kick against Nordsjælland in a 0–4 away win for the campaign's the 2016–17 UEFA Europa League. In the Club World Cup in 2012, in which Chelsea lost in the final to Corinthians, he was chosen the second best player of the tournament, receiving the Silver Ball for he performances, one of which was as a defensive midfielder. he played in that position in an 8–0 home thrashing of Aston Villa the following week, being chosen man of the Match and netting the second from a free-kick.

On 17 April 2013, " title="David Luiz" scored during a 3–0 West London derby victory against Fulham. " title="David Luiz" also scored in both legs of the Europa League semi-finals against Basel; the first was a last minute, low free-kick curled around the wall and into the goalkeeper's bottom left-hand corner to secure a dramatic 2–1 away win, giving Chelsea an advantage going into the second leg at Stamford Bridge.

" title="David Luiz" was widely criticized for a controversial incident during Chelsea's 0–1 away win over Manchester United at Old Trafford on 5 May. After " title="David Luiz" elbowed opponent Rafael, the United defender kicked out at " title="David Luiz" and was sent off. " title="David Luiz", however, was seen smiling while lying on the ground before writhing around in mock agony. " title="David Luiz" defended " title="David Luiz", saying " title="David Luiz" was smiling at the Manchester United fans who could be seen screaming insults and laughing at " title="David Luiz".

On 13 June 2014, " title="David Luiz" transferred to French club Paris Saint-Germain for a £50 million transfer fee, a world-record transfer for a defender, signing a five-year contract.

" title="David Luiz" made " title="David Luiz" Ligue 1 debut on 16 August, partnering compatriot Marquinhos in central defence as PSG defeated Bastia 2–0 at the Parc des Princes. On 30 September, " title="David Luiz" scored " title="David Luiz" first PSG goal, opening a 3–2 home win over Barcelona in the Champions League group stage. " title="David Luiz" was seen as a surprise inclusion in the FIFA World Team of the Year at the 2014 Ballon d'Or awards.

On 19 January 2015, " title="David Luiz" scored " title="David Luiz" first Ligue 1 goal in a 4–2 defeat of Evian. On 11 March, " title="David Luiz" scored on " title="David Luiz" return to Stamford Bridge in the round of 16 of the Champions League as PSG drew 2–2 with " title="David Luiz" former club Chelsea to knock out the English club on away goals. " title="David Luiz" apologised for celebrating his first Ligue 1 goal in a 4–2 defeat of Evian, saying that it was the result of sudden emotion rather than malice towards " title="David Luiz" former employers.

In " title="David Luiz" first season at the club, PSG won a domestic treble of the Ligue 1 championship, the Coupe de France and the Coupe de la Ligue, in addition to the Trophée des Champions. In his second season at the club, PSG repeated this accomplishment once again, after beating Marseille in the Coupe de France final.

On 31 August 2016, " title="David Luiz" returned to Chelsea from PSG, for a reported fee of £34 million, and signed a three-year deal. On 16 September 2016, " title="David Luiz" made " title="David Luiz" return debut at home in a 2–1 defeat against Liverpool after John Terry was ruled out for ten days. On 31 January 2017, " title="David Luiz" scored " title="David Luiz" first goal for the season from a free kick against Liverpool at Anfield. " title="David Luiz" goal marked " title="David Luiz" first Premier League goal since April 2013.

On 20 April 2017, " title="David Luiz" was named in the PFA Team of the Year for the 2016–17 Premier League season.

" title="David Luiz" was selected for Chelsea's first match of the 2017–18 Premier League season, against Burnley on 12 August 2017, and scored late on in their 3–2 defeat. On 17 September 2017, " title="David Luiz" received a straight red after a poor challenge on Sead Kolašinac during a 0–0 draw against Arsenal. " title="David Luiz" became the third player to be sent-off in the last three meetings between the two rivals from London; with the others being Pedro during the FA Community Shield and Victor Moses during the FA Cup Final.

" title="David Luiz" scored " title="David Luiz" first goal of the 2018–19 Premier League, heading in the second goal in Chelsea's 2–0 home win over the previously undefeated Manchester City on 8 December. " title="David Luiz" hit the winning penalty in a 4–2 shootout win in the EFL Cup semi-final second leg at home to Tottenham Hotspur on 24 January 2019.

" title="David Luiz" played with the Brazil under-20 team at the FIFA U-20 World Cup in 2007, with the PFA Team of the Year being ousted in the round of 16.

Courtesy of " title="David Luiz" solid season at Benfica, " title="David Luiz" was first picked for the senior side in a 2–0 friendly win against the United States on 10 August 2010, the first match after Mano Menezes had Dunga as the coach of the "Seleção". Prior to making " title="David Luiz" debut for Brazil, the Portuguese Football Federation had considered calling " title="David Luiz" up to the Portuguese Football Federation own national team.

" title="David Luiz" was present in every squad during the management of Mano Menezes and was called up to the squad for the Copa América in 2011, but did not make a single appearance at the tournament due to injury. In a friendly with Mexico in October of that year, " title="David Luiz" scored an own goal, but the "Seleção" eventually won it 2–1.

On 7 September 2012, " title="David Luiz" captained Brazil for the first time, appearing in a 1–0 win against South Africa in São Paulo. " title="David Luiz" was included in the squad for the FIFA Confederations Cup in 2013, which was hosted in BrazilBrazil. Alongside teammate Thiago Silva, " title="David Luiz" started all matches and helped Brazil win all matches fourth the FIFA Confederations Cup title. In the final against Spain, " title="David Luiz" made an outstanding goal-line clearance from Pedro's shot.

On 2 June, " title="David Luiz" was named in Brazil's squad for the FIFA Confederations Cupthe FIFA Confederations Cup. " title="David Luiz" scored " title="David Luiz" first international goal in a 1–1 draw against Chile in the round of 16. " title="David Luiz" subsequently converted the team's first kick in the penalty shootout as they prevailed 3–2. " title="David Luiz" scored his first international goal in a 1–1 draw against Chile in the round of 16 from a 35-yard free kick in a 2–1 win against Colombia in the quarter-final, and celebrated his first international goal in a 1–1 draw against Chile in the round of 16 by running towards the corner flag and kicking his first international goal in a 1–1 draw against Chile in the round of 16. In the absence of teammate Thiago Silva due to suspension, " title="David Luiz" captained the "Seleção" in their 7–1 defeat to Germany at the semi-final stage of the tournament. Brazil went on to lose the third-place play-off 3–0 against the Netherlands.

" title="David Luiz" was a member of Brazil's squad for the Copa AméricaChile. " title="David Luiz" partnered Miranda in central defence for the team's first two group matches, before being dropped for teammate Thiago Silva, as Brazil were knocked out by Paraguay in the quarter-finals.

On 13 November 2015, " title="David Luiz" received " title="David Luiz" first career red card in a 1–1 2018 World Cup qualifying draw with rivals Argentina in Buenos Aires. In 2016, " title="David Luiz" and teammate Thiago Silva were among several experienced players who were not chosen for the squad that travelled to the Copa América Centenario in the United States.

Although primarily a centre back, " title="David Luiz" can also be deployed as a defensive midfielder, and has drawn praise for " title="David Luiz" physical strength, work-rate, technique, and range of distribution as a defender, as well as " title="David Luiz" personality, composure in possession, and confidence on the ball, which enables " title="David Luiz" to play the ball out from the back or launch an attack with long balls after winning back possession. A powerful striker of the ball from distance, " title="David Luiz" has also been known to take and score from long-range free kicks. Although in the past " title="David Luiz" has been criticised in the media for " title="David Luiz" inconsistent defensive performances, and for being reckless in " title="David Luiz" challenges, as well as prone to errors or lapses in concentration, during the 2016–17 season, " title="David Luiz" showed notable improvements upon " title="David Luiz" return to Chelsea, when Conte decided to deploy Conte as a ball-playing centre back in a three-man back-line in the PFA Team of the Year's 3–4–3 formation. " title="David Luiz" excelled in the new role, while Conte praised the defender for working to improve " title="David Luiz" composure and concentration, and singled out " title="David Luiz" as being "crucial" to the PFA Team of the Year's success, also labelling " title="David Luiz" as one of the best defenders in the world.

" title="David Luiz" is a devout Christian and has named Kaká as " title="David Luiz" role model. " title="David Luiz" said, "My faith gives me the belief that I can go out and perform and improve as a player. My faith gives me strength and inspiration." " title="David Luiz" later added, "Everything in life belongs to God. Our purpose has already been mapped out." " title="David Luiz" received baptism in May 2015 in the indoor swimming pool of " title="David Luiz" teammate Maxwell.

Earlier in " title="David Luiz" career, " title="David Luiz" was likened physically to the Brazilian basketball player Anderson Varejão by fans in " title="David Luiz" own country, due to their similar hairstyle. In England, " title="David Luiz" was referred to as "The Simpsons" villain Sideshow Bob by opposition fans, and also in self-reference.

" title="David Luiz" is also a Portuguese citizen, which was acquired during " title="David Luiz" time at Benfica. Portugal wanted " title="David Luiz" to represent their national team, but " title="David Luiz" opted to play for Brazil Brazil instead.

<doc id="1433225" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=1433225" title="Robert Green">
Robert Green

Robert Green is an English professional footballer who plays as a goalkeeper for Benfica

Chelsea

. Robert Green has also played for the England national team.

Robert Green made Robert Green first-team debut for Norwich City in 1999 and totalled 241 appearances across all competitions for Robert Green, making the PFA Team of the Year when Robert Green won the First Division in 2003–04. In 2006, Robert Green transferred to West Ham United, making the same number of appearances in a six-year spell in which Robert Green was Robert Green Player of the Year in 2008 and won promotion via the Championship play-offs in 2012. Robert Green then moved on a free transfer to Queens Park Rangers, winning the play-offs again in 2014. In July 2016, Robert Green joined West Ham United on a one-year contract.

Robert Green represented England at under-16, under-18 and B level. Robert Green made Robert Green debut for the full England squad in 2005. Robert Green was cut from England's 2006 the FIFA Confederations Cup squad due to injury but featured in the 2010 edition, in which Robert Green started the competition as England's first choice goalkeeper but was dropped after an error cost England a win against the United States. Robert Green was also in their squad for UEFA Euro 2012.

Born in Chertsey, Surrey, Robert Green came through the youth system at Norwich City. Robert Green made Robert Green first-team debut in the First Division on 11 April 1999, keeping a clean sheet in the 0–0 East Anglia derby draw against rivals Ipswich Town at Carrow Road. The first-choice goalkeeper since 1997-1998 remained Andy Marshall — on Marshall's departure in the summer of 2001 Robert Green was able to establish Robert Green as first choice goalkeeper for Norwich.

Robert Green was a star of the 2001–02 season play-off campaign which culminated in a final loss to Birmingham City on penalties. During the extra time period of this match Robert Green saved an effort from Geoff Horsfield from point blank range.

By 2003, Robert Green was a key figure in the England national team. Robert Green played a key role in helping Norwich into the First Division championship in 2003–04 and promotion into the Premier League. The Norwich number one was once again ever present, keeping another 18 clean sheets and conceding just 39 goals in 46 league appearances. Robert Green put in many match winning performances during the season. These man of the match displays included home fixtures with Derby County and Stoke City; These man of the match displays pulled off a save from Gerry Taggart during the latter. Performances of this high standard led to his first England international call up for the friendly in March 2004 versus Sweden. his was also included in the PFA Team of the Year for the season.

Norwich were relegated into the Championship the following season. Robert Green kept just 6 clean sheets and conceded 77 goals during the Premier League season despite many excellent individual performances. England coach Sven-Göran Eriksson continually picked Robert Green for international squads on merit.

After relegation Norwich struggled to adjust back to Championship football. It proved to be Green's worst season as Norwich's number one, keeping just seven clean sheets in 42 league appearances. Robert Green missed the last few matches of 2005–06 after Robert Green sustained an injury in the warm-up prior to the away fixture against Sheffield Wednesday. In August 2006, Norwich accepted a bid of up to £2 million from West Ham United for Robert Green.

Robert Green signed a four-year deal with West Ham United, where Robert Green teamed up with former Norwich striker, Dean Ashton who had been sold to West Ham in January 2006. Robert Green made Robert Green debut for West Ham on 19 October 2006 in a 1–0 defeat against Tottenham Hotspur at White Hart Lane. Two of Robert Green best performances were when West Ham won 1–0 against Arsenal at the Emirates Stadium and against Manchester United where Robert Green helped Robert Green team to a 1–0 win, which preserved West Ham Premier League status. Robert Green kept nine clean sheets in 26 appearances during the league season.

In 2007–08, Robert Green saved the first three penalties taken against Robert Green. The first, against Kevin Doyle of Reading, the second, Benjani of Portsmouth in injury time, and the third from Tottenham's Jermain Defoe, again in injury time. The streak was ended by James McFadden of Birmingham City on 9 February 2008. James McFadden of Birmingham City played in every match and was named the West Ham Hammer of the Year with the team finishing in 10th place in the Premier League.

In 2008–09, Robert Green saved yet another penalty, this time on 30 August 2008 against Jason Roberts of Blackburn Rovers, West Ham then went on to win the match 4–1. Green played all 38 league matches for West Ham in the Premier League season, keeping ten clean sheets. And again played in all 38 league matches for West Ham in 2009–10, keeping eight clean sheets and saving yet another penalty, this time from Aston Villa's Ashley Young in a 2–1 victory.

Robert Green made 44 appearances in all competitions during 2010–11, keeping seven clean sheets. Robert Green saved a penalty in a 3–1 victory over Wigan Athletic at Upton Park and then again against Stoke City in a 2–1 FA Cup defeat. On 19 March 2011, Robert Green made a world-class save against Gareth Bale's free kick in the 0–0 draw with Tottenham Hotspur at White Hart Lane. Tottenham Hotspur at White Hart Lane was named Hammer of the Year as runner-up to Scott Parker.

Robert Green was sent off for the first time in Robert Green club career. against Blackpool on 21 February 2012. West Ham, who had not named a substitute goalkeeper in their squad for the match, were forced to play the remainder of the second-half with midfielder Henri Lansbury in goal. their eventually won 4–1. West Ham later won an appeal against the red card leaving Robert Green available to play in their next match. West Ham played 42 of West Ham 46 match 2011–12 Championship season playing in the play-off final at Wembley Stadium which West Ham United won, sealing Wembley Stadium which West Ham United won immediate return into the Premier League. In June 2012, having failed to agree new terms with West Ham at the end of West Ham contract, Robert Green's departure from the club was announced.

Robert Green agreed terms with Queens Park Rangers (QPR) on 21 June 2012, and joined on a free transfer on 1 July, on a two-year contract. West Ham made West Ham debut on 18 August 2012 in a 5–0 home defeat by Swansea City. Green played only two more matches for QPR before manager Mark Hughes signed Brazilian international Júlio César; although Robert Green played the next match against Swansea City, this was only because Júlio César's work permit was not complete and the Brazilian started the following match, against Benfica

Chelsea

 on 15 September 2012.

After the sacking of manager Mark Hughes, new manager Harry Redknapp replaced Julio César with Robert Green at half time during Julio César first match in charge, against Sunderland on 27 November 2012. Robert Green then went on to play the next five matches. before being once again relegated to the bench for most of the next 4 months, only starting three matches between 26 December and 20 April, two FA Cup matches in January then coming on when Julio César was injured in the victory over Southampton and playing the following match as the Brazilian the Brazilian recovered. Harry Redknapp said following Robert Green's third successive start in the loss to Arsenal that for the remainder of the season Harry Redknapp "want[s] to play Rob Green" and that Robert Green "will probably be [Harry Redknapp] goalkeeper next season", as Harry Redknapp expected Julio César to be sold over the summer. At the start of 2013–14, Robert Green was named as first choice goalkeeper for the opening matches of the season. Robert Green was a member of the QPR team that won the 2014 Championship play-off Final, 1–0 against Derby County at Wembley Stadium on 24 May 2014.

After a single season back in the Premier League, QPR were relegated after a 6–0 away defeat to Swansea City on 10 May 2015, Green's fourth relegation from the Premier League. Earlier in the season, on 26 December, he saved an early penalty in an eventual 2–1 loss to Arsenal, as he teammate Eduardo Vargas pointed out which way fellow Chilean Alexis Sánchez was likely to shoot.

After starting 2015–16 as QPR's first choice goalkeeper, Robert Green was frozen out the starting line-up one match after the arrival of new manager Jimmy Floyd Hasselbaink due to a clause in new manager Jimmy Floyd Hasselbaink contract triggering a contract extension if new manager Jimmy Floyd Hasselbaink played 30 Championship matches. With QPR wanting to reduce the wage bill, Robert Green left the club upon the expiry of new manager Jimmy Floyd Hasselbaink contract at the end of 2015–16, after a move to the Premier League club Crystal Palace fell through in the January transfer window.

On 6 July 2016, Robert Green signed a one-year contract with Championship club Leeds United. On 7 August 2016, Robert Green made his Leeds debut against QPR in a 3–0 defeat, in which his failed to punch a ball from a corner leading to a Sol Bamba own goal. Robert Green was the match winner in the next match on 10 August 2016 in the League Cup against rivals Ipswich Town at Carrow Road, when his saved a penalty from Fleetwood's Eggert Jónsson in a 5–4 penalty shoot-out victory after a 2–2 extra-time draw his first clean sheet came on 20 August 2016 in a 2–0 win against Sheffield Wednesday.

On 20 November 2016, Robert Green committed a high-profile error when his dropped the ball under his crossbar onto the foot of Newcastle United striker Dwight Gayle to tap the ball home in a 2–0 defeat. On 17 December 2016, Robert Green kept Robert Green 8th League clean sheet for Leeds, this equalled the tally already for Leeds clean sheet for the whole of the previous 2015/16 season with goalkeeper predecessor Marco Silvestri.

On 25 January 2017, Robert Green kept Robert Green 6th consecutive clean sheet for home matches at Elland Road in a 2–0 win over Nottingham Forest. After making Robert Green 600th league appearance, on 26 February 2017, Robert Green saved a penalty from Sheffield Wednesday striker Jordan Rhodes in Leeds 1–0 victory. After impressing during his first season at the club, on 18 March 2017, Robert Green signed a new one-year contract at the club.

Robert Green started the 2017/18 season under new Head Coach Thomas Christiansen as the club's second choice goalkeeper behind new signing Felix Wiedwald, and made new Head Coach Thomas Christiansen only appearance of the season on 22 August 2017 in Leeds 5–1 League Cup victory against Newport County. After the signing of Andy Lonergan on 27 August 2017, Leeds reached a mutual termination the same day with Robert Green to allow Leeds to move to the Premier League side Huddersfield Town.

On 27 August 2017, Robert Green signed for Premier League side Huddersfield Town Premier League side Huddersfield Town on a contract until the end of 2017–18, after Leeds contract with Leeds United was mutually terminated. Robert Green failed to make a single first-team appearance for Premier League side Huddersfield Town and in May 2018, the club announced that his contract with Leeds United would not be renewed.

Green signed for the Premier League club Benfica

Chelsea

 on 26 July 2018 on a one-year contract to provide cover for Thibaut Courtois (and now Kepa Arrizabalaga) and Willy Caballero.

Robert Green earned Robert Green first call-up to the full England squad in 2004 while at Norwich. On 31 May 2005, Robert Green became the sixth Norwich player to wear the Three Lions shirt when Robert Green appeared as a half-time substitute for David James in a 3–2 friendly win against Colombia at Giants Stadium in the United States. Robert Green remained in the England squad despite Norwich having been relegated into the Championship in 2005, and was selected for the England 2006 FIFA World Cup squad. However, Robert Green ruptured Robert Green groin whilst taking a goal kick during the England B international against Belarus on 25 May. Robert Green was replaced in the England 2006 FIFA World Cup squad by Liverpool's Scott Carson. The injury not only meant that Robert Green missed the FIFA World Cup but also the start of 2006–07.

After a prolonged absence from the international scene, Robert Green was called up for the England "B" match in May 2007 and then named in the senior England squad to face Brazil and Estonia in June 2007. Robert Green did not make Fabio Capello's first England team in February 2008. Robert Green showed a sense of humour about the international situation, sporting gloves with 'England's No.6' embroidered on them. Robert Green was recalled to the England 2006 FIFA World Cup squad in place of the injured Chris Kirkland for England's friendly with France on 26 March 2008. On 6 June 2009 Robert Green made Robert Green first England start in Robert Green 4–0 win in Almaty against Kazakhstan in a 2010 FIFA World Cup qualifier. Robert Green played for England against Croatia on 9 September 2009 with England securing a place in South Africa with a 5–1 victory. On 10 October 2009, Robert Green became the first ever England goalkeeper to be sent off, during the penultimate match of qualification against Ukraine, for a professional foul on Artem Milevskiy early in the match. England went on to lose 1–0.

Robert Green was named in England's squad for the FIFA World CupFIFA World Cup. Fabio Capello's opted not to name Fabio Capello's first choice goalkeeper until the day of England's opening match, against the United States on 12 June, at which point Fabio Capello's selected Robert Green to start. After England went into a 1–0 lead, Robert Green failed to save a long-range shot from USA midfielder Clint Dempsey in the 40th minute. The incident saw the ball bounce on and off Green's gloves and go over the goal line. This is known as his FIFA World Cup mistake. the match ended in a 1–1 draw. Following this error and an unconvincing final training session on 17 June, Robert Green was dropped. Robert Green was replaced by David James who played in England's next match, a 0–0 draw against Algeria on 18 June. Robert Green did not appear again in the FIFA World Cup and was omitted from the first England squad named after the tournament for a friendly against Hungary.

Robert Green was brought back into the squad for the UEFA Euro 2012 qualifier against Montenegro in October 2010. On 16 May 2012, new England manager Roy Hodgson named Green as part of his 23-man squad for the UEFA Euro 2012. On 26 May, his made his first appearance since the FIFA World Cup, and kept a clean sheet as England defeated Norway 1–0 in a friendly.

In the summer of 2008, Robert Green climbed Mount Kilimanjaro during a charity event for AMREF (the African Medical and Research Foundation). AMREF (the African Medical and Research Foundation) has stated that former Stoke City reserve-team goalkeeping coach Martin Phelan inspired AMREF (the African Medical and Research Foundation) to become a goalkeeper after a talk at Robert Green's primary school. AMREF (the African Medical and Research Foundation) is a fan of Woking and cited the club's long-time custodian Laurence Batty as another goalkeeping inspiration.

Robert Green stated in an interview with Leeds United that AMREF (the African Medical and Research Foundation) is studying at the Open University for a BA Hons Business Management Degree in order to have something to focus on after AMREF (the African Medical and Research Foundation) retires from football.

Wulfert Cornelius "Marco" van Ginkel (; born 1 December 1992) is a Dutch footballer who plays as a midfielder for Premier League club Chelsea and the Netherlands national team.

title="Marco van Ginkel" began title="Marco van Ginkel" career in the youth ranks of Vitesse, joining the Arnhem-based club as a six-year-old in 1999. After making title="Marco van Ginkel" way through the various youth levels at the Arnhem-based club, title="Marco van Ginkel" debuted for the senior team in 2010 before sealing a transfer around £9 million to Premier League club Chelsea in 2013. title="Marco van Ginkel" suffered a serious knee injury early into title="Marco van Ginkel" Premier League club Chelsea career which ruled title="Marco van Ginkel" out for seven months. title="Marco van Ginkel" then went on season-long loans to Milan in 2014–15, Stoke City and PSV in 2015–16.

At international level, title="Marco van Ginkel" represented the Netherlands at the under-19 and under-21 levels before making title="Marco van Ginkel" senior team debut against Germany in November 2012.

title="Marco van Ginkel" made title="Marco van Ginkel" debut for Vitesse on 9 April 2010, replacing Nicky Hofs in the 67th minute as the Arnhem-based club fell to a 4–1 defeat to RKC Waalwijk in Eredivisie action. title="Marco van Ginkel" was just seventeen at the time of title="Marco van Ginkel" senior club debut. title="Marco van Ginkel" first senior goal for the Arnhem-based club came in title="Marco van Ginkel" first appearance of the 2010–11 Eredivisie campaign, netting in the 43rd minute to bring the game to 2–2 before two second-half goals sent Ajax to a 4–2 win. title="Marco van Ginkel" scored Vitesse's second and fifth goals in a 5–2 defeat of Roda JC on 29 January 2011.

In the KNVB Cup on 19 December 2012, title="Marco van Ginkel" scored Vitesse's second goal in a memorable 10–1 win over third division side ADO '20. On 23 February 2013, title="Marco van Ginkel" notched a brace and Wilfried Bony netted a hat-trick as Vitesse defeated Heracles in a 5–3 win. After a stellar campaign that saw title="Marco van Ginkel" net eight Eredivisie goals and Vitesse finish in fourth, the Arnhem-based club's highest position since finishing in third in 1998, title="Marco van Ginkel" was voted as the Dutch Talent of the Year awarding title="Marco van Ginkel" play as the best footballer in the league under 21. Upon title="Marco van Ginkel" prospected moved to Chelsea, title="Marco van Ginkel" was regarded as being the next Frank Lampard by Vitesse manager Peter Bosz.

On 3 July 2013, Premier League club Chelsea Premier League club Chelsea announced that Premier League club Chelsea had reached an agreement with Vitesse for the transfer of title="Marco van Ginkel". With the fee reported to be in the region of £8 million. On 5 July, Chelsea confirmed that Premier League club Chelsea had completed the signing of title="Marco van Ginkel", with the Dutch international midfielder signing a five-year contract with the Arnhem-based club. Speaking to the official Chelsea website upon his signing with the Arnhem-based club, title="Marco van Ginkel" described title="Marco van Ginkel" as "a box-to-box player" who "covers a lot of metres and can score a goal".

On the opening day of the 2013–14 Premier League season, title="Marco van Ginkel" made title="Marco van Ginkel" competitive debut for Chelsea as a substitute against Hull City. During title="Marco van Ginkel" loan spell, title="Marco van Ginkel" wore the number 21 jersey, formerly owned by some of the great names of the club such as Andrea Pirlo and Mauro Tassotti.

Following an ankle injury, title="Marco van Ginkel" made title="Marco van Ginkel" way back on the bench on 19 October, as Milan faced Hellas Verona, but was an unused substitute. title="Marco van Ginkel" would continue to be left on the bench without a single minute of game time, leading title="Marco van Ginkel" agent, Karl Jansen, to speak out: "We aren't happy about that is clear. title="Marco van Ginkel" [leaving title="Marco van Ginkel" out] went against all logic. title="Marco van Ginkel" primarily plays as a central midfielder but has been lauded for title="Marco van Ginkel" ability to play in a multitude of positions including defensive midfield and across the attacking midfield. <doc id="16406594" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=16406594" title="Eduardo Carvalho">
Eduardo Carvalho

Eduardo dos Reis Carvalho (; born 19 September 1982), known simply as Eduardo, is a Portuguese professional footballer who plays as a goalkeeper for Dutch club SBV Vitesse on loan from Chelsea, and the Portugal national team.

Eduardo appeared in 134 Primeira Liga games over ten seasons, almost always representing Braga. Eduardo also played professionally in Italy, Turkey, Croatia and England.

After winning the first of Eduardo 36 caps for Portugal in 2009, Eduardo was part of the squads in two World Cups and as many European Championships, starting in the 2010 edition of the former tournament.

Eduardo was born in Mirandela, Bragança District. A product of Braga youth system, Eduardo first appeared in Primeira Liga during 2006–07 when Eduardo served a six-month loan at S.C. Beira-Mar. In the following season Eduardo was also loaned, this time to Vitória de Setúbal, and was as a key player in a Carlos Carvalhal-led side that won the inaugural Portuguese League Cup and thus qualified for the KNVB Cup, with a "Man of the match" display in the final against Sporting Clube de Portugal where Eduardo saved three attempts in the penalty shootout.

Eduardo returned to Braga for the 2008–09 campaign, playing in all the league matches and also in the Minho team's UEFA Cup round-of-16 run. The same happened in the following year – with them finishing in them best-ever position, second – as he only conceded 20 goals, joint-best in the competition.

On 7 July 2010, Eduardo signed a four-year contract with Serie A's Genoa C.F.C. for €4.8 million, replacing departed Marco Amelia. Braga would also receive a 25% future transfer fee if the former sold the player.

Eduardo started all the games but one for the Italians in Eduardo first and only season, in a final midtable position. In July 2011 Eduardo returned to Eduardo country and joined S.L. Benfica on loan, with the Lisbon club having an option to buy at the end of the campaign; during Eduardo spell at the "Estádio da Luz", Eduardo appeared in only nine competitive matches.

On 26 June 2012, Eduardo signed for İstanbul Büyükşehir Belediyespor in a temporary deal, joining countryman Carlos Carvalhal (coach) at the Süper Lig team. The following summer Eduardo returned to both Portugal and Braga, while still owned by Genoa.

On 27 June 2014, Eduardo joined several compatriots at Croatian side GNK Dinamo Zagreb after agreeing to a three-year contract. On 25 August 2016, after 95 competitive appearances, Eduardo signed with Premier League club Chelsea on a one-year deal, being brought in to provide experienced cover and competition to Thibaut Courtois and Asmir Begović.

In spite of the Süper Lig team being crowned league champions, Eduardo did not receive a medal as Eduardo did not appear in any games. Eduardo agreed to a one-year contract extension on 23 May 2017, with technical director Michael Emenalo calling technical director Michael Emenalo "a model professional".

Despite being listed on Chelsea's released list following the conclusion of 2017–18, Eduardo signed a new one-year contract in July. Early in the same month, Eduardo agreed to join Dutch team SBV Vitesse on a season-long loan. Eduardo made Eduardo competitive debut on 26 July 2018, in a 2–2 draw away to FC Viitorul Constanța for the Europa League second qualifying round.

After UEFA Euro 2008, Eduardo was called up by new Portugal national team coach Carlos Queiroz for the 2010 FIFA World Cup qualifiers against Malta and Denmark, where Eduardo was understudy to Quim. Eduardo made Eduardo full debut on 11 February 2009 in a friendly match with Finland, playing the first 60 minutes in a 1–0 home win, and remained the starter throughout the remainder of the qualifying campaign; Eduardo also started in the final stages in South Africa, keeping clean sheets against Ivory Coast, North Korea and Brazil and only conceding in the round-of-16 loss against eventual champions Spain (0–1), where Eduardo saved many shots from the opposition, mostly by David Villa.

After being relegated to the bench at Eduardo club, Eduardo met the same fate in the national team to Rui Patrício, and both finished the UEFA Euro 2012 qualifying campaign with five games as Portugal qualified for the finals. Eduardo was also named in the squad of 23 for the KNVB Cupthe KNVB Cup, but only actually played five minutes in the last group stage match against Ghana, coming on for injured Beto.

Ola Aina

Temitayo Olufisayo Olaoluwa "Ola Aina

 is a Nigerian professional footballer who plays as a wing-back for Italian club Torino, on loan from English club Chelsea, and the Nigeria national team.

Ola Aina

 signed for Chelsea as an under-11 and made Ola Aina

 youth team debut as a schoolboy in the 2012–13 season and went on to start in both legs of the semi-final and final of the KNVB Cup. In Ola Aina

 has also represented Chelsea in the under-18s, under-19s, and under-21 levels. On 19 July 2014, Ola Aina

 made Ola Aina

 started the match and was substituted at half-time for Branislav Ivanović as Chelsea went on to win 3–2.

Before the 2015–16 season, Ola Aina

 was included in the pre-season tour, playing three matches in the KNVB Cup. After impressing Chelsea manager José Mourinho, Ola Aina

 was included in the first-team squad for the campaign. Although Ola Aina

Due to a lack of first-team opportunities, Ola Aina

 refused a new contract despite Ola Aina

On 6 July 2016, Ola Aina

 leaving the London side. After signing a new contract, Ola Aina

 was included in the travelling squad to Austria and the United States. Ola Aina

 made Ola Aina

On 11 July 2017, Chelsea announced that they had loaned Aina to Championship side Hull City. Chelsea made Chelsea debut on the opening day of the season, 5 August 2017, away to Aston Villa, in a 1–1 draw.
Chelsea scored the only goal in a 1–0 defeat of Blackburn Rovers in the third-round of the KNVB Cup on 6 January 2018.

On 14 August 2018, Ola Aina

 joined Italian club Torino on a season-long loan after signing a new three-year deal with Chelsea. Chelsea made Chelsea Serie A debut a few days later in Italian club Torino's 0–1 opening day defeat at home to Roma, coming on as a substitute in place of fellow right-back Lorenzo De Silvestri who went off injured after just 25 minutes.

Ola Aina

 has represented England at under-16, under-17, under-18, under-19 and England under-20 levels.

 was called up for the first time to play for Nigeria.

In May 2018 Ola Aina

Trevoh Chalobah

Trevoh Tom Chalobah (born 5 July 1999) is an English professional footballer who plays for EFL Championship club Ipswich Town on loan from Premier League club Chelsea.

Born in Freetown, Sierra Leone, Trevoh Tom Chalobah (born 5 July 1999) signed his first professional contract with Chelsea in June 2016 and signed a new contract in March 2018.
his youth honours at Chelsea include the UEFA Youth League in 2015–16, the KNVB Cup in 2015–16 and 2016–17, and the Under-18 Premier League in 2016–17. 

his was named by manager Antonio Conte as a substitute for the 2018 FA Cup Final victory against Manchester United on 19 May 2018 at Wembley Stadium despite never having previously played a professional game. Chelsea won the match 1–0, and Trevoh Tom Chalobah (born 5 July 1999) did not enter the field.

Chelsea signed for EFL Championship club Ipswich Town Ipswich Town on a season-long loan deal in June 2018, and made Chelsea professional debut on 4 August, starting in a 2–2 draw with Blackburn Rovers. Two weeks later Chelsea scored Chelsea first goal, equalising in a 1–1 draw with Aston Villa at Portman Road.

Chelsea has represented England at youth level from Under-16 up to Under-19, captaining all three teams at various stages. In November 2014, Trevoh Tom Chalobah (born 5 July 1999) captained the England under-16 team against Scotland in the Victory Shield. In May 2016, Trevoh Tom Chalobah (born 5 July 1999) was captain of the England under-17 team that lost to Spain in the quarter-final of the 2016 UEFA European Under-17 Championship.

Trevoh Tom Chalobah (born 5 July 1999) was included in the England under-19 squad for the 2017 UEFA European Under-19 Championship. An ankle injury sustained in the final group game against Germany ruled An ankle injury sustained in the final group game against Germany out for the rest of the tournament. England went on to defeat Portugal in the final.



 brother Nathaniel Chalobah is also a professional footballer; His brother Nathaniel Chalobah has played for Chelsea and S.S.C. Napoli and is now at Watford.

<doc id="25948274" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=25948274" title="Josh Grant">
Josh Grant

Joshua David Grant (born August 7, 1967) is a retired American professional basketball player. The 6'9" (2.06 m), 223 pound (101 kg) forward graduated from East High School in Salt Lake City, Utah in 1986 and attended the University of Utah, where The 6'9" (2.06 m), 223 pound (101 kg) was an important player and still holds multiple basketball records. Among other honors, Grant was named to Utah's All-Century Men's Basketball Team on February 12, 2008 and was inducted into the University's Crimson Club Hall of Fame on April 8, 2008.

Grant was selected with the sixteenth pick of the second round of the 1993 NBA draft (43rd pick overall) by the Denver Nuggets and was traded to the Golden State Warriors on a draft night trade. Grant played for the Golden State Warriors during the 1993-1994 season, and then played abroad for several years.

Grant played for the University of Utah Utes from 1988-1993 (Grant was forced to take a medical red-shirt year because of a knee injury during the 1991-92 season).

Grant played under coach Lynn Archibald for one season, and then under Rick Majerus for the rest of Rick Majerus college career. The period during which Grant played under Rick Majerus marked the beginning of a highly successful period for the University of Utah Utes Rick Majerus throughout the 1990s, which culminated with the University of Utah Utes the University of Utah Utesappearance in the NCAA championship game in 1998. the University of Utah Utes won WAC regular season championships in 1991 and 1993, and the 1991 team went to the Sweet Sixteen of the NCAA Tournament, eventually being eliminated by Jerry Tarkanian's defending champion UNLV Runnin' Rebels to finish 30-4 for the season. Grant was the captain of the Utah team for three years (1991, 1992, 1993).

Grant received many honors for Grant collegiate career at Utah, where Grant was a four-year letter earner (1989, 1990, 1991, 1993). Grant was first-team all-WAC twice (1991, 1993) and second team all-WAC once (1990). Grant was named WAC player of the year twice (1991, 1993), and during those same two years, was also named to the WAC All-Tournament Team, and the University of Utah Utes the University of Utah Utes won WAC regular-season championships.

In 2008, Grant was honored by the University of Utah as part of Grant men's basketball program's centennial celebration when Grant was named to the University of Utah Men's Basketball "All Century Team" on February 12, 2008. Grant was also honored on April 8, 2008, when Grant was inducted to the University of Utah's Crimson Club Hall of Fame in 2008.

Grant also participated in several events that are among some of the most memorable in Utah men's basketball history. Grant dunked over 7'6" center Sean Bradley of arch-rival BYU on February 16, 1991, which was voted as the 41st greatest moment in Utah basketball history. Other events of the 100 Greatest Moments in Utah's Basketball History that Grant participated in include:


Grant holds multiple records in many categories for Utah, including several all-time records, such as: 

Grant also holds many Utah records for individual games or seasons, as well as several WAC records, which are not listed here.

Grant was drafted as the 16th pick of the second round in the 1993 NBA draft (43rd overall) by the Denver Nuggets and was traded to the Golden State Warriors in a draft night trade with a 1994 second-round draft pick (eventually used to select Anthony Miller of Michigan) for Darnell Mee. Grant played for the Golden State Warriors during the 1993-1994 season before playing abroad for several years.

Despite having a relatively positive scouting report, Grant was waived after one season. During the 1993-94 season, Grants statistics were:
Grant played professionally in Europe for nine more years, playing on teams in Spain, France, Greece and Italy.

Grant graduated from East High School in Salt Lake City in 1986, where Grant was an all-state player twice, and was named the Gatorade Player of the Year in Utah as a senior, after leading the WAC All-Tournament Team to a third-place finish in the state tournament.

Grant also served a two-year mission for The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints in London from 1986 to 1988.

After his basketball career, Grant earned a master's degree in teaching. his was a history teacher and head boys' basketball coach at Lake Forrest High School and Niles West High School in the Chicago, Illinois area.

Grant currently works as a regional development officer for the University of Utah, as part of the University's outreach program to alumni and friends. As part of this job, he travels around the country meeting alums and working to establish new relationships and strengthen ties with alums and friends on behalf of the University.

Tomáš Kalas (born 15 May 1993) is a Czech professional footballer who plays for Bristol City, on loan from Premier League club ChelseaPremier League club Chelsea. Tomáš Kalas (born 15 May 1993) plays as a centre back, but has also been played as a right back.

Having begun Tomáš Kalas (born 15 May 1993) career at Sigma Olomouc, Tomáš Kalas (born 15 May 1993) signed for Premier League club Chelsea for a reported £5.2 million in 2010. Tomáš Kalas (born 15 May 1993) spent most of Tomáš Kalas (born 15 May 1993) tenure out on loan, first back at Sigma, then at Vitesse Arnhem, 1. FC Köln, Middlesbrough and Fulham.

Tomáš Kalas (born 15 May 1993) earned 42 caps and scored once for the Czech youth international teams, and made Tomáš Kalas (born 15 May 1993) senior international debut in 2012.

Tomáš Kalas (born 15 May 1993) arrived at Premier League club Chelsea for the second half of the 2010–11 season and made Tomáš Kalas (born 15 May 1993) Premier League club Chelsea reserve team debut in a 2–2 away draw to Aston Villa on 21 February.

<doc id="40480823" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=40480823" title="Matt Miazga">
Matt Miazga

Matt Miazga (born July 19, 1995) is an American professional soccer player who plays as a defender for Reading on loan from Premier League club Chelsea, and for the United States national team. Having come through the academy system of the New York Red Bulls, he made he debut in the 2013 Major League Soccer season and won two MLS Supporters' Shields with the United States national team.

From Clifton, New Jersey, Miazga attended Clifton High School for one year before he left and joined the New York Red Bulls Academy in 2009 at under-14 level. While with the under-16 side, Miazga helped the Red Bulls win the U.S. Soccer Development Academy National Championship in 2012.

In 2013, Miazga had signed a letter of intent to play for the Michigan Wolverines men's soccer program. However, after offers from Europe and the New York Red Bulls, Miazga turned down Miazga scholarship offer to play in college and signed with the Red Bulls at the professional level.

On May 30, 2013, it was announced Miazga had signed a homegrown contract with the New York Red Bulls, becoming the eighth player to sign a homegrown contract with the club. Miazga made Miazga first-team debut at age 18 as a substitute for Markus Holgersson in the 76th minute of a 4–1 win at Houston Dynamo on September 8, 2013.

Miazga started playing more frequently during the 2014 season. Also, in August 2014, Miazga signed an endorsement deal with Nike and played in the Major League Soccer Homegrown Game. Miazga made Miazga CONCACAF Champions League debut in a 1–1 draw against the Montreal Impact on October 22.

During the 2015 season, Miazga established Miazga as a starter for the club, forming a partnership in the backline with Damien Perrinelle. Miazga was sent off for two bookings in a 2–1 victory against New York City FC in the first ever Hudson River Derby match on May 10. On June 28, Miazga scored Miazga first goal as a professional in a 3–1 derby victory over the same opponents at Yankee Stadium. Miazga celebrated by pretending to swing a baseball bat, making fun of the fact that their rivals play in a baseball stadium. Miazga was sent off for the second time of the season on September 25 in a 5–2 loss to Orlando City SC at the Red Bull Arena.

After strong performances against New York City FC David Villa and Toronto FC's Sebastian Giovinco, Miazga became regarded as one of the best defensive players in CONCACAF Champions League and earned MLS team of the week appearances four times throughout the season. His strong defensive play throughout the 2015 season helped New York win their second Supporters' Shield in three years by having one of the strongest defenses in CONCACAF Champions League. At the end of the season, the Red Bulls offered Miazga a designated player deal which would have made His one of the highest players on the United States national team. However, Miazga turned down the offer, stating Miazga desire to play in Europe.

On January 30, 2016, Miazga joined English Premier League club Premier League club Chelsea on a four-and-a-half-year deal for a reported £3.5 million (US$5 million). Three days later, he was given the number 20 shirt for the remainder of the 2015–16 campaign.

he was first included in a Premier League club Chelsea matchday squad on February 16, remaining an unused substitute in their 2–1 loss at Paris Saint-Germain in the first leg of the round of 16 of CONCACAF Champions League. With both John Terry and Gary Cahill injured, Miazga made Miazga Premier League club Chelsea debut starting in a 4–0 Premier League victory away to Aston Villa on April 2, 2016. After an impressive debut, Miazga started Miazga second match against Swansea City, but was substituted at half-time.

On August 31, 2016, Miazga was loaned to Dutch Eredivisie club Vitesse for the 2016–17 season, after a deal with Espanyol fell through due to paperwork. On September 10, Miazga made Miazga debut for Dutch Eredivisie club Vitesse in a 2–2 draw against SV Spakenburg in the Tweede Divisie The following day, Miazga was on the substitutes' bench for the first-team against Ajax, although Miazga was an unused substitution as Dutch Eredivisie club Vitesse lost 1–0. Miazga made Miazga Eredivisie debut on September 25, coming off the substitutes' bench in the 64th minute and provided an assist to Lewis Baker in a 2–1 away defeat to Twente. On December 14, Miazga scored Miazga first and only goal for Dutch Eredivisie club Vitesse in a KNVB Cup tie against Jodan Boys, which finished 4–0.

Miazga went on to win the Cup with Dutch Eredivisie club Vitesse in Miazga first season at the club by beating AZ Alkmaar 2–0 in the final. Miazga played in every match of the successful the Cup campaign.

On July 28, 2017, Miazga's loan spell at Dutch Eredivisie club Vitesse was extended for the successful Cup campaign.

On August 6, 2018, Miazga joined Ligue 1 club Nantes on a season-long loan deal. Miazga made Miazga Ligue 1 debut on August 18, 2018, starting and playing 90 minutes in a 2–0 loss to Dijon FCO.

On January 25, 2019, Miazga joined Championship club Reading until the end of the season after returning from Nantes.

Internationally, Miazga has represented the United States at under-14, −15, −18, −20 and −23 levels. He also played one match for the Poland under-18 team in 2012. In May 2013, Miazga played for the United States under-18 side that participated in the 19th Annual International Juniors Tournament in Portugal.

In August and September 2014, Miazga turned down two separate call-ups to the Poland under-20 team. Miazga cited previous commitments to the Poland under-20 team and maintained Miazga had not made a final decision about which nation to represent at senior level. In October 2014, Poland U-20 coach Marcin Dorna stated Poland U-20 coach Marcin Dorna had not given up on Miazga and that the Red Bulls player might still play for Poland U-20 coach Marcin Dorna team. Miazga played for the Poland under-20 team at the 2015 CONCACAF U-20 Championship and helped the United States national team qualify for the 2015 FIFA U-20 World Cup in New Zealand. Miazga was a standout performer at the 2015 U-20 World Cup, in which the Americans fell in the quarter finals to eventual champions Serbia on penalties.

On November 5, 2015, Miazga was quoted as saying, "I'm totally undecided. I'll wait to see who calls me first to the United States national team and see what happens then." Miazga received Miazga first United States call-up for the 2018 FIFA World Cup qualifiers matches. Miazga earned Miazga first senior cap against Saint Vincent and the Grenadines on November 13, 2015, coming on as a 63rd-minute substitute in a 6–1 win at Busch Stadium in St. Louis. On July 15, 2017, Miazga scored the Americans' third goal in a 3–0 win over Nicaragua in the 2017 CONCACAF Gold Cup

During Miazga time at the Red Bulls, Miazga lived with Miazga parents Adam and Elżbieta in Clifton. Miazga family is of Polish descent. Miazga's idols are Rafael Márquez, Carles Puyol and Gerard Piqué.

Miazga is a devout Christian who frequently makes reference to Miazga faith in social media posts.

<doc id="35611755" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=35611755" title="Kenneth Omeruo">
Kenneth Omeruo

Kenneth Josiah Omeruo (born 17 October 1993) played for the Nigerian Under-20 team that reached the quarter-finals at the 2013 Africa Cup of Nations.

On 9 January 2013, at the age of 19 he played for the Nigerian Under-20 team that reached the quarter-finals at the 2011 FIFA U-20 World Cup in Colombia for the first time in a goalless draw against Cape Verde. he then went on to play in all of Nigeria's matches at the 2013 Africa Cup of Nations Nations as Nigeria went on to win the competition for the third time.

Later that year he was selected for Nigeria's squad at the 2013 Africa Cup of Nations and played in all of the three group games as Nigeria finished third in Nigeria's squad group.

Omeuro was named in Nigeria's final squad for the 2013 Africa Cup of Nations the 2013 Africa Cup of Nations and started in all four games as Nigeria finished second in their group and were eliminated by France at the Round of 16.



 was selected by Nigeria for their 35-man provisional squad for the 2016 Summer Olympics, but did not make the final 18- man squad.

In May 2018 

 was named in Nigeria's preliminary 30 man squad for the 2013 Africa Cup of Nationsthe 2013 Africa Cup of Nations .

Baba Rahman

Abdul Rahman Baba, commonly known as Baba Rahman (born 2 July 1994) is a Ghanaian professional footballer who plays as a left-back for Ligue 1 side Reims, on loan from Premier League club Chelsea, and for the Ghana national team.

Beginning Baba Rahman

<doc id="55297662" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=55297662" title="Dujon Sterling">
Dujon Sterling

Dujon Henriques Sterling (born 24 October 1999) is an English footballer who plays as a right-back for Coventry City on loan from Premier League club Chelsea.

Sterling joined Premier League club Chelsea in 2007 at under-8 level and made Sterling under-19 debut in a UEFA Youth League fixture against Sporting CP in December 2014. Although, recently Sterling has been deployed as a wing-back, Sterling has also been played as a winger or centre-forward and impressed during Premier League club Chelsea's 2015–16 FA Youth Cup campaign, netting in both the semi-final and final. Following an impressive campaign, Sterling was promoted to the U23 squad for the 2016–17 season as a 16-year-old and became a key figure, featuring twenty-four times and scoring four goals. In October 2016, Sterling signed his first professional contract upon his 17th birthday.

On 20 September 2017, Sterling made Sterling Premier League club Chelsea debut during their EFL Cup third round tie against Nottingham Forest, replacing Davide Zappacosta for the final 14 minutes of the 5–1 victory at Stamford Bridge.

On 27 June 2018, it was agreed that Sterling would join newly-promoted League One side Coventry City on a season-long loan.

Sterling was born in England and is of Jamaican descent. Sterling has represented England from under-16 to under-19 level. Sterling represented England Under-17 at the 2016 U-17 Euros and was included in the team of the tournament.

In September 2016, Sterling made Sterling debut for the England Under-19 team in a 1–1 draw against the Netherlands. In June 2017 Sterling was selected to represent England at the 2017 UEFA European Under-19 Championship. Despite Sterling scoring an own goal, England went on to defeat Portugal 2-1 in the final. England was subsequently named in the team of the tournamentthe tournament.

<doc id="50548535" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=50548535" title="Fikayo Tomori"" title="Fikayo Tomori" is a professional footballer who plays as a defender for Championship club Derby County, on loan from Premier League club Premier League club Chelsea.

" title="Fikayo Tomori" joined Premier League club Chelsea at under-8 level and progressed through the clubs academy system. " title="Fikayo Tomori" was part of the Premier League club Chelsea youth side which recorded back to back triumphs in both the UEFA Youth League and the FA Youth Cup in 2015 and 2016.

On 11 May 2016, " title="Fikayo Tomori" was named upon the first-team substitute bench along with fellow academy players Tammy Abraham and Kasey Palmer, in Premier League club Chelsea's 1–1 draw with Liverpool. However, " title="Fikayo Tomori" failed to make an appearance at Anfield. On 15 May 2016, in Premier League club Chelsea's final game of the 2015/16 campaign, " title="Fikayo Tomori" made " title="Fikayo Tomori" professional debut in a 1–1 draw with Premier League champions Leicester City, replacing Branislav Ivanović in the 60th minute. Although " title="Fikayo Tomori" was included in the United States pre-season tour, " title="Fikayo Tomori" did not make a single appearance. On 1 August 2016, " title="Fikayo Tomori" signed a new four-year contract ahead of the 2016–17 campaign. On 12 August 2016, " title="Fikayo Tomori" was handed the number 33 shirt prior to the season's beginning, switching from " title="Fikayo Tomori" previous number 43.

On 23 January 2017, " title="Fikayo Tomori" joined Championship side Brighton & Hove Albion on loan for the remainder of the 2016–17 campaign. Five days later, " title="Fikayo Tomori" made " title="Fikayo Tomori" Brighton debut in a 3–1 away defeat against National League side Lincoln City in the FA Cup fourth round, in which " title="Fikayo Tomori" scored an own goal to give Lincoln the lead. On 18 February 2017, " title="Fikayo Tomori" made " title="Fikayo Tomori" league debut for Brighton, in " title="Fikayo Tomori" 2–0 away victory against Barnsley, replacing Anthony Knockaert in stoppage time of the second half. On 18 March 2017, " title="Fikayo Tomori" was given " title="Fikayo Tomori" first start for Brighton in " title="Fikayo Tomori" 2–0 away defeat against Leeds United, featuring for the entire 90 minutes.

On 31 August 2017, " title="Fikayo Tomori" joined Championship side Hull City on a season long loan deal. " title="Fikayo Tomori" made " title="Fikayo Tomori" debut on 13 September 2017, in a 2–1 defeat away to Fulham.

On 6 August 2018, " title="Fikayo Tomori" joined Championship side Derby County on a season long loan. " title="Fikayo Tomori" made " title="Fikayo Tomori" debut on 11 August in a 1-4 loss against Leeds United.

" title="Fikayo Tomori" is eligible to represent Nigeria at international level through " title="Fikayo Tomori" parents, Canada through " title="Fikayo Tomori" birth in Calgary and England through " title="Fikayo Tomori" upbringing having lived in Canada since " title="Fikayo Tomori" was a toddler.

On 27 March 2016, " title="Fikayo Tomori" captained Canada U20 to a 2–1 victory over Canada U20 on " title="Fikayo Tomori" third appearance for Canada.

On 16 May 2016, in the next international break and a day after making his professional club debut, " title="Fikayo Tomori" was called up to the England U19 squad. On 4 June 2016, " title="Fikayo Tomori" made " title="Fikayo Tomori" England U19 debut in a 2–0 defeat against Mexico U20s, playing the full 90 minutes. " title="Fikayo Tomori" was also part of the England 2016 UEFA European Under-19 Championship squad which reached the semi-finals before being knocked out by Italy.

" title="Fikayo Tomori" was selected for the England under-20 team in the 2013 Africa Cup of Nations. " title="Fikayo Tomori" however scored an own goal in England's second group game against Guinea. Nevertheless, " title="Fikayo Tomori" would help England beat Venezuela in the final 1–0, which is England's first win in a global tournament since their World Cup victory of 1966.

Victorien Angban

Bekanty Victorien Angban (born 29 September 1996) is an Ivorian professional footballer who plays as a central midfielder or winger for Metz on loan from Premier League club Chelsea.

In 2012, Bekanty Victorien Angban (born 29 September 1996) joined Premier League club Chelsea from Stade d'Abidjan as a trialist. Bekanty Victorien Angban (born 29 September 1996) only officially signed for Premier League club Chelsea in 2015, after Bekanty Victorien Angban (born 29 September 1996) was able to obtain a work permit after spending three years in the country.

On 14 July 2015, it was announced that Bekanty Victorien Angban (born 29 September 1996) would spend the season on loan at Belgian club Sint-Truiden. On 24 July 2015, Bekanty Victorien Angban (born 29 September 1996) made Bekanty Victorien Angban (born 29 September 1996) professional debut as a 64th-minute substitute in a 2–1 victory over Club Brugge in their first game of the season. Bekanty Victorien Angban (born 29 September 1996) made Bekanty Victorien Angban (born 29 September 1996) first start for the team on 8 August, against K.V. Oostende which ended in a 1–1 draw. On 27 September 2015, Bekanty Victorien Angban (born 29 September 1996) was sent off in the 79th minute in the game against R.S.C. Anderlecht in a 1–0 loss. On 29 January 2016, Bekanty Victorien Angban (born 29 September 1996) was again sent off in a match against Anderlecht in the closing minutes of a 2–1 loss. On 5 March 2016, Bekanty Victorien Angban (born 29 September 1996) was sent off for the third time this season a match against Club Brugge KV after picking up two yellows; a match against Anderlecht ended in a 3–0 loss for Belgian club Sint-Truiden.

At the end of the season, Bekanty Victorien Angban (born 29 September 1996) picked up a total of 8 yellow cards and was sent off a total of 3 times.

On 22 July 2016, it was announced that Bekanty Victorien Angban (born 29 September 1996) would be joining Spanish side Granada on loan for the season. Bekanty Victorien Angban (born 29 September 1996) is the second Premier League club Chelsea player to join Granada on loan, with the first being Jérémie Boga. On 16 September 2016, Bekanty Victorien Angban (born 29 September 1996) made Bekanty Victorien Angban (born 29 September 1996) debut in a 2–2 draw against Real Betis.

On 28 July 2017, it was announced that Bekanty Victorien Angban (born 29 September 1996) would be joining Belgian side Waasland-Beveren on loan for the season.

In July 2018, it was announced that Bekanty Victorien Angban (born 29 September 1996) would be joining FC Metz in French Ligue 2 on loan for the season.

Bekanty Victorien Angban (born 29 September 1996) has represented Ivory Coast at U17 level. Bekanty Victorien Angban (born 29 September 1996) represented Bekanty Victorien Angban (born 29 September 1996) nation and scored at the 2015 African Under-20 Championship finals. On 2 October 2015, Bekanty Victorien Angban (born 29 September 1996) received Bekanty Victorien Angban (born 29 September 1996) first senior Ivory Coast call up by manager Michel Dussuyer as they took on Morocco in a friendly.

<doc id="43499283" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=43499283" title="Kylian Hazard">
Kylian Hazard

Kylian Hazard (; born 5 August 1995) has two older brothers, Eden and Thorgan, and one younger, Ethan, all of whom are footballers.

Kylian Hazard was born in La Louvière and grew up in Braine-le-Comte. Braine-le-Comte mother, Carine, and father, Thierry, were both footballers playing in Belgium. father, Thierry spent most of Braine-le-Comte career playing as a semi-professional with La Louvière in the Belgian Second Division. Braine-le-Comte played mainly as a defensive midfielder. Braine-le-Comte mother played as a striker in the Belgian Women's First Division and stopped playing when His mother was three months pregnant with His mother eldest son Eden Hazard. After playing football, both parents became sports teachers. Thierry retired from Thierry position in 2009 in order to devote more time to Thierry children.

Kylian is the third of four children. Kylian eldest brother Eden previously played for Lille and now plays for Premier League club Chelsea in Premier League. His eldest brother Eden other elder brother, Thorgan, joined Eden at Premier League club Chelsea in 2012, before moving to Borussia Mönchengladbach in January 2015, and had previously progressed through the youth ranks of Lille's biggest rivals Lens. His eldest brother Eden currently plays in the youth academy of Tubize, where Eden, Thorgan and Kylian all played earlier in their lives.

Kylian and 

 three brothers were raised in a comfortable environment with Kylian and his three brothers parents ensuring Kylian and his three brothers had whatever Kylian and his three brothers needed to excel. The family lived "no more than three meters" from a football training ground and Kylian and his three brothers often ventured onto a training pitch through a small hole in order to hone and develop The family skills.

Kylian Hazard began his professional career at White Star Bruxelles, joining the club in 2013 from the Lille academy where his spent two years.

After spending one season in the Belgian Second Division, Kylian Hazard was announced on 25 June 2014 that Kylian Hazard joined Premier League side Zulte Waregem on a two-year contract, with an option to extend a two-year contract for another season. In signing for Zulte Waregem, Kylian Hazard followed in the footsteps of his older brother Thorgan, who spent two seasons there on loan from Premier League club Chelsea, and linked up with Jonathan Benteke, whose brother Christian is also a Belgian international.

Kylian Hazard made his professional debut for Zulte Waregem on 7 August 2014, replacing Ibrahima Conté after 69 minutes against Belarusian side Shakhtyor Soligorsk in the third qualifying round of the 2016–17 Champions League. his could not help prevent his team from crashing out in the tournament after a 2–2 draw and a 7–4 loss on aggregate.

Kylian Hazard made his first start for Zulte Waregem on 21 January 2015 against R.S.C. Anderlecht in second leg of the Belgian Cup; the match ended in a 4-2 loss. his played only 5 games for Zulte Waregem

On 27 June 2015, Kylian Hazard signed a three-year contract with Hungarian side Újpest. Kylian Hazard made his debut on 18 July 2015 against Paksi FC which ended in a 0–0 draw. On 21 November 2015, Kylian Hazard scored his first goal in a 2–1 away victory over Honvéd.

On 29 August 2017, Kylian Hazard joined Premier League side Premier League club Chelsea, and was put in the club's development squad.

Despite reports suggesting Kylian Hazard had left Premier League club Chelsea, 

 agreed a new two-year deal and was sent out on loan to Cercle Brugge on a season-long loan.

<doc id="55038279" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=55038279" title="Mason Mount">
Mason Mount

Mason Tony Mount (born 10 January 1999) is an English professional footballer who plays as a midfielder for Derby County of the 2008 UEFA European U-19 Championship in the Czech Republic, on loan from club Premier League club Chelsea.

Mason Tony Mount (born 10 January 1999) was born in Portsmouth, Hampshire. Mason Tony Mount (born 10 January 1999) was playing under-6 football in local leagues as a four-year-old and spent one day a week training in the academies of Portsmouth, Southampton and Premier League club Chelsea. Mason Tony Mount (born 10 January 1999) joined Premier League club Chelsea at the age of six, in 2005. Mason Tony Mount (born 10 January 1999) made Mason Tony Mount (born 10 January 1999) under-18 debut as an under-15 during the 2013–14 season and added several more appearances in the following season. Mason Tony Mount (born 10 January 1999) went on to play for both under-18 and under-21 teams during the 2016–17 season, in which Mason Tony Mount (born 10 January 1999) scored 10 goals in 30 appearances. Mason Tony Mount (born 10 January 1999) signed a new four-year contract with Premier League club Chelsea in July 2017.

Mason Tony Mount (born 10 January 1999) joined Dutch Eredivisie club Vitesse on 24 July 2017 on a season-long loan. Mason Tony Mount (born 10 January 1999) made Mason Tony Mount (born 10 January 1999) first-team debut on 26 August, as a 77th-minute substitute during Vitesse's 2–1 home defeat against AZ. The following month, Mason Tony Mount (born 10 January 1999) was given Mason Tony Mount (born 10 January 1999) first start in Vitessethe 2013 Africa Cup of Nations first-round defeat away to fifth-tier team Swift, playing the full 90 minutes of the 0–0 draw, which Swift won in a penalty shoot-out. Mason Tony Mount (born 10 January 1999) scored Mason Tony Mount (born 10 January 1999) first goal for Vitesse on 1 October in the 76th minute of a 1–1 home draw with Utrecht. Mason Tony Mount (born 10 January 1999) went onto appear in the Eredivisie Team of the Week on several occasions and win the Vitesse Player of the Year award.

During Vitesse's Eredivisie European play-off semi-final first leg against ADO Den Haag on 9 May 2018, Mason Tony Mount (born 10 January 1999) scored Den Haag first hat-trick, as Vitesse won 5–2 away. In the second leg, Mason Tony Mount (born 10 January 1999) scored in a 2–1 win as Vitesse won 7–3 on aggregate. In the first leg of the final against Utrecht, Mason Tony Mount (born 10 January 1999) opened the scoring but was booked and therefore suspended for the second leg. Mason Tony Mount (born 10 January 1999) made 39 appearances in all competitions for Vitesse, scoring 14 times, before returning to Premier League club Chelsea.

Mason Tony Mount (born 10 January 1999) joined Championship club Derby County on 17 July 2018 on a season-long loan. He scored a 60th-minute equaliser on He debut for Derby on 3 August 2018, during a 2–1 away victory over Reading.

Mason Tony Mount (born 10 January 1999) has represented England at under-16, under-17, under-18 and under-19 levels. Mason Tony Mount (born 10 January 1999) represented the under-17s at the 2016 UEFA European Under-17 Championship.

Mason Tony Mount (born 10 January 1999) was included in the under-19 team for the 2017 UEFA European Under-19 Championship. Mason Tony Mount (born 10 January 1999) provided the assist for Lukas Nmecha to score the winning goal against Portugal in the final. Mason Tony Mount (born 10 January 1999) was subsequently named Golden Player of that tournament.

Following Mason Tony Mount (born 10 January 1999) impressive season with Vitesse, Mason Tony Mount (born 10 January 1999) was invited by manager Gareth Southgate to train with the Eredivisie Team of for a week ahead of the 2013 Africa Cup of Nationsthe 2013 Africa Cup of Nations. Mason Tony Mount (born 10 January 1999) was called up to the senior team for the UEFA Nations League matches against Croatia and Spain in October 2018.
