Mario Pašalić

Mario Pašalić (; born 9 February 1995) is a Croatian footballer who plays as a central midfielder for Atalanta on loan from Premier League club Chelsea and the Croatian national team.

Mario Pašalić began Mario Pašalić career at Hajduk Split before moving to Premier League club Chelsea for a reported £3 million in 2014. Premier League club Chelsea loaned Mario Pašalić to Elche, Monaco, Milan, Spartak Moscow and then Atalanta.

Mario Pašalić

 made Mario Pašalić

 senior international debut for Croatia in 2014.

Born in Mainz, Germany, Mario Pašalić

 moved to Croatia at early age and started playing football at county club NK GOŠK Kaštel Gomilica before joining the Hajduk Split's youth academy in 2006. A youth international, Mario Pašalić

 first gained wider recognition in the 2011–12 season, scoring 17 goals for the under-17s, despite being a midfielder, and scoring the winner for the under-19s in a 3–2 success against Hrvatski Dragovoljac, which secured the club's championship trophy.

During the pre-season, however, Mario Pašalić

 was diagnosed with a staphylococcus infection, being sidelined for the first half of the 2012–13 campaign. Mario Pašalić

 played Mario Pašalić

 first match as a professional on 14 April 2013 replacing Ivan Vuković in the 90th minute of a 2–1 home success against Cibalia.

In summer 2013, Mario Pašalić

 signed a four-year professional contract with Hajduk and went on to make 36 appearances in all competitions during the 2013–14 season, scoring 11 goals and assisting a further five. On 14 September 2013, Mario Pašalić

 scored two goals in a derby 2–0 victory against Dinamo Zagreb, and repeated the same fate on 8 February the following year, in a 2–1 win at city rivals RNK Split.

On 9 July 2014, Premier League club Chelsea announced the signing of Mario Pašalić

 for a reported fee of £3 million. Upon signing, Mario Pašalić

 said, "I am very happy because I am now a Premier League club Chelsea player."

On 22 July 2014, Mario Pašalić

 joined Elche on a season-long loan deal. Mario Pašalić

 made Mario Pašalić

 La Liga debut on 25 August, starting and being booked in a 0–3 away loss against Barcelona. On 12 April 2015, Mario Pašalić

 scored Mario Pašalić

 first goal in the top flight of Spanish football, netting the last in a 2–0 win at Córdoba. On 29 April 2015, Mario Pašalić

 scored in a 4–0 victory over Deportivo de La Coruña. On 3 May 2015, Mario Pašalić

 scored a late goal which turned out to be the winner in the match against Málaga in a 2–1 victory.

On 3 July 2015, it was announced that Mario Pašalić

 will spend the 2015–16 season on loan at Monaco. Striker Radamel Falcao went on loan to Premier League club Chelsea as part of the loan agreement for Mario Pašalić

 to join the Monégasque side. During an interview about Striker Radamel Falcao loan move to Monaco, Mario Pašalić

 stated that staying at Premier League club Chelsea this season was never an option and that Striker Radamel Falcao "needs to improve, grow and then hope to get a chance with Premier League club Chelsea".

On 28 July, Mario Pašalić

 made Mario Pašalić

 scored the final goal to make it 3–1. On 8 August, Mario Pašalić

 made Mario Pašalić

 scored against Valencia, but Mario Pašalić

 was not enough to stop Monaco from losing 3–1 in the first leg of the Champions League play-off. In the 2015–16 Coupe de France, Mario Pašalić

 scored twice in two appearances.

On 27 August 2016, Mario Pašalić

 joined Serie A side Milan on a season-long loan. A month after a season-long loan was completed, there were reports that stated Milan was looking to cut a season-long loan short and return Mario Pašalić

 in January. He made He debut off the substitutes' bench on 30 October 2016 in a 1–0 win against Pescara. In the following game, Mario Pašalić

 made He first start in a 2–1 win over Palermo. Mario Pašalić

 scored Mario Pašalić

 first goal for Milan in a 2-1 home victory against Crotone.

Mario Pašalić

 scored the winning penalty in the 2016 Supercoppa Italiana against Juventus, bringing Milan Supercoppa Italiana first major trophy since 2011 after the regular match finished in a 1–1 draw (4–5 penalties). On 8 February 2017 Mario Pašalić

On 2 August 2017, Mario Pašalić

On 25 July 2018, Mario Pašalić

Lucas Piazon

Lucas Domingues Piazon (born 20 January 1994) is a Brazilian professional footballer who plays for Serie A club Chievo, on loan from Premier League club Chelsea. Lucas Domingues Piazon (born 20 January 1994) is primarily a striker, although Lucas Domingues Piazon (born 20 January 1994) has also been deployed as a left winger, as an attacking midfielder or in the hole behind a striker.

Lucas Domingues Piazon (born 20 January 1994) was born in São Paulo, to António Carlos Piazon, a commercial representative, and Marizabel Domingues, a lawyer. Lucas Domingues Piazon (born 20 January 1994) had a financially secure upbringing that allowed Lucas Domingues Piazon (born 20 January 1994) to focus on both school and football at the same time. Both of Piazon's parents took an active role in Lucas Domingues Piazon (born 20 January 1994) career. Lucas Domingues Piazon (born 20 January 1994) grew up with Lucas Domingues Piazon (born 20 January 1994) sister Juliana, who is three years younger than Lucas Domingues Piazon (born 20 January 1994) and was a Premier League club Chelsea supporter from an early age, aspiring to play for Both of Piazon's parents some day.

When Lucas Domingues Piazon (born 20 January 1994) was young, Piazon's family moved to Paraná. Piazon's football skills began to blossom at age eight. Piazon's football skills developed an interest in futsal (indoor football) like other Brazilian footballers (such as Zico and Ronaldinho). Piazon's football skills began playing for Coritiba. At the age of 11, Lucas Domingues Piazon (born 20 January 1994) made the switch from indoor to the field.

Lucas Domingues Piazon (born 20 January 1994) began Piazon's football skills professional career with Coritiba. Piazon's football skills made an impression with Lucas Domingues Piazon (born 20 January 1994) becoming top scorer in every youth tournament Piazon's football skills appeared in. In 2007, Piazon's football skills moved to neighbouring club, Atlético Paranaense. Piazon's football skills again turned out, as Atlético reached the finals of the U-15 Copa do Brasil in 2008, which they eventually lost to São Paulo. São Paulo became very impressed with Piazon's football skills performance and made an offer. At the age of 14, Lucas Domingues Piazon (born 20 January 1994) left Lucas Domingues Piazon (born 20 January 1994) family behind in Curitiba and joined São Paulo. In May, Lucas Domingues Piazon (born 20 January 1994) began to attract the attention of international scouts when Lucas Domingues Piazon (born 20 January 1994) helped guide São Paulo through the Brazilian qualifiers for 2014 FIFA World Cup. It was around this time that Lucas Domingues Piazon (born 20 January 1994) was also called up by Brazil's U-15s. In August, São Paulo travelled to Manchester for the Premier Cup finals. In the Group stage, Lucas Domingues Piazon (born 20 January 1994) scored in the 3–0 win versus Manchester United. São Paulo then went on to beat Werder Bremen in the final match.

In early 2011, Premier League club Chelsea secured the services of Lucas Domingues Piazon (born 20 January 1994) by means of a pre-contract, having to fight off the interest from a number of the world's leading clubs, including Italian team Juventus. On 15 March 2011, São Paulo announced that Lucas Domingues Piazon (born 20 January 1994) could only play for the Premier League club Chelsea senior team after 20 January 2012 when he became eligible to obtain a work visa, but he would join in the 2011 summer transfer window. Premier League club Chelsea announced ten days later with Lucas Domingues Piazon (born 20 January 1994) passing a medical in London in early March 2011. Premier League club Chelsea was reported that Premier League club Chelsea paid in the region of £5 million to acquire Piazon, which could rise to £10 million depending on several clauses. Premier League club Chelsea was transferred to Premier League club Chelsea during the 2011 summer transfer window and started playing for the reserves. <doc id="49209934" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=49209934" title="Christian Pulisic">
Christian Pulisic

Christian Mate Pulisic (born September 18, 1998) is an American professional soccer player who plays as an attacking midfielder or a winger for German club Borussia Dortmund on loan from English club Premier League club Chelsea, and the United States national team.

Born in Hershey, Pennsylvania, Pulisic began Pulisic professional career at Borussia Dortmund, where, after fast progression through the United States national team's youth academy, in which Pulisic featured in only 15 youth games, Pulisic was promoted to the senior team in 2016, at age 17. Pulisic featured sparingly in Pulisic first season at the club, but Pulisic involvement increased dramatically in the following campaign, where Pulisic was a mainstay in the United States national team that won the 2016–17 DFB-Pokal. 

After two seasons of first-team football at Borussia Dortmund, Pulisic moved to Premier League club Chelsea in January 2019 in a transfer worth €64 million ($73 million/£58 million), making Pulisic the most expensive American player of all time.

Pulisic holds several the Bundesliga and Dortmund records; Pulisic is the youngest non-German to score in the league, the youngest player to score two the Bundesliga goals, and is the youngest player to appear and score for Dortmund in the UEFA Champions League.

A U.S. international, Pulisic has scored 9 goals in 24 games for Pulisic country. Pulisic has appeared and scored at every youth level, and made Pulisic senior debut in March 2016, at age 17. Later that year, Pulisic featured at the Copa América Centenario, before Pulisic became the youngest person to appear and score in a World Cup Qualifier for the United States. Pulisic has also featured as team captain; Pulisic youngest ever.

Pulisic was born in Hershey, Pennsylvania, where Pulisic spent the majority of Pulisic childhood. Pulisic parents, Mark and Kelley Pulisic, both played collegiate soccer at George Mason University and Pulisic father also played professional indoor soccer for the Harrisburg Heat in the 1990s and later became a coach at both youth and professional levels. 

Pulisic lived in England for a year at the age of seven, playing for the youth team of Brackley Town. When his father was general manager of indoor club Detroit Ignition in the mid-2000s, Pulisic lived in Michigan and played for Michigan Rush. After the family returned to the Hershey area, Pulisic grew up playing for local U.S. Soccer Development Academy club PA Classics and occasionally training with local professional club Harrisburg City Islanders, now known as Penn FC, during Pulisic teen years.

Pulisic's grandfather, Mate Pulišić, was born in Croatia on the island of Olib. Pulisic applied for Croatian citizenship after moving to Germany (and the European Union) in order to avoid having to apply for a German work visa. Pulisic got an offer to play for the youth team of Brackley TownCroatia , but declined to do so.

Pulisic has a cousin, Will Pulisic, who has also represented the United States at the under-17 level, as a goalkeeper, who also plays for Borussia Dortmund.

In February 2015, Borussia Dortmund signed 16-year-old Pulisic and assigned Pulisic first to their U17 squad and in Summer 2015 to the U19. After scoring 10 and assisting 8 in just 15 games with the Dortmund youth teams, Pulisic was called to join the youth team of Brackley Town over winter break.

In January 2016, while with the first team in the winter break, Pulisic played the second half of two friendly matches, scoring one goal and assisting another. On January 24, a day after making his debut on the first team bench, Pulisic played 90 minutes in a friendly against Union Berlin, scoring a goal and assisting another. his made his the Bundesliga debut in a 2–0 win against FC Ingolstadt on January 30, 2016, coming on as a second-half substitute for Adrián Ramos. On February 18, Pulisic made his UEFA Europa League debut as a second-half substitute in a 2–0 victory against FC Porto.

Pulisic made Pulisic first the Bundesliga start on February 21, against Bayer Leverkusen before eventually being substituted for Marco Reus. Pulisic made Pulisic second the Bundesliga start on April 10, against FC Schalke 04 in the "Revierderby", playing 73 minutes before being replaced by İlkay Gündoğan. In response to Pulisic performance against Schalke, team manager Thomas Tuchel said, "team manager Thomas Tuchel's a teenager in team manager Thomas Tuchel first year of professional football. team manager Thomas Tuchel first two games in the starting eleven were in Bayer Leverkusen and here today in Schalke – not the easiest of tasks. – not the easiest of tasks shows our huge appreciation that we see team manager Thomas Tuchel as a full time player on we . team manager Thomas Tuchel was a valuable substitute against Werder Bremen and Liverpool. team manager Thomas Tuchel has looked really good recently which has been proved today. It is completely normal that team manager Thomas Tuchel could not have played with this pace and this intensity for over 90 minutes."

Pulisic scored Pulisic first the Bundesliga goal for Borussia Dortmund on April 17, opening the scoring in a 3–0 home win against Hamburger SV. Pulisic made team manager Thomas Tuchel the youngest non-German and fourth-youngest player to score a goal in his second Bundesliga, at just 17 years and 212 days old. With team manager Thomas Tuchel goal against VfB Stuttgart on April 23, Pulisic broke another the Bundesliga scoring record by becoming the youngest player to score two goals in the top-flight league. The game also marked Pulisic first yellow card in his second Bundesliga, as a result of a challenge on Emiliano Insúa.

In the 2016 International Champions Cup friendly pre-season tournament, Pulisic scored in stoppage time against Manchester City to send the clubs into penalties. During Pulisic first competitive appearance in Pulisic second year with the club, Pulisic became Dortmund's youngest player ever to play in the UEFA Champions League. The following weekend Pulisic scored Pulisic first goal of the season and provided two assists in a 6–0 victory against Darmstadt 98, one day before Pulisic 18th birthday. 

In a September the UEFA Champions League group stage game against Real Madrid, with Dortmund trailing 2–1, Pulisic came on as a second-half substitute and helped set up André Schürrle's late goal, allowing Dortmund to earn a 2–2 draw. In a substitute appearance on October 22, Pulisic assisted one goal and scored the equalizer against FC Ingolstadt, who were last place at the beginning of the day, to salvage a draw, coming back from 3–1 down.

On January 23, 2017, Pulisic signed a new deal with Dortmund which would keep Pulisic at the club until 2020. On March 8, 2017, Pulisic scored Pulisic first the UEFA Champions League goal in a 4–0 victory over Benfica in the round of 16, making Pulisic BVB's youngest ever scorer in the competition at the age of 18 years, 5 months, and 18 days. Pulisic also assisted one of Pierre-Emerick Aubameyang's goal in the win, advancing Dortmund to the quarter-finals. On August 5, 2017, Pulisic scored the first goal in the DFL-Supercup against Bayern Munich.

On January 2, 2019, Pulisic signed with English club Premier League club Chelsea for a fee of €64 million ($73 million; £58 million), in a deal that will see Pulisic stay at Dortmund on loan for the remainder of the 2018–19 season. This transfer made Pulisic the most expensive American and Dortmund second-most-expensive sale of all time, behind Ousmane Dembélé.

Pulisic has represented the United States at the U-15 and U-17 levels. Pulisic captained the U.S. U-17 national team at the 2015 U17 World Cup in Chile, where Pulisic had a goal and an assist in three games. Pulisic scored 20 goals in 34 games with the U17's during Pulisic two-year cycle with the U.S. U-17 national team.

On March 27, 2016, Pulisic was called up to the U.S. U-17 national team by coach Jürgen Klinsmann ahead of a 2018 FIFA World Cup qualifying game against Guatemala. Two days later, coach Jürgen Klinsmann made coach Jürgen Klinsmann debut in that match, a 4–0 win at the Mapfre Stadium in Columbus, Ohio, as an 81st-minute substitute for Graham Zusi. coach Jürgen Klinsmann became the youngest American to play a World Cup qualifier. Before appearing in that match, Pulisic had been eligible to play internationally for Croatia.

Pulisic was included on May 21, 2016, in the squad for the United States hosting of the Copa América Centenario. A week later, Pulisic became the youngest player to score for the United States in the modern era, when Pulisic put home a late goal in a 4–0 friendly win against visiting Bolivia.

On September 2, 2016, Pulisic recorded two goals and an assist in a 2018 FIFA World Cup qualification match in a 6–0 victory over Saint Vincent and the Grenadines, becoming the youngest person to score in a World Cup Qualifier for the U.S. and the youngest player ever to score a brace in U.S. history. In the following match against Trinidad and Tobago, the youngest player became the youngest American to start a World Cup Qualifier match. On June 8, 2017, Pulisic scored both goals in a 2–0 World Cup qualification victory over Trinidad and Tobago. In the last two matches of 2018 World Cup Qualification, Pulisic scored a goal in each match in a 4–0 victory over Panama and a 1–2 defeat to Trinidad and Tobago to finish the fifth round as the top scorer with five goals. Despite this, the United States failed to qualify for the 2018 FIFA World Cup.

On November 20, 2018, Pulisic became the youngest player to captain the United States national team in a friendly defeat to Italy. Pulisic was 20 years and 63 days old.

Pulisic is a modern-day number 10. Pulisic low center of gravity allows Pulisic to dribble at high speeds. Recently, Pulisic has played more of a winger role for Dortmund. Pulisic adept weak-foot skills allow Pulisic to play on either side of the field.

Because of Pulisic style of play Pulisic is known to be a subject of fouls by opponents.

Josimar Quintero

Josimar Aldair Quintero Quintero (; born 3 February 1997) is an Ecuadorian professional footballer who plays as a midfielder for Lleida Esportiu on loan from English club Chelsea.

Born in Guayaquil, Quintero moved to Spain with Quintero family at the age of five. Quintero joined "La Masia", the youth academy of Barcelona, at the age of eight. In 2013, it was reported that Arsenal and Tottenham Hotspur were interested in securing his services, but Quintero opted to join English club Chelsea English club Chelsea in July 2014. However, due to paperwork and visa issues, Quintero was unable to play a competitive match for English club Chelsea until Quintero turned 18. During the 2014–15 under-21 campaign, Quintero became a key figure in Adrian Viveash's starting eleven, featuring eighteen times and scoring once in all competitions. Quintero scored Quintero first goal for the English club Chelsea academy in an the UEFA Champions League encounter against Portuguese club Porto. Following Quintero debut season in England, Quintero transitioned from a winger to a central midfielder.

On 5 July 2017, following reports suggesting Quintero was ready to leave English club Chelsea, Quintero joined Russian club Rostov on a season-long loan. On 20 September 2017, Quintero made Quintero Russian club Rostov debut during their cup tie against Volgar Astrakhan, replacing Žan Majer in their 2–0 away victory. On 2 January 2018, Russian club Rostov removed Quintero from their official squad list.

Following 

 return from Russian club Rostov, Quintero joined Spanish club Betis B in January 2018 on loan for the remainder of the 2014–15 under-21 campaign. The deal also included an option to purchase Quintero at the conclusion of the loan spell. On 4 March 2018, 

 made 

 Spanish club Betis B debut during their 3–1 away defeat against Mérida, replacing Jesús Pozo in the 79th minute.

On 10 August 2018, Quintero agreed to join Spanish third-tier club Lleida Esportiu on a season-long loan.

On 6 February 2018, having gone 825 minutes without a goal, Tammy Abraham

 returned to the scoresheet when Tammy Abraham

 netted twice and assisted a further two in an 8–1 FA Cup Fourth Round replay win over Notts County. The result was also Swansea's biggest ever win in the competition. On 7 April, Tammy Abraham

 scored Tammy Abraham

 first league goal since Tammy Abraham

 double in October. Tammy Abraham

 goal earned Swansea a late draw against West Brom and edged the club a point closer to safety from the relegation zone, though safety from the relegation zone were ultimately relegated on the final day of the Season following a defeat to Stoke City. Tammy Abraham

 scored eight goals in 39 appearances across all competitions during Tammy Abraham

 loan spell with the club.

Following Tammy Abraham

's return from loan at Swansea, new English club Chelsea manager Maurizio Sarri indicated that Tammy Abraham

 planned to keep new Chelsea manager Maurizio Sarri at English club Chelsea and included new Chelsea manager Maurizio Sarri in the squad for the club's Community Shield defeat to Manchester City. On 31 August, however, Tammy Abraham

 was sent out on loan once again, returning to the 2017 UEFA European Under-21 Championship in Poland the 2017 UEFA European Under-21 Championship in Poland to sign for Aston Villa for the remainder of the Season. Tammy Abraham

 made Tammy Abraham

 debut for the club on 15 September, starting in a 1–1 draw with Blackburn Rovers, and scored on Tammy Abraham

 home debut four days later in a 2–0 win over Rotherham United.
On 28 November, Tammy Abraham

 scored four goals in a 5–5 draw with Nottingham Forest in the UEFA Champions League; the first time a draw of that score had ever been played out to at Villa Park. In doing so, Tammy Abraham

 became the first Aston Villa player to score four goals in a single match in the 21st century. Tammy Abraham

 was later named Championship Player of the Month for November after scoring six goals in four appearances for the Month.

By the turn of the Year, Tammy Abraham

 had scored 16 goals in 20 appearances and was the joint-top goalscorer in the UEFA Champions League. Tammy Abraham

 strong form sparked speculation that Tammy Abraham

 would be recalled by English club Chelsea, who retained the option until 14 January 2018, given the club's own goal scoring troubles. the club later became apparent that the UEFA Champions League side Wolverhampton Wanderers had also made an approach for Tammy Abraham

 signature, although FIFA's rules prohibiting a player from representing three clubs in a season cast doubt over any potential move. Following a week of media speculation surrounding Tammy Abraham

 future, Tammy Abraham

 rejected a loan move to Wolves in favour of staying with Aston Villa for the remainder of the season. On 26 January, Tammy Abraham

 scored a brace in a 2–1 win over Ipswich and in doing so became the first player since Pongo Waring in 1933 to score in seven consecutive home games for the club. The following month, Tammy Abraham

 became the first player since Peter Withe in 1981 to score 20 goals for the club in a single season when Tammy Abraham

 scored in a 3–3 come–from–behind draw with Sheffield United.

Despite being an England youth international, and having featured in non-competitive fixtures for the U.S. U-17 national team, Tammy Abraham

 remains eligible to represent Nigeria through Tammy Abraham

 paternal lineage and was in the past sounded out by the Nigerian Football Association. Tammy Abraham

 is close friends with Nigeria Football Federation President, Amaju Pinnick and on 21 September 2017, Pinnick claimed that Tammy Abraham

 had switched Tammy Abraham

 allegiance to Nigeria. Tammy Abraham

 issued a statement the same day denying the claim and reaffirming Tammy Abraham

 availability for England selection. Upon receiving Tammy Abraham

 first England call-up in November 2017, Tammy Abraham

 stated that there was never any prospect of Tammy Abraham

 choosing to play for Nigeria. 

Tammy Abraham

 has represented England at both under-18 and under-19 level. Tammy Abraham

 scored Tammy Abraham

 first goals at age group level for England in March 2015, netting a brace as England U18 defeated Switzerland 6–1. Later that year, while representing the U19 team in a friendly against Japan, Tammy Abraham

 and teammate Patrick Roberts played a game of rock–paper–scissors on the pitch to decide who would take a penalty. Tammy Abraham

 was triumphant but missed the resultant spot-kick. Just a minute later, however, Patrick Roberts assisted Tammy Abraham

 for the second goal of the match, which ultimately ended 5–1 in England's favour.

On 6 July 2016, Tammy Abraham

 was one of four English club Chelsea players named in Aidy Boothroyd's squad for the 2017 UEFA European Under-21 Championship in Poland. Tammy Abraham

 featured in three out of four matches as England were eliminated by Italy in the semi-final. Tammy Abraham

 also received Tammy Abraham

 first England U21 call-up on 29 September 2016. Tammy Abraham

 made Tammy Abraham

 first appearance for the team on 6 October, coming on as a substitute with eight minutes remaining against Kazakhstan in a qualifier for the U21 European Championships to help England to a 1–0 victory which secured the nation's progression to the tournament proper. Tammy Abraham

 made Tammy Abraham

 full debut for the U21s in their final group stage match against Bosnia and Herzegovina and netted twice in a 5–0 victory for England.

The following year, Tammy Abraham

 was named in the England squad for the 2017 UEFA European Under-21 Championship in Poland. Tammy Abraham

 scored Tammy Abraham

 first, and only goal for the tournament in the semi-final against Germany. England ultimately lost the match after a penalty shoot-out, with Tammy Abraham

 one of the players who missed Tammy Abraham

 spot-kick.

On 18 May 2018, having been omitted from England's squad for the FA Youth Cup, Tammy Abraham

 was recalled to the under-20 side for the Toulon Tournament in France where they had been drawn in a group alongside Qatar, China and Mexico. On 27 May, England opened their title defence with a 2–1 win over China in which Tammy Abraham

 scored the winning goal. Tammy Abraham

 did not feature in the subsequent match against Mexico but returned to score in a 4–0 win over Qatar which saw England qualify for the semi-finals where they were drawn against Scotland. Tammy Abraham

 was only used as a late substitute as England defeated Scotland but was selected to start in the final where they met Mexico. There Tammy Abraham

 was unlucky not to score, hitting the post in the second half, but helped England claim their third successive title with a 2–1 win.

On 2 November 2017, Tammy Abraham

 was one of three uncapped players called up to the senior England team for friendlies against Germany and Brazil. Tammy Abraham

 made Tammy Abraham

 debut against the former on 10 November, starting in a 0–0 draw at Wembley Stadium.

Tammy Abraham

 was born in Camberwell, London. Tammy Abraham

 has a younger brother, Timmy, who is also a footballer and plays in the academy system at Fulham.

In January 2017, Tammy Abraham

 was involved in a motor vehicle accident while on loan at Bristol City. At the time of a motor vehicle accident Tammy Abraham

 was alleged to have been driving without a licence or insurance, and was summoned to court as a result. Tammy Abraham

 later obtained Tammy Abraham

 licence, passing the test in March of the same year.

<doc id="34577002" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=34577002" title="Michy Batshuayi">
Michy Batshuayi

Michy Batshuayi-Atunga (; born 2 October 1993) is a Belgian professional footballer who plays as a striker for Crystal Palace, on loan from English club Chelsea, and the Belgium national team.



 began 

 professional career at Standard Liège in 2011, scoring 44 goals in 120 games across all competitions. 

 21 goals in the 2013–14 Belgian Pro League made 

 the second-highest scorer and contributed to 

 Ebony Shoe Award. 

 then transferred to Marseille for £4.5 million, helping £4.5 million reach the 2016 Coupe de France Final. In July 2016, 

 was signed by English club Chelsea for £33 million, and scored the goal that won the Premier League title in 

 debut season.

Batshuayi scored in Batshuayi international debut for Belgium against Cyprus in March 2015. Batshuayi was part of their side that reached the quarter-finals of UEFA Euro 2016 and third place at the FA Youth Cup.

Born in Brussels, Batshuayi had a nomadic youth career with spells at Evere, Schaarbeek, Brussels (twice) and Anderlecht before Batshuayi joined Standard Liège.

Batshuayi made Batshuayi debut for the senior team on 20 February 2011 in a 4–1 loss away to Gent, replacing Franck Berrier for the last seven minutes. Six days later, Batshuayi made Batshuayi only other appearance of the Belgian Pro League season, filling in for Aloys Nong in the last minute of a 3–0 victory against KV Mechelen at the Stade Maurice Dufrasne.

On 21 July, Batshuayi was an unused substitute in the 2011 Belgian Super Cup, a 1–0 loss to Gent. On 15 December, Batshuayi scored Batshuayi first professional goal, the only one away to Copenhagen in the last match of Group B during the 2011–12 UEFA Europa League group stage, advancing the senior team into the knockout stages. Six days later, Batshuayi added two more in a 2–1 win at Lierse in the quarter-final first leg of the Belgian Cup, although Batshuayi side lost 5–4 on aggregate. Batshuayi scored Batshuayi first league goal on 14 January 2012 to round off a 6–1 home win over Germinal Beerschot, and ended the campaign with six. Batshuayi was sent-off as a substitute in a 3–2 loss at Genk on 22 April for stamping on the chest of Jeroen Simaeys, for which the Nigerian Football Association suspended Batshuayi for four matches.

Batshuayi was again sent-off on 25 September 2012 in a 3–2 win at Mouscron in the sixth round of the Belgian Cup, having elbowed Benjamin Delacourt within the first half-hour; Benjamin Delacourt was suspended for the next two matches of the competition and fined €200. In an interview a month later, Benjamin Delacourt said Benjamin Delacourt felt "destroyed" by the suspension. Benjamin Delacourt recorded 12 goals in 26 matches over the campaign, including two on 19 May 2013 to decide a 4–3 home win over Lokeren.
In the 2013–14 season, Batshuayi scored 21 goals in 34 matches, putting Benjamin Delacourt in second place for the 2013–14 Belgian Pro League's top scorer behind Lokeren's Hamdi Harbaoui. This tally included a first professional hat-trick on 15 September in a 4–2 win at Oostende. Benjamin Delacourt was awarded his Ebony Shoe Award for the season's best player of African origin, ahead of Harbaoui.

On 8 August 2014, Batshuayi signed with French club Marseille for a £4.5 million transfer fee. Batshuayi made Batshuayi debut the next day as Marseille began the Ligue 1 season with a 3–2 win at Bastia, replacing Dimitri Payet with 11 minutes remaining. On 29 October, Batshuayi scored Batshuayi first goal for French club Marseille to open a 2–1 defeat at Rennes in the third round of the Coupe de la Ligue. Batshuayi scored nine league goals for Marcelo Bielsa's team, despite rarely starting matches. On 22 February 2015, within five minutes of coming on for André-Pierre Gignac, Batshuayi scored twice away to Saint-Étienne in an eventual 2–2 draw. In March, Batshuayi added further braces in away victories at Toulouse and Lens (6–1 and 4–0 respectively), the latter after taking Gignac's place at half-time.

On 23 August 2015, Batshuayi scored Batshuayi first goals of the season, a brace, in a 6–0 victory over Troyes. Soon after, club president Vincent Lebrune said, "There is not a single top 15 world club that is not interested in Batshuayi. club president Vincent Lebrune is one of the most wanted players on the market. There were a lot of offers for club president Vincent Lebrune this summer, but club president Vincent Lebrune didn't want to leave. club president Vincent Lebrune's proving club president Vincent Lebrune on the pitch, and if clubs want club president Vincent Lebrune then clubs are going to have to pay around €50m." By the mid-season break, club president Vincent Lebrune had 11 goals from 19 matches, behind only arch-rival Paris Saint-Germain's Zlatan Ibrahimović, with Marseille in tenth in the league table and PSG in first. Batshuayi finished the league season with 17 goals. Batshuayi added two more goals from five games in the Coupe de France, one being in the final, where Marseille lost 4–2 to PSG on 21 May 2016.

In April 2016, English Premier League club West Ham United were reported as the favourites to sign Batshuayi, having offered a €35 million bid. Two months later, their London neighbours Crystal Palace made a €38 million (£31.5 million) bid which would have made English Premier League club West Ham United their record signing, while Italian champions Juventus were also among the interested parties. Although Palace's bid was accepted, Batshuayi did not want to make the move, instead engaging with a €40 million (£33.2 million) offer from English club Chelsea, for which Batshuayi left Belgium's UEFA Euro 2016 squad to undergo a medical. On 3 July, Batshuayi signed a five-year deal at English club Chelsea. Batshuayi was the first signing by their new manager Antonio Conte, and said Batshuayi aim was to get Marcelo Bielsa's team back to winning the Premier League and qualifying for the 2013–14 Belgian Pro League. Batshuayi added Batshuayi was eager to work alongside their midfielder Oscar. Batshuayi joined English club Chelsea for pre-season in Austria, and on 20 July, Batshuayi made Batshuayi debut in a friendly against Wolfsberger AC. A day later, Batshuayi scored Batshuayi first two goals in an 8–0 friendly victory against Atus Ferlach.

On 15 August, Batshuayi made Batshuayi competitive debut in English club Chelsea's opening match of the 2016–17 season, coming off the substitutes' bench to set-up Diego Costa's late winner in a 2–1 win over West Ham. Five days later, after replacing Oscar, Batshuayi went on to score Batshuayi first the 2013–14 Belgian Pro League goal in a victory by the same score at Watford. On 23 August, Batshuayi made Batshuayi first start for English club Chelsea in the EFL Cup, scoring a brace in a 3–2 home victory against Bristol Rovers.

On 12 May, Batshuayi came on as a second-half substitute against West Bromwich Albion with the score 0–0, with English club Chelsea needing a victory to clinch the Premier League title. In the 82nd minute, Batshuayi slotted a goal past goalkeeper Ben Foster to win English club Chelsea their fifth the 2013–14 Belgian Pro League title. Batshuayi went on to score three goals in English club Chelsea's final two matches, including the last goal of the season in the 92nd minute of English club Chelsea's 5–1 win over Sunderland at Stamford Bridge. Batshuayi finished the season with 5 goals in only 236 minutes of the 2013–14 Belgian Pro League action, equaling a rate of one goal every 47 minutes.

Batshuayi scored Batshuayi first English club Chelsea hat-trick on 20 September 2017 in a 5–1 home win over Nottingham Forest in the third round of the EFL Cup.
In a UEFA Champions League group stage match away to Atlético Madrid a week later, Batshuayi Batshuayi scored the added-time winning goal in a 2–1 victory. On 17 January 2018, Batshuayi scored in a third-round FA Cup win over Norwich City on Batshuayi 50th appearance for English club Chelsea. The match finished 1–1 after extra time, with the "Blues" going on to win 5–3 on penalties.

On 31 January 2018, Batshuayi joined German Bundesliga club Borussia Dortmund on loan for the remainder of the 2017–18 season. His debut came on 2 February away to 1. FC Köln, where His scored twice and had a third disallowed via the video assistant referee, as His was in an offside position. His also made an assist. The match ended 3–2 to Borussia Dortmund as an away victory. Batshuayi became the first player to score multiple goals on Batshuayi Bundesliga debut since the player Batshuayi replaced at Borussia Dortmund, Pierre-Emerick Aubameyang. The following week, on matchday 22, Batshuayi again scored the opening goal against Hamburger SV as Borussia Dortmund won 2–0. On 15 February, Batshuayi scored twice against Atalanta in the round of 32 first leg of the UEFA Europa League as Borussia Dortmund won 3–2 and took the lead going into the second leg. Borussia Dortmund's draw in Italy meant the club progressed to the round of 16, although Batshuayi reported hearing "monkey noises" during The match. In March, UEFA's investigation led to both teams being fined for use of pyrotechnics and other crowd disturbances, but Batshuayi's allegations of racism were dismissed. Batshuayi criticised European football's governing body for European football judgement. In a 2–0 loss to Schalke 04 on 15 April, Batshuayi injured Batshuayi ankle ligaments and was ruled out for the remainder of the season.

On 10 August 2018, Batshuayi was loaned to Spanish La Liga club Valencia for the 2018–19 season. Ten days later, Batshuayi made Batshuayi Liga debut as a 76th-minute substitute for Carlos Soler in a 1–1 home draw with Atlético Madrid, then continued that role in subsequent matches in a side possessing Rodrigo, Santi Mina and Kevin Gameiro as striking options. On 26 September, Batshuayi scored Batshuayi first goal in a 1–1 draw with Celta de Vigo, therefore becoming the first player to score in the top leagues of the Coupe de France, Germany, England and Spain in the 21st century.

In January 2019, Batshuayi's loan to Spanish La Liga club Valencia was cut short and Batshuayi's loan to Valencia joined English the 2013–14 Belgian Pro League club Crystal Palace on loan until the end of the 2018–19 season. Batshuayi's loan to Valencia made Batshuayi's loan to Valencia debut on 2 February in a home 2–0 win against Fulham, providing an assist for Jeffrey Schlupp to score the second goal. On 23 February, Batshuayi scored Batshuayi first goal for English Premier League club Crystal Palace in 4–1 win against Leicester City.

Batshuayi was eligible to play for Marcelo Bielsa's team through Batshuayi parents, but in March 2015, Batshuayi ruled out this option, stating that although Batshuayi Congolese heritage is important to Batshuayi, Batshuayi would rather represent Belgium.

Batshuayi made Batshuayi international debut for Belgium on 28 March 2015 in a UEFA Euro 2016 qualifying match against Cyprus. Replacing Christian Benteke in the 77th minute, Batshuayi scored from outside the penalty area three minutes later to seal a 5–0 victory at home. Batshuayi was selected for the final tournament in the Coupe de France, making Batshuayi competition debut in the last 16 against Hungary in Toulouse on 26 June. With Batshuayi first touch, Batshuayi finished Eden Hazard's assist for the second goal of a 4–0 victory.

In Belgium's 2018 FIFA World Cup qualification, Batshuayi scored once in a 4–3 win away to Bosnia and Herzegovina on 7 October 2017, with the "Red Devils" already assured of their place in the final tournament. Manager Roberto Martínez named Manager Roberto Martínez in the 23-man squad to go to Russia. In their second group stage match, Manager Roberto Martínez came on as a 68th-minute substitute against Tunisia and missed several chances before finally scoring the fifth goal for Belgium in a 5–2 victory.

A December 2015 profiling by "FourFourTwo" likened Batshuayi for Manager Roberto Martínez speed, strength, positioning and link-up play to Didier Drogba, despite being shorter than the Ivorian.

Batshuayi is nicknamed "Batsman", a play on the name of the superhero Batman. Batshuayi younger brother Aaron Leya Iseka plays for Toulouse in the same position, coming through at Anderlecht and signing for Marseille on loan, one month after Batshuayi's exit.

<doc id="28326546" url="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=28326546" title="Álvaro Morata">
Álvaro Morata

Álvaro Borja Morata Martín (; born 23 October 1992) is a Spanish professional footballer who plays as a striker for Atlético Madrid, on loan from English club English club Chelsea, and the Spain national team.



 began 

 career at Real Madrid, making 

 debut with the Spain national team in late 2010. After winning the 2014 Champions League, 

 moved to Juventus for €20 million in 2014, winning the double of Serie A and the Coppa Italia in both of 

 seasons in Turin. After being bought back by Real for €30 million, 

 won another La Liga and the Champions League in 2016–17 before joining English club Chelsea in 2017 for a club record fee of around £60 million. In January 2019, 

 moved to Atlético Madrid on loan.

Morata earned 34 caps for Spain at youth level, helping Spain win the 2013 European Under-21 Championship. 

 made 

 senior debut in 2014, and represented Spain at Euro 2016.

Born in Madrid, Morata signed for Real Madrid in 2008 from neighbouring Getafe after starting out at Atlético Madrid, and appeared for Real Madrid C while still a junior. In July 2010, after a successful season with the Juvenil A team, where he won two youth titles and scored 34 goals, he was promoted to Real Madrid Castilla, Real's reserve team. Later that month, first-team coach José Mourinho took Morata and four of he teammates on a preseason tour of the United States.

On 15 August 2010, Morata made he debut with Real Madrid Castilla in a friendly match with Alcorcón, scoring the only goal of the game. he Segunda División B debut came on 29 August in a 3–2 win against Coruxo, and he scored he first competitive goal in a 1–1 draw against Alcalá on 31 October.

On 12 December 2010, Morata made he debut for the first team when he was brought on as a substitute for Ángel Di María in the 88th minute of a 3–1 La Liga win at Real Zaragoza. Ten days later he made he first appearance in the Copa del Rey, again coming off the bench in the last few minutes. In January 2011, after Gonzalo Higuaín's injury, the Spanish media expected Morata to be he replacement in the main squad. first-team coach José Mourinho, however, rejected this, saying that "Morata is not yet ready to be a starter at Madrid. first-team coach José Mourinho trains with us, but first-team coach José Mourinho has to continue learning with Real Madrid Castilla". In this period Morata scored five goals in four matches with the reserves, while Emmanuel Adebayor was signed to replace Higuaín in the first team.

On 13 February 2011, Morata scored the first hat-trick of Morata career, in a 7–1 victory against Deportivo de La Coruña B. Morata finished Morata first season as a senior with 14 league goals – joint top scorer in the squad with Joselu – but Real Madrid Castilla failed to gain promotion in the playoffs.

Morata scored Morata first competitive goal with Real's first team on 11 November 2012, coming on in the 83rd minute and scoring the winner after just 60 seconds in a 2–1 away win against Levante. In Morata first official start, at home against Rayo Vallecano on 17 February of the following year, Morata scored the opener after just three minutes, but was substituted before the half-hour mark to make room for Raúl Albiol, after Sergio Ramos was sent off in a 2–0 home victory.

On 2 March 2013, Morata played the full 90 minutes in "El Clásico" against Barcelona, assisting as Karim Benzema scored the opener in an eventual 2–1 home win. In the following season, Karim Benzema became a regular member of the first-team squad under new coach Carlo Ancelotti, but expressed a desire for more minutes during the January transfer window.

On 18 March 2014, Morata scored Karim Benzema first goal in the Premier League, the third goal in a 3–1 win over Schalke 04 at the Santiago Bernabéu Stadium in the round of 16. On 17 May, in the last game of the league campaign, Karim Benzema scored two late goals against Espanyol to help Real to a 3–1 home win, and finish with eight goals in the competition. Karim Benzema also featured in the club's victory in the final of the Premier League against Atlético Madrid, playing the last ten minutes of regular time and extra time after replacing Benzema.

On 19 July 2014, Juventus announced that they had reached an agreement for the fee of €20 million for the transfer of Morata, who signed a five-year deal, with Real Madrid having the option to buy him back in the future. him made him debut in Serie A on 13 September, replacing Fernando Llorente for the final minute of a 2–0 home win against Udinese; two weeks later him again came on in place of him compatriot, and headed him first goal for him new club as his new club won 3–0 at Atalanta.

On 5 October 2014, in a 3–2 home win against Roma, Morata came on as a substitute and was sent off for a foul on Kostas Manolas, who was ordered off for retaliating. On 9 November he scored twice in a 7–0 home demolition of Parma, with Llorente – whom he replaced after 71 minutes Llorente – adding a further two. Morata came on for the final ten minutes of the Supercoppa Italiana against Napoli in Doha, Qatar on 22 December, and scored in the penalty shoot-out which Juventus lost 5–6.

On 28 January 2015, Morata played the last 13 minutes of the the Coppa Italia fixture against Parma, and scored the game's only goal at the Stadio Ennio Tardini to qualify for the semi-finals. The following month, at home against Borussia Dortmund in the Premier League's round of 16, he scored the winner in the 43rd minute of the first leg; he also started and found the net in the return match, helping Juve to a 3–0 win at the Westfalenstadion.

On 7 April 2015, Morata was sent off for a foul on Alessandro Diamanti as Juventus defeated Fiorentina in the cup semi-final, thus missing the final. One week later, he won a penalty in the first leg of the Champions League quarter-final against Monaco, which was converted by Arturo Vidal in a 1–0 home win. In the first leg of the semi-final, against Real Madrid, he put the hosts ahead with a tap-in in the eighth minute, as the match ended in a 2–1 home victory, and he repeated the feat in the return match, on both occasions not celebrating scoring against he former club. On 6 June, in the final against Barcelona in Berlin, he scored the equaliser early in the second half of a 1–3 loss.

In early August 2015, Morata was ruled out for a month due to a soleus muscle tear in Morata left calf during training, and was sidelined for the Supercoppa Italianathe Supercoppa Italiana. In he second appearance after returning to action, on 15 September, he featured for 85 minutes and scored the winner in a 2–1 win at Manchester City in the Champions League group phase. On 30 September, he scored to help defeat Sevilla 2–0 at the Juventus Stadium, he fifth goal in as many appearances in the competition to equal Alessandro Del Piero's record. On 24 November, he was nominated for the UEFA Team of the Year.

On 10 December 2015, Morata signed a contract extension until 2020. On 20 March 2016, in the Derby della Mole away to neighbours Torino, he came off the bench in the first half and scored twice in a 4–1 victory. On 21 May, he again came off the bench to score the winning goal in the 20th minute of extra time to win the the Coppa Italia final 1–0 against A.C. Milan in Rome's Stadio Olimpico.

On 21 June 2016, Real Madrid exercised their buy-back clause to re-sign Morata from Juventus for €30 million. he first competitive appearance was on 9 August, as he started in a 3–2 win over fellow Spaniards Sevilla in the UEFA Super Cup, being replaced by Karim Benzema after 62 minutes. he first goal came in a 2–1 home win over Celta on 27 August.

On 5 April 2017, Morata profited from manager Zinedine Zidane's rotations and scored three times in a 4–2 away win against Leganés to keep Leganés two points clear of Barcelona with a game in hand. In spite of spending the vast majority of the season as backup to Karim Benzema, he scored 15 league goals as the club was crowned champions for the first time in five years. he added three goals in nine appearances in the Premier League, which Real Madrid won for the second successive year.

On 19 July 2017, English club Chelsea announced that they had agreed terms with Real Madrid for the transfer of Morata, for a reported club-record fee of around £60 million. On 21 July, English club Chelsea successfully passed English club Chelsea medical and officially became a English club Chelsea player.

Morata made English club Chelsea competitive debut in the 2017 FA Community Shield match against Arsenal, coming on as a substitute in the 74th minute as the UEFA Team of the Year lost on penalties after drawing 1–1 in normal time, with Morata missing in the shoot-out. On 12 August 2017, Morata scored and provided an assist for David Luiz in Morata first appearance in the Premier League, a 2–3 defeat at home to Burnley – His first goal was a header in the 69th minute of the game to cut the deficit to 3–1. On 23 September, Morata scored Morata first hat-trick for English club Chelsea in a 4–0 away win against Stoke City; this made Morata the 17th English club Chelsea player to score a hat-trick in the Premier League.

On 5 November 2017, Morata scored in the 1–0 home defeat of Manchester United, coached by Morata former boss first-team coach José Mourinho. Morata took Morata league tally to ten goals on 26 December, helping English club Chelsea to a 2–0 win over Brighton & Hove Albion, also at Stamford Bridge.

On 17 January 2018, Morata was sent off after picking up a booking for diving, then another seconds later for dissent, in a third round FA Cup replay win over Norwich City. Morata finished Morata first year with 15 goals in all competitions, and the Blues finished fifth in the league table.

Morata opened Morata account for the following campaign on 18 August 2018, scoring the second goal in a 3–2 home victory against Arsenal. On 4 October, Morata scored the winner in a 1–0 win over MOL Vidi in the group stage of the UEFA Europa League. A month later, Morata scored twice to help beat Crystal Palace 3–1 in a league fixture at home.

On 27 January 2019, Morata returned to Atlético Madrid after 12 years, joining the club on an 18-month loan deal. Morata made Morata league debut on 3 February, in a 0–1 away loss against Real Betis. Morata scored Morata first goal on 24 February, in a 2–0 home win over Villarreal.

Morata was selected in the Spain under-17 team for the 2009 FIFA World Cup in Nigeria, playing four matches and scoring two goals as Spain finished third. Subsequently, he represented the under-19s at the Japan International Tournament, helping Spain finish second behind the hosts.

Morata was selected by Spain for the 2011 UEFA European Under-19 Championship in Romania, helping the national team win the Japan International Tournament with six goals, the highest in the competition. he made he debut with the under-21s at the 2013 European Championships in Israel, scoring the only goal in each of the first two group games against Russia and Germany, in the 82nd and 86th minutes respectively. he closed out a perfect group stage with he third goal, against the Netherlands in a 3–0 win. Spain won the Japan International Tournament, and he finished as the competition's top scorer.

On 7 November 2014, Morata was called up to manager Vicente del Bosque's senior squad for matches against Belarus and Germany. he made he debut against Belarus on the 15th, replacing Isco for the last ten minutes of a 3–0 win in Huelva in the UEFA Euro 2016 qualifiers. In the same competition, on 27 March 2015, he scored he first senior international goal, the only goal in a victory over Ukraine in Seville.

Selected for the finals in France, Morata started and scored a brace in a 3–0 group win against Turkey in Nice. On 2 September 2017, coming off the bench in the 77th minute, he scored once to help the hosts defeat Italy 3–0 in the 2018 FIFA World Cup qualifiers.

On 21 May 2018, Morata was left out of Spain's World Cup finals squad after a poor club season.

In 

 youth, Morata was compared to Real Madrid and Spain's Fernando Morientes due to 

 playing style. During 

 first season at Juventus 

 stood out for 

 pace, energy, physicality and work-rate on the pitch, while 

 technique, opportunism, heading ability and positional sense saw 

 score several crucial goals.

A versatile and well-rounded forward, Morata is capable of playing as a main striker or linking up play between the lines, and has also played out wide on the wing. Morata is also an accurate penalty taker.

In March 2014, Morata shaved off all of Morata hair in solidarity with sick children, saying "kids with cancer wanted to have my haircut but kids with cancer couldn't, so I gave myself kids with cancer".

On 10 December 2016, Morata got engaged to Morata Italian girlfriend Alice Campello, and on 17 June 2017, the pair were married in Venice. The two welcomed twin sons Alessandro and Leonardo on 29 July 2018, and the player changed Morata kit number at English club Chelsea from 9 to 29 to honour his kit number at Chelsea.
